1.0 Site Considerations
Contractor is advised that all conditions pertaining to the Site, travel, access, conduct and behavior of
Contractor’s personnel will be closely monitored. Any actions contrary to the requirements appearing in
these documents will constitute reason for dismissal of personnel.
Company will require that Land Owner and occupants of lands along the total Project routing, be given
the utmost respect and understanding, with any and all requests arising from Contractor’s needs for
access across lands, along existing roadways, through fences and gates, etc. Contractor must give a rapid
response to any Land Owner’s reasonable request for the preservation of lifestyle as exists prior to
Contractor’s involvement in the Project.
1.1   Environmental Disturbance
Contractor shall plan and carry out the Work using the best practices and in such a manner as to limit
the disturbance or damage to the environment to levels acceptable to any duly constituted federal,
provincial or local agency, board or other authority having jurisdiction in respect of the Work or any
portion thereof (“Authorities Having Jurisdiction”).
Contractor shall confine construction traffic to within the established working limits and to approved
temporary access trails. Continuous efforts shall be made to prevent and control fires, soil erosion, and
air, noise and water pollution. In cases where some temporary disturbance or damage is unavoidably
caused due to the nature of the construction work, Contractor shall, as soon as practical, remove the
cause of such temporary disturbance, notify Company to agree on action for repair, repair the damage,
and generally restore the affected areas to their original condition to the fullest extent practical.
Contractor shall take all reasonable steps to minimize interference with existing agricultural operations
on the ROW.
Contractor shall minimize the impact on surrounding land by using approved dust control measures
when, in Company’s opinion, conditions so warrant.
Contractor is advised that a report summarizing rare plant species, Aboriginal traditional land use
concerns and site-specific important wildlife habitat along the ROW will be completed prior to the
commencement of Work. These areas will be flagged and/or fenced by Contractor or others prior to
commencement of the Work. Contractor shall ensure all Contractor Parties are aware of these areas and
Contractor has identified such areas will be out of bounds to Contractor Parties and Construction
Equipment.
If air access is required to the ROW, Contractor shall comply with all regulations or restrictions regarding
helicopter access particularly in ecologically sensitive areas, and Contractor shall avoid making low level
helicopter flights to minimize disturbance to the public, livestock, and wildlife.
Contractor Parties shall not make any recreational use of all-terrain vehicles (“ATV”) on any part of
the ROW or Sites.
Contractor shall be responsible to abide by all Applicable laws to concerning environmental protection
and obtain all necessary Required Approvals unless specifically stated otherwise, elsewhere in the
Contract Documents.
1.2   Workers Orientation



                                              Page 10 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                             OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Contractor shall ensure all employees, servants and agents of all Subcontractors are:
          Informed of the environmental concerns and special conditions of the Worksite; and
          Instructed on the requirements of environmental laws, rules and regulations applicable to the
           construction area.
1.3       Historical Resources and Ecological Sites
Contractor is advised that in addition to the specifications, the terms of the Company’s Environmental
Protection Plan (“EPP” or “EMP”) general and Project specific will be in effect with the Project specific
EPP taking precedence. All flexibilities are the prerogative of the Company. There may be special sites of
archaeological, paleontological, historical or ecological importance existing adjacent to or extending into
the available working area. These sites shall be fenced off from the working area by Contractor, as
directed by Company prior to commencing other construction activities on the ROW. Contractor shall
ensure that its Contractor Parties and Construction Equipment stay out of these sites, and Contractor
Parties who breach this requirement may be subject to dismissal. Contractor Parties should be advised
that they may be charged as an individual under the regulator with no protection from their employer.
In the event that any archaeological, paleontological, historical or ecological sites are discovered during
construction, Contractor shall take immediate measures to protect the site. No artifacts shall be
removed from the site. The location of the site shall be immediately brought to the attention of
Company who will advise the Land Owner and the appropriate Authorities Having Jurisdiction. Until the
site has been assessed by a qualified archaeologist, Contractor shall cease work within thirty (30) metres
of the site.
Any fossils, coins, articles of value or antiquity and structures and remains or other things of geological,
paleontological or archaeological interest discovered in the performance of the Work shall be deemed
to be property of the Provincial Government. Contractor shall take precautions to prevent Contractor
Parties or any other persons from removing or damaging any such articles or things and shall
immediately upon discovery thereof, and before removal, inform Company of such discovery and carry
out Company's orders as to protection or removal of such discoveries.
1.4       Wildlife and Livestock
Contractor shall make every effort to ensure that wildlife encountered along ROW and other work areas
are not unduly harassed or killed by equipment or personnel. No wildlife shall be fed. Wildlife injuries
due to any activities shall be reported to Company.
Contractor shall make every effort to ensure that livestock are not unduly harassed by equipment or
personnel. No livestock shall be fed. Where livestock are likely to be present, all gates shall be closed
unless a watchperson is maintaining the gate.
Hunting and fishing by Contractor Parties and Other Parties is not allowed on the ROW, Site and all
access used by the Project. Contractor Parties shall not have firearms or pets on the Worksite or ROW at
any time.
Beaver dams, or other areas containing water which supports beaver or muskrat populations, shall not
be opened to drain the impounded water, without the prior approval of Company and Authorities
Having Jurisdiction.
The vandalism or theft of trapper equipment or trapped animals shall not be tolerated.

1.5   Debris Disposal
Contractor shall ensure that general rubbish such as food wrapping, garbage and sanitary wastes are
confined to the Site and are collected on a daily basis by each work crew. Construction rubbish shall not
be disposed of in the pipeline trench. It is the responsibility of Contractor to dispose of said wastes in a
manner and at a site approved by Authorities Having Jurisdiction, to the satisfaction of Company.
Contractor shall ensure that the Site is left in a tidy and workmanlike condition following the cessation
of daily activities.
No disposal of materials will be permitted off the Site, other than at established disposal locations,
unless prior approval is obtained from the appropriate Land Owner and Authorities Having Jurisdiction.
Any open burning of waste materials must have prior approval from the Land Owner and Authorities
Having Jurisdiction.
1.6   Weed, Pollution and Dust Control
Contractor shall ensure that all equipment brought to the Site is pressure washed and all equipment and
vehicles arrive in a clean condition in order to minimize the risk of weed introduction. Company shall
inspect equipment and any pieces not clean to the satisfaction of Company shall be re-washed at an
offsite location acceptable to Company, the Authorities Having Jurisdiction and the Land Owner if on
Private land.
Where requested by the Land Owner or the Authorities Having Jurisdiction, Company may request
Contractor to clean equipment between individual Land Owner's parcels to minimize weed introduction
from one area to another. When Company requests tracked equipment be “air cleaned” Contractor shall
be compensated in accordance with the applicable Unit Price Item in Schedule C – Commercial Terms.
Contractor shall not permit liquid wastes, fuels or other potential pollutants to be deposited on the
ground or into bodies of water. Fuel trucks and service vehicles shall carry at least ten (10) kg of
absorbent material, thirty (30) square metres of six-mil polyethylene, a shovel and an adequate supply
of heavy gauge plastic garbage bags. In the event of spills involving fuel or hazardous material
Contractor shall immediately notify Company. Refueling and lubrication changes for all mobile
equipment shall be carried out at a minimum distance of one hundred (100) metres from any body of
water to prevent any spilled material from entering the body of water. Non-mobile equipment within
this zone shall have a lined berm appropriate for containing any spills, and spill clean-up materials (same
minimum quantities as for fuel trucks) shall be kept within fifty (50) metres of such equipment.
In the event of spills involving fuel or hazardous material, Contractor shall immediately contain the spill,
trenching and diking or deploying booms and straw bales as necessary. Contained fluids shall be
recovered by vacuum truck, absorbent material soaking, or burning, as appropriate. Contractor shall
clean up every spill by removing any contaminated soil to an approved disposal site, all to Company's
satisfaction. For any such spill with a spill volume of twenty (20) litres or more, or any spill of refined
petroleum products or chemicals into a water source, Contractor shall immediately notify Company and
others in accordance with the requirements of the provincial regulations (Alberta Environment and
Sustainable Resource Development (“AESRD”) or the Spill Reporting Regulation under the British
Columbia Environmental Management Act (2008)). Where contaminated soil has been removed, it shall



                                              Page 13 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                             OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


be replaced with clean fill material of similar characteristics and the area shall be revegetated - all at no
additional compensation to Contractor.
Should a spill of more than one hundred (100) litres occur, after removing contained fluids and
absorbent materials, Contractor shall be required to use in-situ bio-remediation techniques on the
contaminated soil. Should bio-remediation not reduce contaminants to levels acceptable to Company
and Authorities Having Jurisdiction, Contractor shall be responsible for removing and replacing material
at the spill site.
Contractor shall ensure the following measures are employed to minimize the risk of fuel spills:
          All containers, hoses, and nozzles are free of leaks;
          All fuel nozzles are equipped with functional automatic shut-offs;
          Operators are stationed at both ends of the hose during fuelling unless the ends are visible and
           are readily accessible by one operator; and
          Fuel remaining in the hose is returned to the storage facility.

All stationary fuel tanks with a capacity greater than one thousand (1000) litres shall be double walled or
positioned in an impervious bermed area capable of retaining one hundred and twenty-five percent
(125%) of the capacity of the largest tank within that berm. All such tanks shall be visually monitored for
leaks and shall be gauged when filling to prevent over filling.
Equipment service wastes shall be disposed of in an industrial waste facility in accordance with any
requirements of Applicable Laws and Authorities Having Jurisdiction. Where there is a potential for a
spill, equipment shall be serviced over a tarpaulin. Double walled tanks are exempt from this
requirement when identified and preapproved by Company. Contractor shall exercise care to minimize
noise from its activities, including blasting, in accordance with local regulations.
Contractor shall exercise care to minimize uncontrolled emissions of dust (particulate matter) from its
activities on the Site and on graveled roads. These measures shall include watering down the ROW and
suspending topsoil stripping and replacement during strong winds as directed by Company or required
by Attachment A-1.5 - Line List or the Authorities Having Jurisdiction. All such control measures taken
shall be in accordance with any Applicable Laws.
Particular care shall be taken in residential areas. Contractor shall implement dust suppression
measures, as required, to minimize dust adjacent to residences.
1.7       Access and Traffic Control
Access to the ROW shall generally be via existing roads and established trails. Contractor shall note that
a Temporary Field Authorization (TFA) from the Alberta Energy Regulator (‘AER’) and Ministry of Forest,
Lands, Natural Resource Operations (“MFLNRO”) is required for ALL vehicle and equipment use off of
the approved Worksite within Crown Lands in Alberta and British Columbia respectively. Road use
agreements are required for all existing access roads and or trails from those Land Owner’s having a
current agreement (“L.O.C.”). Company intends to acquire all road use agreements for road and or trails
identified on the access map. Contractor shall make arrangements for any other access roads and
provide Company with a copy of the road use agreement prior to using the road. It will be Contractor’s
responsibility to ensure that all agreements and Required Approvals for the temporary use of the access
roads are in place prior to their use.



                                                Page 14 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                             OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT

ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Development of access to the ROW shall be limited as follows:
Any building of new access or upgrading of existing access shall be done only following approval of each
by Company through the Contractor’s Access, Clear, Grade and Reclamation Plan (“ACGR Plan”), as
further detailed in this Attachment B-2.4 – Construction Specifications. Any new road shall avoid
important plant and wildlife locations, as identified by Company.
          In most cases, no new roads shall be developed, though existing trails that show evidence of
           earlier grading may be upgraded, and other trails may be used in their existing condition by light
           traffic.
          On freehold land, regardless of any agreement with the Land Owner, the access development
           must meet the Project specific EPP requirements for soil, water, wildlife, rare plants and
           historical resources.
Access for vehicles and equipment across roads shall be by ramps through bar ditches and the road
travel surface shall be protected from damage.
Access for vehicles and equipment across watercourses shall be in accordance with this Attachment B-
2.4 – Construction Specifications and the Watercourse Crossing Table included in Attachment A-1.6 –
Watercourse List.
Travel on the ROW shall be at speeds less than thirty (30) km per hour and when passing workers slow
to five (5) km per hour unless otherwise addressed in the Contractor’s Project Safety Plan and agreed to
between Company and Contractor for special circumstances. Contractor shall use the stripped portions
of the ROW for vehicle and equipment travel, whenever and to the extent practical. For example, pipe
stringing and skid truck traffic in these areas.
When traveling on sod and topsoil, unnecessary wheel spin shall be strictly avoided.
1.8       Special Requirements by Land Owners and Tenants
Prior to the commencement of any Work and before entering any part of the ROW, Contractor shall
review with Company to confirm that all Land Owners and other rights holders (grazing, trap line, guide,
water) have been notified by Company of the impending construction and construction access has been
granted.
Contractor shall observe any special requirements of Attachment A-1.5 - Line List and on the Appendix
B-1 - Drawings. Where structures, shrubbery or valuable trees are encountered during construction and
the use of trenching equipment may result in unnecessary damage to property, shrubs or trees,
Contractor may be required to employ specialized construction techniques as approved by Company. No
additional compensation will be paid to Contractor to accommodate these situations for those special
requirements identified on the Line List at the time of Bid.
1.9       Environmental Damage
Where in the opinion of Company certain or all Work activities, due to wet ROW conditions are causing
or may cause damage to the ROW in the form of topsoil and subsoil mixing, structure loss or
compaction, Company will request the Contractor to suspend Work in specific areas.
Where wet Site conditions prevail Contractor shall take immediate mitigative action to minimize
environmental damage, including but not limited to the following:



                                                Page 15 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                           OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


       To the extent practical restrict the movement of traffic on the Site;
       Restrict or reroute some of the traffic at wet areas;
       Suspend traffic at specific locations until Site conditions have adequately dried in the opinion of
        Company to allow work to proceed; and,
       Using swamp mats at certain locations
Due to the localized nature of traffic and weather events, Contractor is required in advance of any
shutdown order by Company, to self-prevent damages to soils, and must instruct all resources in this
regard.
On cultivated land, land under hay production and bush land, travel on the ROW shall be modified or
suspended where rutting depths reach within 2 in or 5 cm of the bottom of the topsoil (A horizon).
On parklands, grass lands and improved pasture, travel on the ROW shall be modified or suspended
where rutting penetrates through the sod layer.
In bush land, travel and work on the ROW shall be modified or suspended where rutting of the ground
surface will cause irreparable damage in the opinion of the Company.
Contractor shall make reasonable efforts to minimize weather or construction related damages to the
affected portion of the ROW and surrounding area by pumping water, scarifying, progressively blading
off the thawed or wet topsoil or upper surface material, or other means of enhancing ROW drying and
other measures deemed necessary by Company that will not, in the opinion of Company, result in
additional negative impact or irreparable damage to said lands.
1.9.1   Environmental Response Team
Contractor shall designate a foreman and a crew as an Environmental Response Team (“ERT”) prior to
commencing work. The ERT will be responsible for responding to emergencies and implementing
necessary remedial action for any environmental emergency situations. Contractor shall provide the ERT
with training and instructions in how to respond and execute potential emergency work. Situations
where an ERT would be required are:
       Potential sedimentation of watercourses or water bodies as a result of rainfall, snowmelt, etc.
       Potential sedimentation of private property as a result of rainfall, snowmelt, etc.
       Embankment or slope failures.
       Fuel, oil and/or chemical spills.
       Fires
       HDD surface mud returns (SMR)
The duties of the ERT shall include, but not be limited to, the construction of dykes, ditches and berms,
the installation and maintenance of silt traps and fences, and pumping of excess water.
Contractor shall ensure that the ERT and required equipment are capable of quickly responding to any
environmental risks or emergencies resulting from the Work.
Prior to commencing Work on the ROW, Contractor shall submit to Company a list of personnel
designated to the ERT, their location and the location of the required equipment and material. This list
shall be re-submitted at any time that the information changes.
A typical ERT will consist of the following makeup:

       One (1) backhoe (Cat 320 or equivalent), one (1) small dozer (D6 or equivalent), and one (1)

1.10 Public Roads
Contractor shall adhere to the load limits, tire and axle configurations, and load and dimension
restrictions required by the Authorities Having Jurisdiction over roads, bridges and railways that
Contractor uses or crosses during the performance of the Work.
The travelled surfaces of roads, highways and railways shall be cleaned free of mud, dirt or any debris,
immediately after such material has been deposited by equipment traversing these said roads or exiting
from the Site.
1.11 Conduct and Safety
In addition to the requirements of the Contract Documents, alcohol, illegal drugs and any prescription
or non-prescription drugs/medication that could impair judgment shall not be permitted on Site or on
any of Company Property. Failure to comply shall be reason for Company to require the immediate
removal from Site by Contractor of the Contractor Party.
Contractor shall exercise due care in closing gates and fences, repairing fences, guarding open ditches,
and taking other measures as necessary to safeguard people, livestock, crops, and wildlife from death,
loss, or injury.
As a minimum, Contractor shall hold daily tailgate meetings with each work crew to discuss and review
environmental and safety issues, in accordance with the frequency requirements in Schedule A – Scope
of Work, and Schedule D – HSE.
All activities by Contractor Parties in confined space locations shall strictly conform to requirements of
Schedule D – HSE and Contractor’s Project Safety Plan including receipt of a Safe Work Permit from
Company prior to starting such activities. Contractor is advised that the Pipeline route passes through

WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


popular fall hunting areas. Construction warning signs must be clearly displayed at all public access
points to the ROW.
1.12 Mitigation of Induced Voltage Effects
As sections of the pipeline will be installed parallel, adjacent to, and crossing under power lines,
Contractor shall ensure that it has a qualified electrical supervisor on site to be responsible for and
direct all work in close proximity to electrical transmission lines. Contractor shall provide the resume of
the qualified electrical supervisor to Company for approval prior to any work commencing in the field.
Where the pipeline is laid on or within close proximity to an existing AC power transmission
line ROW, Contractor shall measure the induced voltage in the pipe prior to and frequently during the
period when workmen might contact any section of pipe.
Should the measured voltage between the pipe and ground exceed twelve (12) volts RMS, Contractor
shall render the pipe safe for human contact by grounding and/or attaching equipotential grids. Such
voltage measurements and ground and/or grid attachment shall be in accordance with a Grounding Plan
to be provided to Company prior to commencement of any work in close proximity of overhead power
lines. As a minimum, this plan shall specify instruments to be used, calibration, and address procedures
for measuring, ongoing monitoring and documentation of findings, proposed grounding methods for
pipe and equipment.
1.13 Fire Prevention and Emergencies
Construction vehicles on the ROW shall carry a fire extinguisher of a type and size required by Schedule
D – Health and Safety and Contractor’s Project Safety Plan. Light construction vehicles shall also carry a
shovel. Contractor shall ensure that it has sufficient equipment and personnel at the Site at all times to
permit the suppression of any accidental fire originating from its construction activities. In the event of a
fire on the Site, Contractor shall immediately proceed to extinguish the fire and inform Company of the
fire.
Contractor shall comply with the applicable provincial fire regulations including the Forest and Prairie
Protection regulations, the FireSmart Guidebook for the Oil and Gas Industry and the BC Wildfire
Regulation and Attachment A-2.5 - Forest Fire Regulations.
To reduce the risk of fires due to smoking on the site, Contractor shall cause the following precautionary
measures to be implemented:
       Provide butt cans on equipment;
       Maximize ashtray use in vehicles;
       In the absence of above, butts shall be stubbed out on mineral soil and the dead butts dispensed
        of in appropriate containers; and
       Careless disposal of smoking materials shall not be tolerated.
       Contractor shall submit to Company for approval a detailed written emergency response plan
        one week prior to commencement of work on the Site, all in accordance with the more detailed
        requirements on emergency preparedness in accordance with Appendix D – HSE Documents.
        Contractor shall give notification to Company before commencement of the Work.
Contractor is advised that on Project and during high fire hazard that smoking outside of vehicles may be
prohibited.

2.0 Right of Way (ROW)
The ROW is provided by Company for the Work as attached to Attachment B-1.4 – IFB Alignment Sheets
and Attachment B-1.7 – Construction Typicals. The use of Temporary Work Space (“TWS”) is subject to
Company approval in accordance with the justification procedures of this Attachment B-2.4 –
Construction Specifications. Contractor shall note that a Temporary Field Authorization (“TFA”) from the
AER is required for any Additional Temporary Work Space within the Green Zone of Alberta or a Crown
Land Tenure from MFLNRO in British Columbia.
Additional Temporary Work Space, Contractor's yard, staging or lay down areas, storage space and
access trails requested by Contractor, in addition to that already acquired by Company, are all subject to
examination by environmental and historical resource specialists. Contractor is advised that such
examinations of these spaces is expected to take at least one week, however the approval process from
the Authorities Having Jurisdiction is beyond the control of Company. Contractor is further advised that
approval of these spaces is dependent on the resource specialists finding no significant resources, and
therefore approval is not assured. Company will endeavor to expedite the examination process.
In selecting any new space or shoo-flies, Contractor shall consider the following parameters: relatively
level ground, minimizing shoo-fly length, good load bearing soils, good drainage, minimal tree clearing,
and minimal visual impact. Disturbance to the environment shall be minimized. All areas utilized by the
Project activities are subject to the requirements of soil integrity protection.
The Site limits, as specified and/or staked by Company, are not to be exceeded. Contractor shall be
liable for all costs for ROW damages.
Contractor shall comply with requirements itemized in Attachment A-1.5 - Line List, which include a
landholder line list of cautions and restrictions and a crossing line list.
Contractor shall not remove or take down fences or open gates without first obtaining the consent of
the property owners and any tenants. All gates shall be operated as requested by the Land Owners or as
directed by Company. Contractor shall co-ordinate, in advance, all such activities with Company.
Contractor shall take all reasonable steps to minimize interference with existing and future agricultural
operations on the ROW.
All agreements between Contractor and a Land Owner shall be in writing and shall not change the
requirements for use and restoration of ROW and adjacent areas to the satisfaction of Company.
Contractor shall protect all road and railroad surfaces from damage by tracked or cleated equipment.
Should a surface be damaged, it shall be restored to original condition at no additional compensation to
Contractor and, if requested by Company, Contractor shall obtain a damage release from the owner of
the facility.
3.0 Existing Structures
3.1   Above Ground Structures
This section refers to the location, protection, removal, and replacement of existing above ground
structures. Structures shall be interpreted as being all utility poles, canals, sidewalks, buildings, bridges,
private roads, fences, and other man-made things that may be encountered during construction.

Contractor shall supply all materials required for the location, protection, removal, and replacement of
existing structures. Unless specified otherwise, materials supplied shall be equal to or better in quality
than those being replaced. Fencing materials must be new.
It is the responsibility of Contractor to determine the presence of and locate all existing structures
within the ROW and on adjoining properties that may be encountered during construction. Company
will make available Appendix B-1 - Drawings, Attachment A-1.5 - Line List, and crossing agreements
containing all information in its possession concerning existing structures but will not guarantee the
accuracy or completeness of such information.
Should Contractor, through its negligence damage or break existing structures, will be liable for all costs.
In any event of damage or loss, Contractor shall suspend construction operation immediately and notify
the structure company and Company immediately. Contractor shall repair immediately any such damage
when, in the opinion of Company, such damage cannot await repair by the clean-up operation. Cost of
fines, penalties and/or downtime resulting from suspension of the Work due to damage to existing
structures shall be borne by Contractor.
Where cutting or replacing of existing structures is deemed necessary, Contractor shall so advise
Company in advance of this activity and shall not proceed without written approval of the owner of the
existing structure as well as Company’s approval.
During the pre-work period described in Schedule A - Scope of Work, Contractor shall work with
Company to review each portion of the Work awarded in order to identify any power poles or other
structures that will interfere with its construction operations. Company will make best efforts to have
poles or other structures moved to facilitate the Work, but makes no guarantees that all above ground
structures will be able to be moved. Contractor may be required to revise construction procedures to
accommodate some surface structures.
Contractor shall be solely responsible for determining the existence and location of, and shall take all
precautions to avoid damage to overhead telephone lines, power lines, poles and guy wires or any other
above ground structures crossing or adjacent to the pipeline being constructed.
Contractor shall be solely liable for all costs for repairs to any damage caused to such above- ground
facilities or structures. Contractor shall pay particular attention to existing valve and pump station sites
to determine the exact location of all power and communication cables and conduit. It shall be the
responsibility of Contractor to notify the owners of all such above ground structures, seventy-two (72)
hours (or in accordance with the crossing agreements) in advance of any such intended crossing.
3.2     Buried Facilities

3.2.1    General

Contractor shall be solely responsible for determining the existence and location of, and shall take all
precautions to avoid damage to other pipelines, water mains, sewers, underground telephone cables,
telegraph and power conduits, or other underground structures crossing or adjacent to the Pipeline.
Contractor shall be solely liable for all costs for repairs to any damage caused to such underground
facilities or structures. Contractor shall pay particular attention to existing valve and pump station sites
to determine the exact location of all power and communication cables and conduit. It shall be the

responsibility of Contractor to notify the owners of all such underground structures, seventy-two (72)
hours (or in accordance with the Crossing Agreement) in advance of any such intended crossing.
Company shall ensure that an approved crossing agreement is in place for those buried facilities known
to Company prior to construction. Contractor shall abide by all terms and conditions contained therein.
Contractor shall make arrangements with the facility owner’s field representative for locating all buried
facilities and preventing damage to them. Contractor shall be required to sufficiently confirm locations
and elevation of all buried facilities to be crossed before field engineering operations to allow Company
to determine in advance, any necessary changes in elevation or location of the Pipeline to be installed.
Buried facilities of which Company is aware are shown in Attachment B-1.4 – Alignment Sheets.
Contractor is advised that the new pipeline installation will be parallel and adjacent to existing pipelines,
in addition to crossing various buried facilities owned by others; e.g. gas or oil pipelines, water or sewer
lines and electrical or communications cables, etc.
Contractor is responsible for ensuring all existing buried facilities are located, staked, fully exposed,
adequately protected and fenced as required, in accordance with this Specification, provincial
regulations (Alberta Pipeline Act, BC Oil and Gas Activities Act), and Authorities Having Jurisdiction.
Prior to any work on the ROW or a facility site, Contractor shall comply with the requirements of this
Specification to identify, locate, expose if necessary and protect all buried and/or aboveground facilities.
Prior to any work on the ROW, Company and Contractor shall jointly organize and conduct a meeting to
discuss and implement a plan for managing buried facilities on the Project.
The intent of this meeting is to ensure that all parties involved understand their roles and
responsibilities and to ensure a coordinated approach in identifying/confirming all existing buried
facilities.
The “management of buried facilities” includes, but is not limited to, the following tasks, i.e. carrying out
contact/notifications, identifying, electronic locating and staking, electronic searching or sweeping for,
exposing (hand or hydrovac) and confirming existing buried facilities.
All personnel directly involved in the management of buried facilities shall attend the meeting to review
procedures and responsibilities. As a minimum, the following personnel must attend this meeting:
For Contractor:
       Superintendent
       Safety Coordinator(s)
       Ground Disturbance Supervisor
       Hydrovac Foreman
       Field Engineer
For Company:
       Field Engineer
       Chief Inspector and/or Assistant(s)
       Safety Inspector(s)
       Hydrovac Inspector(s)

For the Construction Survey company:
       Survey Coordinator
       Survey Crew(s) that will be conducting electronic locating and staking of buried facilities
For the Third-Party Buried Facility Locating companies:
       All crews that will be doing electronic searching/sweeping for buried facilities
Contractor shall assign a qualified individual as to coordinate all work associated with the management
of buried facilities (“Ground Disturbance Supervisor”).
Company will also assign an individual to work closely with the Ground Disturbance Supervisor.
The essential elements of the buried facility management program, as a minimum, must include the
following:
       Contractor shall maintain a record/log as facility owners are contacted. This record must identify
        the facility owner, person(s) contacted, date and time of contact and, any relevant comments or
        information.
       Throughout the duration of the Project, ensure that all available reference data or documents
        including but not limited to EGIS, AbaData, Legal / Easement Plans, Wellsite Plans, Pipeline
        Drawings, Construction Alignments Drawings, Crossing Agreements, Line List (“Reference
        Documents”) are reviewed / compared, to look for obvious discrepancies and/or any additional
        information that may help to determine all existing buried facilities.
       Contractor must prepare a Buried Facility List, and make note of any discrepancies (“Buried
        Facility List”). This list will be a “living document” and must be updated regularly as actual
        existing buried facilities are confirmed. As the process continues, this Buried Facility List will
        ultimately include all existing facilities that have been confirmed. Any time the Buried Facility
        List is updated it must be provided to those performing ground disturbance work on the Project,
        so that they have up-to-date information to work with.
If there are any discrepancies in the Reference Documents or, if there are any discrepancies between
the Reference Documents and actual field locates/staking, it is essential that further investigation and
follow-up is immediately initiated which would include but not limit to meeting with facility owner
representatives to:
       Review facility owner plan drawings (if any are available).
       Ask questions about known existing or recently installed facilities that may not yet appear in
        Reference Documents.
       If the facility owner has not already done so, request facility owner representatives to personally
        locate their existing buried facilities.
Re-sweep areas in question and, if necessary:
       Re-sweep areas that couldn’t be swept previously due to physical barriers on the ROW,(e.g., soil
        berms, manure piles, stacks of hay or straw, parked vehicles, machinery or equipment,
        buildings, etc.) prior to ground disturbance;
       Speak with Land Owners to see if they might offer any helpful information.

When exposing buried facilities by hydrovac (“Hydrovacing Exposure Results”) or by hand) if
discrepancies are found between Hydrovacing Exposure Results, Reference Documents and/or
electronic locates and staking, further investigation is required as soon as the discrepancy is identified.
Ground Disturbance work will cease until all parties are confident that the discrepancies have been
resolved.
NOTE: Facilities must be exposed (hand or hydrovac) in three (3) locations, as a minimum, i.e. work side
boundary, centerline of ditch and spoil side boundary and, at any suspected fittings and/or sharp
changes in direction.
In addition to any efforts to resolve identified discrepancies, the basic elements in the process of
identifying, locating and confirming existing buried facilities will typically include the following:
       Company survey crew(s) will electronically locate and stake approximate location and depth of
        all buried facilities as identified on the Construction Alignment Sheets.
       Contractor will conduct an independent electronic four (4) way sweep of the entire
        construction ROW, including Extra Work Space Areas, to confirm previous locating work by
        survey crew(s) and, in an attempt to determine if there are any other buried facilities that were
        not identified on the Construction Alignments and not located by the survey crew(s).
       Company will conduct an independent electronic four (4) way sweep of the entire
        construction ROW, including Extra Work Space Areas, to confirm previous locating work by
        survey crew(s) and, in an attempt to determine if there are any other buried facilities that were
        not identified on the Construction Alignments and not located by the survey crew(s).
       Contractor shall hydrovac or hand expose buried facilities that have been located and staked by
        the survey crew(s) and/or the third-party line locating companies.
Contractor shall notify and coordinate with the respective Land Owners, the locating and exposing of all
buried facilities. Notification must be done as per the Crossing Agreement provincial (AER/OGC)
requirements (AER/OGC). The names and addresses of the representatives of all known facility owners
will be provided in Attachment A-1.5 - Line List. Specific requirements pertaining to facility crossings are
detailed in the Contract Documents.
Contractor shall ensure that all buried facilities are located and fully exposed by experienced persons, a
minimum of five hundred (500) metres in advance of any work, i.e. excavation of hydrovac slurry
disposal pits, installing crossing ramps/bridges, vehicles or equipment crossing, and any stripping,
grading or excavation work.
Contractor shall ensure that, as a minimum, the following individuals involved in ground disturbance
activities have attended ground disturbance training and be in possession of a valid Ground Disturbance
certificate:
       Contractor’s Ground Disturbance Supervisor, and
       All other supervisors/Foremen directing ground disturbance activities within thirty (30) metres
        of buried facilities, and
       All other supervisors/Foremen, persons directing the equipment operator (i.e., spotters) and
        operators involved in Ground Disturbance activities within five (5) metres of buried facilities.

Only backhoe operators “designated” by Contractor and found by Company to be acceptable for this
type of work will be allowed to excavate within five (5) metres of buried facilities. Contractor must
provide Company with a list of the designated operators and update the list as required. Operator
acceptability shall be based on the following:
       In possession of current Ground Disturbance certification;
       Demonstrated experience in excavating buried facilities, in particular operating pipelines;
       Attendance of a Pre-Phase Safety Meeting presented by Contractor and the Company or
        Company Representative, specific to excavating in the vicinity of operating facilities, which
        would highlight associated hazards and procedures to be followed; and


NOTE: if, in the opinion of Company, a designated operator does not demonstrate the ability to excavate
buried facilities safely, that operator will no longer be allowed to do so and will be removed from
Contractor’s list of designated operators.
Contractor’s Ground Disturbance Supervisor shall ensure the following guidelines are adhered to, as a
minimum, in conjunction with all requirements of the Contract Documents and the Applicable laws such
as BC Oil and Gas Activities or AER Pipeline Act, prior to any Ground Disturbance activity in the vicinity of
existing buried facilities.
No Ground Disturbance activity shall occur within thirty (30) metres of any buried facilities unless:
       The required notification has been made to the facility owner(s);
       All facilities within thirty (30) metres of the proposed ground disturbance activity have been
        accurately located and staked, prior to commencement of the work, unless otherwise approved
        by the Company and facility owner in accordance with the Provincial Regulations (AER or OGC).
No Ground Disturbance activity shall occur within five (5) metres of any buried facilities unless:
       The required notification has been made to the facility owner(s);
       The buried facility had been located, staked and fully exposed in accordance with the Contract
        Documents and/or Provincial Regulations (AER or OGC);
       A Ground Disturbance check list has been completed for each buried facility
        excavated/daylighted; and
Note: Providing the owner of the buried parallel adjacent pipeline agrees, one ground disturbance check
list per/day, will be sufficient when exposing a parallel adjacent pipeline.
       A Safe Work Permit is in place (if required) in accordance with the Contract Documents;
       A Crossing Agreement is on site, it has been reviewed and all work is in accordance with the
        requirements therein;
       The owner of the buried facility is on site, unless otherwise approved by Company and facility
        owner, in accordance with the Provincial Regulations (AER or OGC).
For additional requirements regarding excavation and boring or drilling in the vicinity of buried facilities,
refer to Section 15.0 of this Attachment B-2.4 – Construction Specifications.
3.2.2   Locating (Electronically) and Staking Buried Facilities




                                               Page 24 of 148

Prior to the start of any work, Contractor shall notify BC One Call or Alberta One Call and all facility
owners and ensure that all buried facilities that cross or encroach on the ROW including any workspace
beyond the Temporary Works Space parameters (“Extra Work Space Areas”) are located and staked.
Contractor shall make contact (in writing or by fax where possible) and maintain a contact record/log.
The contact log shall as a minimum record name of owner, person(s) contacted, date and time of call
and brief summary of discussion. This contact log shall be made available to Company when requested.
Contractor is cautioned that not all buried facility owners are registered with BC One Call or Alberta One
Call.
Contractor shall directly hire a company that specializes in the electronic location of buried facilities to
carry out an electronic sweep of the “entire” ROW and Extra Work Space Areas prior to any ground
disturbance activities. As a minimum this shall include a four (4) way sweep.
As part of the construction ROW staking program, Company survey crews will “electronically” identify
(stake) the approximate location and depth of adjacent parallel pipeline(s) as well as all other buried
facilities known to Company, which cross and/or encroach on the ROW, including Extra Work Space
Areas. However, Contractor is responsible for ensuring that all buried facilities are located, staked,
exposed as required, adequately protected and fenced as required. Contractor is to maintain the
integrity of all survey stakes and workers shall not attempt to re-establish survey stakes that have been
knocked down or destroyed; Contractor must notify Company immediately and any re-staking shall be
done by Company survey crews.
Adjacent parallel pipeline(s) will be staked at approximately fifty (50) metre intervals, and more
frequently where necessary, to ensure construction crews can readily identify the location and/or any
deviation of the parallel pipeline(s).
Buried facilities that cross the Construction ROW shall be staked in a minimum of three (3) locations,
i.e. work-side boundary, centerline of proposed new trench and spoil-side boundary and, at any
suspected fittings and/or sharp changes in direction. Buried facilities that cross Extra Work Space Areas
shall be staked as directed by the facility owner and/or Company.
Buried facilities that encroach within (i.e. but do not cross) the Construction ROW and/or Extra Work
Space Areas shall be staked to ensure they are accurately located. Staking intervals for all buried
facilities that cross or encroach on the ROW or Extra Work Space Areas must not exceed ten (10) metres
and, staking of buried facilities should extend a minimum of one (1) stake beyond both construction
limit boundaries where possible (Land Owner permission is required for any staking that occurs beyond
the construction limit boundaries).
3.2.3   Exposing Buried Facilities
Prior to exposing buried facilities Contractor and Company shall carry out a hazard assessment and
complete a Ground Disturbance check list. A sample of the Ground Disturbance check list is included in
Schedule D - HSE.
Buried facilities may be exposed by hand digging or hydrovac method. Tools such as pick and bars, that
could damage the facility, shall not be used. The method and locating procedure proposed by Contractor
shall be submitted to Company seven (7) days prior to commencement of the work.
Prior to any hydrovac work commencing, Contractor shall provide Company with a detailed
hydrovac plan for Company approval. This plan shall include information on the type of hydrovac unit to


                                               Page 25 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                              OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


be used (e.g., ground pressures, technical data on nozzle types, pressures and gpm) and the slurry
disposal procedure. Contractor shall notify Company prior to commencement of this work.
Slurry resulting from hydrovac operations shall be disposed of on subsoil only and to the extent practical
within the same land tract, to the satisfaction of Company.
All buried facilities that cross the Construction ROW shall be fully exposed in a minimum of three (3)
locations, i.e. work-side boundary, centerline of proposed new trench, and spoil-side boundary, and at
any suspected fittings and/or sharp changes in direction. Buried facilities that cross Extra Work Space
Areas shall be exposed as directed by the facility owner and/or Company, to ensure the facility is
accurately located, confirmed and adequately protected.
All buried facilities that encroach within (i.e. but do not cross) the Construction ROW and/or Extra Work
Space Areas shall be fully exposed as directed by the facility owner and/or Company, to ensure the
buried facility is accurately located and adequately protected.
As a minimum, the top and sides of all buried facilities and all known protruding appurtenances (e.g.
plugs, weldolets or any branch piping coming off the buried facility) must be hand or hydrovac exposed
to positively confirm identity and location, prior to any mechanical excavation occurring within five (5)
metres of the buried facility. Exposing of all buried facilities must be carried out to the satisfaction of the
facility owner and Company.
Contractor will be required to fully expose any parallel adjacent pipeline(s), to confirm location, depth
and pipe size. The interval and exact location of exposures shall be determined by the facility owner
and/or Company on a Project specific basis. When required to expose the adjacent pipeline(s), these
general guidelines are to be followed:
    A. Where the separation between the new pipeline and the adjacent pipeline is ten (10) metres or
       greater, exposure holes will be no further apart than line of sight or one (1) kilometre and in
       accordance with (d) below;
    B. Where the separation between the new pipeline and the adjacent pipeline is less than ten (10)
       metres, exposure holes will generally be no further apart than line of sight or one hundred (100)
       metres maximum and in accordance with (d) below;
    C. Under no circumstances will ground disturbance work be allowed within the parallel
       adjacent ROW without the written approval of Company and the owner of the ROW. A Safe
       Work Permit or Ground Disturbance Check List issued by the owner of the facility will constitute
       written approval.
    D. The adjacent pipeline shall be located and exposed as follows:
                at the center of all side bends up to five (5) degrees,
                at a point one hundred (100) metres on either side of and at the center of all side-
                 bends in excess of five (5) degrees, to ensure the deflection of the bend is located,
                at equipment crossing locations, on each side of wet areas,
                on each side of road, highway, railroad or other crossings, and
                at any other locations required by Company, where depth and location may be in doubt.
3.2.4   Identification of Buried Facilities
After being fully exposed, all underground facilities shall be identified by placing markers (i.e. 1x4 or 2x4)
in the exposure holes. These markers are to be clearly visible to construction traffic, with information


                                               Page 26 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                             OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


and colours as specified in Appendix B-1 - Drawings. Where markers are placed in exposure holes to
identify the location of an adjacent parallel pipeline, they must be placed “alongside and on the work
side” of the adjacent pipeline and “facing” the ROW. Where practical, and as determined by Company
and/or facility owner, these exposure holes may then be backfilled with the markers in place. Markers
will be removed during final cleanup.
Contractor shall ensure a copy of the Crossing Agreement for each facility remains at the crossing
location in a weather proof container to ensure all workers have access to the Crossing Agreement on
site during construction.
All exposure holes, open excavations and sight holes associated with the location of buried facilities,
including those on parallel adjacent pipelines, shall be fenced and/or covered with suitable materials
that will guard against persons, livestock or wildlife falling into the open excavation, e.g. where livestock
is present, barbwire fencing will be required and snow fence may be used where livestock is not present.
Contractor shall receive no compensation for this fencing.
3.2.5   Work Adjacent to or Over Buried Facilities
Prior to any ground disturbance work within five (5) metres of buried facilities, and any pipelines,
electrical, fiber-optics or telephone cables, water or sewer lines, drainage tile, etc., Contractor shall
ensure a Ground Disturbance check list has been completed. All work shall be done in accordance with
the requirements of the Company or facility owner and the conditions of the Permit.
A safety buffer will be established by Company survey crews and maintained by Contractor alongside of
adjacent parallel pipeline(s) and equipment/vehicles shall not encroach on this safety buffer, except
where specifically allowed elsewhere in this Specification or approved in writing by Company, in
accordance with the approved ROW configuration. Persons violating this rule may be permanently
removed from the Project.
Buried facilities shall be ramped to the Company's satisfaction as further detailed in this Attachment B-
2.4 Construction Specifications, prior to crossing the facility with equipment or heavy vehicles or
commencing any work in the vicinity of the facility. After the installation of ramps, all construction traffic
(including pickups) must use the ramps for crossing over the facilities.
Except where specifically allowed in this Specification or approved in writing by Company, the use of
tracked equipment over pipelines, for the purpose of stripping or grading, is strictly prohibited. Any
person found operating any equipment over the existing pipeline(s), without authorization, may be
subject to immediate dismissal from the Work.
If Contractor is required to work over an existing buried facility, approval must be obtained from
Company and/or facility owner; a Safe Work Permit may also be required, as determined by Company or
facility owner. A work pad may be required to ensure a minimum of two (2) metres cover exists
between the top of the facility and surface of the work pad. As a minimum, the work pad shall consist of
competent subsoil material as approved by Company and owner of the facility.
No equipment is to be allowed over buried facilities in wet areas.
3.2.6   Excavating In Close Proximity to Parallel Adjacent Facilities




                                               Page 27 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                            OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Where excavation occurs in close proximity to adjacent buried facilities, extreme care must be taken to
ensure that “sloughing” of soils does not undermine the facility, thereby placing the integrity of the
facility at risk.
Contractor shall immediately suspend trenching operations and notify Company if signs of soil instability
occur during these excavations. Trenching will not resume until adequate measures (e.g. sheet piling)
are taken to protect the facility against movement associated with the excavation, to the satisfaction of
Company and/or the owner of the facility affected.
Storage of surplus spoil over top of operating adjacent pipelines or within the established safety buffer
will not be allowed unless approved in writing by the owner of the adjacent pipeline.
3.2.7   Crossing Ramp Requirements
All buried facilities shall be crossed in accordance with the terms of the Crossing Agreement(s) (or as
directed by the facility owner) and any letters of agreement, or as specified herein.
Equipment/vehicle crossings of all Oil and Gas pipelines NPS 8 and greater shall be carried out using “rig
mats” as a foundation for the crossing ramps in accordance with the Drawings and Specifications.
Other equipment/vehicle crossings of buried facilities (e.g. pipelines NPS 8 and less and electrical
or fiber-optic cables) shall be through the use of soil ramps. Ramps must be built and installed in
accordance with this section and the Drawings and to satisfaction of the buried facility owner and in
accordance with the Crossing Agreement.
Crossing-ramps over pipelines less in size than NPS 8 and cables shall be constructed of suitable dry
material (subsoil), with a maximum particle size of one hundred fifty (150) millimetres in accordance
with the Drawings and Specifications and the Crossing Agreement. Adequate topsoil shall be stripped on
both sides of the buried facility to allow subsoil to be skimmed from the ROW to adequately ramp the
facility, without leaving a deep depression that will collect water. In private lands, geotextile must be
placed between the subsoil ramp and any unstripped topsoil.
Crossing of adjacent parallel pipelines with equipment or vehicles (except as otherwise approved in this
Specification) will be allowed only where crossing locations have been identified in the ACGR Plan, and
approved by the owner of the facility.
Contractor shall maintain soil crossing-ramps such that rutting of the ramps does not reduce the
required minimum depth of cover. Wet ROW conditions may preclude the use of these ramps
by rubber-tired vehicles/equipment. If wet conditions prevail, and rutting prevents Contractor from
maintaining minimum cover requirements, the affected ramps shall not be used. Contractor may, at
Contractor’s option, replace the ramp with a bridge satisfactory to Company.
During winter construction, snow may be used for ramping buried facilities where soil ramps are
allowed in this Specification and approved by Company. “Watering and freezing-in” snow ramps may be
required to ensure adequate bearing strength for heavy vehicles and/or equipment.
Contractor’s costs for all work associated with the location, staking, exposing, ramping, crossing and
pipe installation under all buried facilities identified in the Contract Documents shall be included in the
Base Lay Price.
4.0 Construction Surveying

4.1   Surveys by Company
Company’s survey crew will stake the limits of the construction ROW, including any additional
Temporary Work Space as shown on the Drawings, the approximate location of all known buried
facilities which cross or encroach on the construction ROW, the approximate location of adjacent
pipelines, safety buffers and provide survey station markers at approximately one hundred (100) metre
intervals.
During construction, Company survey crews will stake the centerline of the proposed pipeline, certain
engineering features such as change in pipe wall thicknesses, valve locations, buoyancy control devices
test leads, etc. All stakes will be colour coded in accordance with the Project Survey Colour Code as
shown in Appendix B-1 - Drawings.
Company will cooperate reasonably with Contractor in arranging for staking operations at such times to
minimize loss or destruction of stakes. The Company’s Survey crew will stake the centerline of ditch
prior to topsoil stripping operations for trench, and trench and spoil side stripping and then restake the
centerline to facilitate the trenching operation.
Through grade planning the contractor is to identify where work space is to be positioned, and Company
will approve the use of the space. Company’s survey team will mark the approved workspace.
Contractor must provide forty-eight (48) hours’ notice to Company and the survey team for any work to
be completed out of normal sequence. If work space is placed in the wrong place due to
misinterpretation of the directions from the Contractor the costs will be the responsibility of the
Contractor.
Contractor shall not replace stakes, which have been removed or offset for any reason. However,
restaking costs made necessary due to negligence of Contractor's operations shall be borne by
Contractor.
Company survey crews will perform an as-built survey for Company’s permanent record and will
make as-built measurements for the purposes of determining and adjusting payment to Contractor
under the terms of the Contract Documents.
4.2   Surveys by Contractor
Contractor shall make itself aware of legal survey markers in the field before proceeding with the Work.
Contractor shall not disturb, deface, alter, destroy or remove any legal survey markers. If this should
occur due to negligence on the part of Contractor, Company will have the markers replaced by a
registered land surveyor at Contractor's cost.
It is the responsibility of Contractor to determine the exact location and depth of all existing buried
facilities crossing and/or paralleling the ROW in accordance with the Authorities Having Jurisdiction. All
underground facilities shall be staked in accordance with this Attachment b-2.4 – Construction
Specifications.
Contractor shall confirm the location, depth of cover and fully expose all buried facilities to be crossed,
unless allowed otherwise in this Specification, five hundred (500) metres in advance of any equipment
crossing, and to facilitate the installation of equipment crossing ramps.
During or following backfill activities the Contractor must confirm the ditch center to ensure the location
of the roach is or will be positioned properly over the excavation and pipeline.

Contractor shall maintain stakes placed by Company survey crews defining safety buffers along existing
parallel adjacent pipelines throughout the duration of the Work unless otherwise allowed by Company.
No movement of equipment or vehicles shall be allowed inside the safety buffer except where

The location of known underground facilities staked in the field by Company survey crews or shown on

Contractor shall perform all necessary field surveys for the proper installation of bored and cased
crossings, for the grading of the trench and bending of the pipe to properly fit the trench contours, for
field locating all existing underground facilities and for such other installations, not specified to be

Contractor shall pay particular attention to the elevation and location of fabricated assemblies to ensure
that they are installed level, at the proper height and free from excessive stresses. Contractor shall
ensure the pipeline through valve assemblies is installed at the correct elevation based on the
dimensions shown on the Typical Valve Assembly Drawing.
5.0 Clearing, Grubbing, Grading, Topsoil and Upper Surface Material Management
5.1   General
Contractor must supply a representative to be present during clearing to identify locations of Extra Work
Space Areas, in consultation with Company. Company will supply survey support to flag requested areas
prior to clearing. Contractor is responsible for the verification of all Extra Work Space Areas.
Where the Contractor requests Extra Work Space Areas after the advance clearing operation is
complete, the cost to clear, salvage merchantable, and dispose of non-merchantable will be the
responsibility of the Contractor. Merchantable timber must be limbed, processed and decked along with
the regular clearing operation. Additional timber cleared following clearing may require removal with
other salvaged wood at Contractor’s cost. Use of these materials for rollback may not be permitted. Use
of the material for rollback will be at the discretion of Company Representative.
Contractor is advised that due to the sensitive ecological systems being traversed, an Access, Clear,
Grade and Restoration Plan ("ACGR Plan") will be used as a required procedure and working tool to
minimize disturbance and environmental impacts and ensure that the integrity of existing above and
below ground facilities are not jeopardized during the execution of the Work.
Contractor is advised that the grade planning process benefits both Company and the Contractor. The
grade plan allows anticipation by the Contractor for situations that will require planning, different
procedures, more equipment, more space, manpower and materials. The Company is afforded the lead
time to approve the plans, obtain the space, get environmental assessments performed, change
procedures and seek regulatory clearances.
The ACGR Plan is not to be used as a mechanism for the Contractor to claim extra costs. All work
included in the grade plan is to be included in the Base Lay Price unless specifically agreed to by
Company in writing. There will be no process during in field grade planning for Company representatives
to approve extra cost work.


                                              Page 30 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                         OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


The ACGR Plan is to be created by the Contractor in consultation with Company. Company will have
qualified personnel available to participate in the ACGR Plan planning process. The Contractor must also
have qualified representatives committed to create the grade plan. The ACGR Plan is a significant
undertaking that requires a full time commitment potentially over a period of several weeks. It is an on
the ground, in the field, process, followed by computer generation of the schematics and descriptions.
This ACGR Plan will be developed in co-ordination with Company, Contractor's grade foreman,
environmental representative and superintendent or assistant. No work shall be started until Company
provides written approval of same. As a minimum this ACGR Plan shall be developed in accordance with
the requirements identified below. This ACGR plan shall be submitted to Company for approval fifteen
(15) days before grading begins.
In developing the ACGR Plan, Contractor shall make all efforts to:
       Familiarize itself with Project requirements.
       Minimize the use of Company's Available Temporary Working Space to the extent practical.
       Minimize grading to the extent practical.
       Ensure the integrity of topsoil or upper surface material is not jeopardized.
       Contain its work within the staked boundaries of the approved working areas.
       Use only existing access to the ROW to the greatest extent practical and implement traffic
        control in general.
The ACGR Plan must be submitted in an electronic format acceptable to Company. The format is not set,
and can take the form of Excel programs, GPS programs, mapping programs, etc., provided the scale
clearly indicates the plans, procedures, and the space on a metre by metre basis. Non-computerized
formats may be allowed on smaller Projects. The Contractor must present the format for their ACGR
Plan to Company shortly after the award of the Work.
Contractor shall provide their proposed ACGR Plan to Company for approval one (1) month in advance
of commencing any work on the ROW. The ACGR Plan will be similar in some respects to the alignment
sheets but not a reiteration without verification. The graded plan will be more specific as to location.
The ACGR Plan as a minimum shall fully address the following:
           Identify locations where crossing of existing pipeline(s) is required and the method of
            crossing with equipment;
           Identify all off ROW access from existing improved roads;
           Identify areas of restricted clearing and work space;
           Restricted work space on the ROW;
           Landholder cautions and restrictions (line list requirements);
           Identify requirements for salvaging merchantable timber within private lands;
           Identify method of disposing of clearing debris;
           Identify requirement, location and volume of timber for rip rap;
           Agreement between Company and Contractor on final location of pipeline within ROW;
           Method of developing winter access to and along the ROW;
           Topsoil / upper surface material stripping procedures, including plans and justification for
            stripping in excess of the width indicated on Appendix B-1 Drawings;

           The need and justification for the use of Company acquired and Contractor acquired
            Available Temporary Working Spaces;
           The need and justification for the use of additional Temporary Work Space required by
            Contractor;
           Clearing and grade constraints at watercourse crossings;

Contractor shall clear (if required) grade the ROW in accordance with Appendix B-1 Drawings, ACGR Plan
and to the satisfaction of Company.
Contractor shall prepare specific sediment control plans for all crossings of named rivers and named
creeks and any erosion prone areas, which may be susceptible to flooding during heavy rain falls. The
sediment control plan shall, as a minimum, include the following:
           Preventative measures to be used during Construction to minimize the risk of environmental
            damage.
           Control measures to be employed in the event of heavy rainfall causing flood conditions.

5.1.1   Fences and Temporary Gates
Prior to commencing construction activities on the ROW, Contractor shall open fences crossing
the ROW and install temporary gates therein in accordance with the drawings. Adjacent posts shall be
adequately braced to prevent slackening of the wire.
Before such fences are opened, Contractor shall notify the Land Owner or tenant, and where practical,
the opening of the fences shall be in accordance with the wishes of said Land Owner. Contractor shall
ensure that no loss or inconvenience shall accrue to the Land Owner by opening fences, installing gates
or failing to properly close gates. Contractor shall be liable for any damage claims or actions arising from
such temporary openings in fences.
Where page wire, wooden or other special types of fences are encountered, Contractor shall construct
the temporary gates of the same materials as the original fence unless otherwise approved by Company.
When requested by Company, Contractor shall furnish a watchperson(s) at certain gates in order to
ensure that no stock or cattle get in or out of the field. Contractor shall be diligent in maintaining the
gates and fences along and crossing the ROW and at access roads.
Contractor shall also fence off Historical and Ecological sites in accordance with this Attachment B-2.4 –
Construction Specifications and as required by Company.
Temporary fencing required during construction where livestock is present shall be constructed of
barbwire while snow fencing may be used where livestock is not present, unless otherwise approved by
Company.
The cost for all fences, gates, and special conditions as noted in Attachment B-2.4 – Construction
Specifications shall be at no additional compensation to Contractor.
5.1.2   Clearing
Contractor shall clear, unless otherwise specifically stated, only the width sufficient for its requirements
and as justified in the ACGR Plan. Contractor shall perform the Work in such a manner as to limit the
damage incurred to the absolute minimum. Where Contractor fails to observe restrictions and
limitations and causes damage to property beyond the ROW limits secured by Company, such damage
shall be Contractor's liability.
Where a Land Owner has a special request to save particular trees or shrubs as indicated in the Line
Lists, the trees or shrubs shall be flagged by Contractor prior to clearing. Snow fencing or other suitable
fencing shall then be erected around the trees or shrubs to protect them from damage during
construction at Contractor's cost. Contractor shall use special installation techniques and/or boring to
install the pipeline underneath specimen trees, shrubs shelter belts and/or windrows as specified on
Attachment A-1.5 - Line List.
In order to prevent damage to existing property, pipelines, adjacent trees and brush, bordering trees
and damaged or leaning trees shall be felled onto the cleared ROW.
Contractor shall expect to hand clear all slopes leading to watercourses and within the buffer strip at all
watercourses. At named watercourses, Contractor shall leave a buffer strip of understory vegetation,
extending ten (10) to twenty (20) metres back from the top of the immediate stream banks, until
immediately prior to commencement of actual crossing construction. This buffer may be reduced by
Company Representative to three (3) to five (5) metres if the approach slopes to watercourse are steep.


                                              Page 33 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                           OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Trees shall be felled away from drainages and watercourses to reduce damage to aquatic habitat. Trees,
debris or soil inadvertently deposited within the high water mark of any drainage or watercourse shall
be immediately removed without an approved crossing plan. Trees shall not be skidded across a
drainage or watercourse. A feller buncher may take the place of hand falling with specific permission
from Company. The permission will be based on the ability to accomplish low disturbance by straight
line motion with no track twist in the buffer area.
At all watercourse crossings clearing activities shall be conducted so as to minimize disturbance to root
systems.
Contractor shall salvage and process merchantable timber in accordance with the harvesting standards
in Attachment A-2.1 -Timber Salvage Plan and deck along the edge of the ROW at no additional
compensation to Contractor. Remaining tree stumps shall not project more than three hundred (300)
millimetres above ground level.
All non merchantable timber or slash (including tree tops, branches, bush, stumps and such other
debris) shall be disposed of in accordance with the Contract Documents, except only where Company
requests material be retained at designated areas for erosion control or for reclamation work by others.
All burning operations shall be conducted on mineral soil with a minimum of one blade width stripped
around the pile or in burning sloops, or as directed by the Authorities Having Jurisdiction.
Any intention by Contractor to employ mulching methodologies must be specifically approved by
Company. Mulching, grinding and chipping of cleared debris may be considered by Company as an
alternate disposal method to burning. Contractor shall provide Company with a written procedure for
approval, fifteen (15) days prior to the disposal work commencement. Company’s written approval will
include type of equipment to be used and method of disposing of chips or grindings. Land Owners and
Authorities Having Jurisdiction must be in concurrence with the procedure. Contractor will give
notification to Company prior to the commencement of disposal work.
Fires shall not be left unattended. Under winter conditions this may be relaxed by Company for fires 6
hours from the time of ignition. Contractor shall maintain responsible personnel and adequate
firefighting equipment on site to control burning and prevent fire spreading to adjacent timber, brush,
grass or crops. This shall include maintaining a water truck on site during all burning operations.
Contractor shall secure required burning permits from the Authorities Having Jurisdiction and shall not
commence burning operations until approval is granted by Company. A copy of all such permits shall be
provided to Company.
Contractor shall make all efforts to dispose of cleared debris during clearing operations and shall
minimize residual debris that is left for disposal during cleanup.
Contractor shall secure the Land Owner’s written consent, obtain Company's approval and request that
Company obtain a permit from the Authorities Having Jurisdiction (if required) to dispose of all stumps
and other debris which cannot be burned.
Contractor shall identify the requirement for timber as rip-rap or other construction purposes prior to
salvage operations to allow wood to be decked for use at a later date. Refer to Attachment A-2.1 -
Timber Salvage Plan and Schedule A - Scope of Work for any restrictions associated with the use of
merchantable timber for rip-rap. The plan for the use of merchantable timber for corduroy must be
accompanied by the plan to build frost into the ROW.
