PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                           OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Timber, slash, brush or geotextile used as rip-rap in swamps or wet areas shall be removed from
the swamp or ROW by pulling it up and spreading it over the full width of the ROW, or by moving it to
the upland areas for spreading or burning. This requirement may be waived by Company in consultation
with the Land Owner, tenant, governmental agency and Company. In the event that approval to leave
rip rap in place is granted, Contractor shall ensure that drainage patterns are not impeded and a
minimum of forty (40) centimetres of soil covers the rip rap material. Materials shall be disposed of in
accordance with the clean-up requirements of this Attachment B-2.4 – Construction Specifications.
5.1.3   Grubbing
Grubbing means the removal and proper disposition of all stumps, roots, and partially embedded rocks
or boulders. Grubbing shall be conducted with the use of brush rakes, or Company approved alternate,
and restricted to the ditch line and working areas where required to allow safe utilization of equipment
and vehicles. On land with the potential for cultivation, Contractor shall grub all stumps. On all other
land Contractor shall minimize grubbing activities and shall not grub within two (2) metres of standing
timber or in deep muskeg areas. Contractor shall back fill and compact the depressions from the
grubbing operation to prevent water from collecting and forming a bog hole. All grubbed material shall
be disposed of in accordance with this Attachment B-2.4 – Construction Specifications.
In coulees and watercourse valleys, all temporary workspace areas, grubbing shall be minimized to the
extent practical.
Contractor's cost of; grubbing shall be included in the Base Lay Price, unless otherwise stated in the
Contract.
5.1.4   Duff and Upper Surface Material (USM) Conservation (Bush Land)
Prior to grading or leveling of the ROW, in forested land, Contractor shall salvage upper surface material
such as duff, leaf matter, upper mineral soil layer, and miscellaneous grubbing material. As a minimum,
in level areas the Contractor shall salvage the upper surface material (USM) from the trench area up to a
full ROW USM removal is required in grade areas, and where the schedule seeks to avoid wet condition
shutdowns. The depth of the USM salvage will vary at Company’s discretion up to fifteen (15)
centimetres. The salvaged material shall be stored in accordance with the drawings and, as a minimum,
salvaged in a fashion that will minimize the risk of losing any of the material.
Contractor is advised that USM removal is generally limited to fifteen (15) centimetres or less. The
Contractor must inform all operators performing USM removal of this limitation, to prevent space
problems from occurring later in the construction process. Company will not obtain more space for
over-stripping USM, and will not be responsible for construction delay costs associated with the reduced
space. Areas that require more than fifteen (15) centimetres of USM removal for special reasons will be
listed on the alignment sheets or notified in the field by Company Representative during the ACGR Plan
planning process.
Placement of USM stockpiles is at the Contractors’ discretion, provided that in any placement trade off,
the decision should not require more space. Windrowing of the USM is generally expected to reduce
the need for Extra Work Space Areas.
If the USM is stored on one side of the ROW, or not split equally, the contractor is advised that the USM
must be lifted over the roach to facilitate an even spread during clean up. Discrete USM stockpiles must
be labeled under winter conditions with survey lath.


                                              Page 35 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                           OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Salvage of the USM layer will not be required in muskeg areas where the organic layer exceeds 60 cm.
Wet areas may also be exempt by Company Representative. Test holes must be dug to prove the depth
of the organic layer.
All costs associated with salvage of the upper surface material and replacement of this material during
cleanup shall be included in the Base Lay Price.
5.1.5   Topsoil Conservation
Prior to any grading or movement of vehicles of equipment that could damage topsoil on the Site,
topsoil shall be stripped and conserved to depths and/or colour changes as indicated on Contract
Documents and as directed by Company.
Contractor is advised that the topsoil and subsoil handling procedures, the space acquired to execute
the procedures, and the accuracy of the removal, placement, and replacement are all interrelated
concepts. Company must balance regulatory, Land Owner, and ENGO perspectives to successfully
complete the work.
Contractor is expected to be familiar or become familiar with the soil handling procedures for normal
circumstances, side bends, foreign lines, road crossings, rail crossings, and water crossings.
Contractor is advised that short distances, up to one thousand (1000) metres in any given location, may
require specialized construction procedures for a variety of reasons. This may include reverse lay,
reversed construction direction, drag sections, single pipe joint transfer, operate on ditch spoil, operate
on stripped topsoil, remove soils to other locations, and others. These locations and procedures must be
included in the Base Lay Price unless agreed otherwise with Company during bid clarification.
The procedure, width, and depth of topsoil stripping will all be listed on the construction alignment
sheets. The Contractor is not allowed to change any of these requirements by interpretation of
flexibilities indicated in other environmental documents, without case specific written permission from
Company. Flexibilities indicated in any environmental document are the prerogative of Company, not
the Contractors.
The space required to accommodate the topsoil stripping procedure, grade cuts, width and depth of the
soils, all in concert with pipe construction and installation, is the subject of the ACGR Plan. Space
acquired in advance of construction may not be sufficient for the contractors’ plans. Space and
procedural changes requested by the contractor may not be possible to approve or change. This
specifically includes any change to the ROW configuration for the placement of stripped A and B horizon
soils. If Company is unable to accommodate the requests or changes for space and procedure, the
resulting work will not result in any additional costs to Company.
Accuracy requirements for soil handling including removal, placement and replacement of topsoil,
subsoil, and ditch spoil, will involve equipment combinations of bulldozer, grader, backhoe, wheel
trenchers, and chain type trenchers. Which type of equipment will depend on soil characteristics, space
restrictions, and soil stockpile separation requirements, lack of soil stockpile separation, trench packing
requirements, pipe diameter considerations, and contractor execution capability. Contractor must
cooperate with the Company Representatives to achieve the required accuracy. Contractor is advised
that topsoil stripping is not to be performed by beginner operators. All equipment applications to
achieve the required accuracy for soil handing will be included in the Base Lay Price. Some characteristic
situations are as follows:


                                              Page 36 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                            OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


           Thin topsoils, ten (10) centimetres or less, require grader stripping.
           Thick topsoils require initial bulldozer removal for a high main pile peak with grader touch
            up to even the pile edge.
           Where the topsoil and subsoil interface is variable and/or very different in color, transitional
            stripping will be required with graders. Large graders will be required to prevent excessive
            multiple soil peaks.
           The topsoil/subsoil interface textural show percentage, and/or the color show percentage,
            will be determined by the Company Representative. This will normally be ten (10) to twenty
            (20) percent show prior to transitional, and seventy (70) to ninety (90) percent after
            transitional.
           Where the separation distance between soil horizons (A><B><C) is less than one (1) metre,
            alternative backfill methodologies to prevent overlap will be required. This is normally
            backhoes equipped with toothless buckets or clean-up blades. Overlap of different soil
            horizon materials is not allowed and will result in non-compliance shutdowns at
            Contractor’s cost.
           Specific to the pipe and Project, a protocol for trench packing must be discussed with
            Company. Packing only with tracked equipment, packing only with graders, or combinations
            are possible. If packing is required with specialized equipment, it will be specially highlighted
            in the bid documents.
           Topsoil will not be replaced in any area until the subsoil is smooth and free of ruts. A grader
            must be used to perform this work. All subsoil prepared areas must be approved by a
            Company Representative prior to topsoil replacement.
           Topsoil replacement in thin topsoils ten (10) centimetres or less must be performed with
            graders.
Contractor shall disc or rotor-till the areas to be stripped which have thick sod development on hay and
pasture land, as directed by Company. This operation may be waived by Company on sandy or dry soils
and on land with poor sod development.
All stripped topsoil shall be stockpiled separately from any subsoil, with a minimum of one (1) metre
separation. The one (1) metre separation may be relaxed if a sharp stripping edge can be created on
undisturbed hay land and pasture land.
Contractor shall salvage the “transitional layer” of lower topsoil/upper subsoil on agricultural lands
(non-bush lands) where directed by Company during non-frozen conditions. The transition layer must be
stockpiled in a discrete pile adjacent to the topsoil pile in accordance with the requirements of Appendix
B-1 Drawings and the EPP.
Potentially, surface material/topsoil in unimproved peaty soils will be trench width stripped unless
grading requirements dictate a wider stripping width. The salvage width/depth in peaty soils is shown
on the Drawings. This may also be accomplished through application of the mineral soil at depth
procedure.
All tracked equipment, unless otherwise approved by Company, shall stay outside the foreign line staked
safety buffer. The safety buffer shall be maintained all the while there is stripping, grading or excavation
work occurring within ten (10) metres of existing parallel adjacent pipeline(s).




                                              Page 37 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                             OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


No equipment or work of any kind will be allowed over existing pipelines unless allowed otherwise in
this Attachment B-2.4 – Construction Specifications.
Contractor shall strip an adequate width of topsoil for each of the topsoil stripping methods to ensure
topsoil is not mixed with subsoil or lost during construction. Contractor shall pay particular attention to
the width of topsoil stripped where poor or wet soil conditions exist to ensure that sloughing trench
conditions do not cause loss of topsoil or contamination of topsoil.
Wherever grading is required (side hills, slopes, stream crossings, road crossings, etc.), the topsoil shall
be stripped and stockpiled separately from graded or excavated subsoil, all at no additional
compensation to Contractor. Additional areas to be used by Contractor at each crossing shall be stripped
of topsoil prior to placement of any subsoil material in that area all at no additional compensation to
Contractor. Stripping is also required at locations of subsoil storage piles. Exemption of this
requirement is possible under winter conditions (frozen).
At locations where topsoil stripping occurs to accommodate grading requirements, Contractor shall
identify the topsoil piles with a suitably marked survey stake to minimize the risk of confusion at
time of restoration. Topsoil and subsoil colour differences should not be relied on due to moisture
and other factors.
Company may consider the use of geotextile or other Company approved protective covering in areas of
restricted space to prevent mixing of trench spoil and topsoil.
Contractor shall provide openings in the topsoil pile to permit drainage, wildlife crossings, and, where
necessary, to permit the Landowner to move his stock and equipment across the ROW. These openings
shall meet any requirement in Attachment A-1.5 - Line Lists and be no further apart than four hundred
(400) metres on average unless otherwise approved by Company.
All handling of topsoil shall take place only when it is relatively dry, to avoid deformation of soil
structure when too wet or pulverization when too dry as well as damage and soil intermixing due to
excessive rutting. In the event that significant soil erosion occurs due to high winds during topsoil
handling, Company may direct Contractor to suspend topsoil handling until conditions improve.
The decisions regarding such suspensions of Work will be made by Company and will be verbally
conveyed to Contractor and confirmed in writing.
At each road crossing, within the bar ditches topsoil shall be stripped full width and this topsoil shall be
stored within the bar ditch limits. Topsoil shall not be used for vehicle ramps across bar ditches.
Equipment used to strip the bar ditches shall be manually cleaned of any vegetation debris by track
shovels before that equipment leaves the road allowance. Exceptions will be individually considered by
Company.
At certain locations along the ROW, Contractor may be requested to “air clean” equipment to prevent
the risk of spreading weeds from one area to another. Company will advise Contractor of the location
where air cleaning equipment is required. Contractor shall maintain a record of all equipment cleaned,
the time of cleaning and the location. The applicable Unit Price Item shall apply when Company requests
equipment to be air cleaned.
5.1.6   Grading




                                               Page 38 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                          OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


The ROW shall be graded to facilitate the safe movement of pipeline vehicles and equipment, and to
safely perform the Work and to provide access to the Pipeline in accordance with the Contract
Documents and Good Industry Practices. Contractor may have to drill, blast and excavate rock in order
to build an adequate work surface along the pipeline route.
Grade cuts shall not be started outside the ROW unless Extra Work Space Areas approval has been
obtained from the Landowner or Authorities Having Jurisdiction. To the extent practical, grade cuts shall
not be started within two (2) metres of standing trees to protect the root system.
No graded material shall be placed off of the ROW unless Extra Work Space Areas has been obtained
from the Land Owner or regulatory authorities. No graded material shall be allowed to spread into treed
areas. Material shall be graded away from watercourses to minimize the risk of material entering the
watercourse.
Temporary erosion control devices shall be required during construction to prevent siltation entering
watercourses or private property. All grading shall be completed to maintain the original drainage or
water flow conditions as nearly as practical and shall conform to the regulations of Authorities Having
Jurisdiction.
Under winter conditions grade material may be placed on unstripped topsoil or USM provided the
surface is frozen and smooth. The grade material must be removed from the area concurrent with
construction. Under summer conditions, grade material area must be stripped, unless there is a well-
developed sod layer approved by Company.
Contractor must take steps concurrent with strip and grade activities, to label the topsoil, USM, and ‘B’
and ‘C’ spoil piles with survey lath and black marker. Contractor is advised that repair of errors made
due to the replacement sequence of soils will be at Contractor’s cost.
At road crossings, Contractor shall install temporary ramps through bar ditches in order to protect road
shoulders from ROW traffic damage. Culverts shall be installed through these ramps if required for
water flow. Topsoil shall not be used to build these ramps.
Contractor shall do necessary grading at river, stream and coulee crossings and at other locations
needed to permit the passage of its equipment, spanning drains, ditches and small streams with
temporary bridges or culverts in accordance with Attachment A-1.6 – Watercourse List and Attachment
B-2.4 – Construction Specifications so as not to interfere with stream flow or unduly damage stream
banks. The required setbacks, exclusive of the vehicle crossing must be respected. Care shall be taken to
prevent the damming or blocking of any drainage course. Contractor shall confirm with Company that
approval of the Authorities Having Jurisdiction over same has been secured prior to installation of any
crossing.
Two tone grade will only be allowed at Company’s discretion.
Contractor must advise Company as a part of the bid process where matting is expected to be used and
what type of mat is intended to be used.
Contractor is advised that Company recognizes three (3) different types of mats.
           Digging Mats that are typically made from thirty (30) centimetres squared timbers that are
            bolted or cabled together (“Digging Mats”). Contractor must supply all required digging
            mats within the Base Lay price.


                                             Page 39 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                            OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


            Tab and Slot Rig Mats that are typically made from wood alone and are nailed or bolted
             together (“Tab and Slot Rig Mats”). A separate Unit Price Item is required for their use. The
             Unit Price Item must specify cost per mat and/or per liner metre of ROW prepared for a
             given width. The Unit Price Item must cover sourcing, trucking placement and removal. The
             Company will not pay for the rental time after damage occurs, nor the replacement cost of
             damaged mats.
            Metal Edge Swamp Mats are typically made from planks surrounded with a metal edge.
             Length is up to 12.2 metres (40 ft) but many are shorter (“Metal Edge Swamp Mats”). A
             separate Unit Price Item is required for their use. The Unit Price Item must specify cost per
             mat of a given length and/or per liner metre of ROW prepared for a given width. The Unit
             Price Item must cover sourcing, trucking placement and removal. The Company will not pay
             for the rental time after damage occurs, nor the replacement cost of damaged mats.
Mats that are being paid for by Company must be removed as soon as possible to control costs.
Unnecessary delays and costs will be back charged to the contractor.
Contractor must keep a database of the mat locations and types. The information must be provided to
Company on request. Lost mats, including the rental, will not be paid for by Company.
5.1.7    Soil Erosion Control
When other dust control measures (water and packing) for topsoil and subsoil piles are not effective as
determined by Company and where directed by Company, Contractor shall apply a Company approved
tackifier solution to topsoil piles to control wind erosion of topsoil stockpiles and the working side of
the ROW. The costs associated with watering and packing piles shall be included in the Base Lay Price.
The tackifier shall be a Calcium-based Ligno Sulphonate (70%/30% water/product mix) applied at a
minimum rate of 1.1 litres/square metre. Contractor should be responsible to ensure that rate applied
realizes satisfactory erosion control. Tackifier shall be applied evenly using a hydroseeder, a spray bar or
other means satisfactory to Company. When tackifier is requested by Company, Contractor shall be
compensated for the supply and application of tackifier in accordance with the applicable Unit Price
Item in Schedule C - Commercial Terms.
The tackifier applicator shall be equipped to coat all sides of a peaked spoil pile, windrow and stockpiled
area.
A tackifier application that is not applied in compliance with this Specification and fails to provide
satisfactory erosion control, in the opinion of Company, shall be redone at no additional compensation
to Contractor.

6.1     Delivery and Transfer of Materials
All materials furnished by Company shall be received by Contractor on the schedule and at the delivery
points specified in Appendix A-3 - Company Supplied Materials.
Company will keep Contractor informed as to the movements of materials to be supplied by Company
and will endeavour to effect delivery of such materials in accordance with the schedule furnished to
Contractor.

Contractor shall cooperate with Company's representative during receipt and transfer of materials.
Upon transfer of material at the delivery locations, the material shall be checked for quantity and
condition by Contractor. Contractor shall, upon taking custody of the materials, satisfy itself that
materials are in an acceptable condition and appropriate quantity and shall advise Company of any
damaged, missing or otherwise unacceptable materials at the time of custody transfer to Contractor.
Contractor may store at stockpile or warehouse sites, valves and other materials whose usefulness
would not be impaired by storage in the open providing adequate security, as acceptable to Company, is
in place. Valves shall be stored in the full opened position. Material which could be damaged by
exposure to the elements shall be stored under cover in an area approved by Company, until need for
installation.
The transfer of Company furnished pipe and material from Company to Contractor and from Contractor
to Company shall be handled by the use of a Material Receiving Report (“MRR”). Both Contractor and
Company shall sign each Material Transfer Form (M.T.F.) and a copy of each shall be furnished to
Contractor.
Such written record shall deem that Contractor shall be responsible for all material after same has been
delivered to Contractor, and the lack of inspection by Contractor will not relieve it of responsibility for
the replacement of lost, stolen, damaged or missing material, at no additional compensation to
Contractor. Company will be responsible for correction of defects in Company supplied materials,
identified prior to the acceptance of the materials by Contractor.
Contractor shall, upon taking custody of the materials, perform a visual inspection to verify the
condition of the coating on pre-coated materials. Contractor may, at its own expense, elect to inspect
the coating for pin-holes, using an electronic holiday detector. Any coating defects in excess of three (3)
jeeps per pipe joint or assembly, found in the course of this inspection shall be clearly marked and will
be repaired at Company's expense. Any coating defects or damage found after the preliminary
inspection shall be repaired at Contractor's expense.
Contractor may waive all or any part of the preliminary coating inspection. However, by waiving this
preliminary inspection and mark-up of coating defects, Contractor automatically assumes full
responsibility for all coating repairs.
Company may warehouse certain miscellaneous, critical or delicate material at designated warehouse
sites, as identified in Schedule A - Scope of Work.
Valves and fittings may be provided to Contractor with end caps to maintain internal cleanliness. These
caps shall be maintained in place until the valves are installed in the fabrication. In the event that valve
ends are not capped at time of transfer to Contractor, Contractor will seal off the ends to the
satisfaction of Company and maintain this protection until the valves are installed in the fabrication.
Should any pipe or other material be damaged by Contractor, or should any pipe or other material for
which Contractor is responsible under Contract become damaged, lost, stolen, or otherwise
unaccounted for, the following terms and conditions shall apply:
           Contractor shall, at Company's option and at Contractor's expense, either satisfactorily
            repair such pipe or material or shall bear the full replacement costs for such pipe or material
            delivered to the job site;

6.1.1   Stockpile Sites
Stockpile sites for pipe have been acquired and prepared by Company and located as identified
Appendix A-3 - Company Supplied Materials. Pipe will be provided to Contractor stockpiled at these
sites.
Contractor is required to minimize further disturbance at the stockpile sites. These stockpile sites are
considered part of the construction Site and therefore the requirements of the Contract Documents and
environmental protection are applicable to these sites. This may specifically include topsoil stripping in
whole or in part.
Contractor will review each stockpile site to determine whether any additional site work is necessary to
allow load out of pipe from these sites. Contractor shall request in writing from Company any site
modifications it deems necessary to safely load out pipe, ten (10) days in advance of needing to make
these site changes. Company will review requested changes and where possible, within Project and
regulatory guidelines will work with Contractor to allow these site improvements. All costs associated
with further site improvements will be at no additional compensation to Contractor.
Contractor shall ensure that appropriate signs are erected in accordance with local authorities and
contract conditions, warning the public of construction activities.
Once Contractor has removed all the pipe from a stockpile site any lumber, spacer rope, end caps or
stockpile debris shall be cleaned up and disposed of to the satisfaction of the Authorities Having
Jurisdiction. Contractor shall reclaim these sites as follows:
       Previously disturbed industrial sites shall be levelled and returned to a condition consistent with
        that which existed when Contractor commenced removing pipe from them; and
       Stockpile sites located on agricultural land shall be de-compacted, with the rocks picked and
        topsoil replaced in accordance with this Attachment B-2.4 – construction Specifications.
       The cleanup work of the stockpile sites shall be at no additional compensation to Contractor.
        Contractor will not be required to revegetate the stockpile sites.

6.1.2   Pipe Handling and Hauling
Contractor shall load, haul and string pipe and other material in such a manner as to avoid damage to
such pipe, pipe coating or material.
Contractor shall ensure that any pipe end caps, ropes or clips that fall from loads during transportation
are picked up immediately.
Contractor shall be responsible for obtaining any special permits or approvals for the hauling and
stringing of pipe joints. Contractor shall abide by all Applicable Laws.
Pipe shall be loaded and unloaded by means of Company approved lifting devices. A minimum allowable
angle of forty five degrees (45°) and maximum allowable angle of seventy degrees (70°) shall be
maintained between the pipe and tag line during pipe handling operations. In the event that these
angles cannot be maintained, a Company approved spreader bar shall be used.
Contractor shall submit for approval to Company the proposed lifting hook and spreader bar design one
week before work begins. The engineering integrity of these designs shall be approved by a registered
engineer prior to submission to Company. The lifting hook shall be curved to fit to the pipe wall and
lined to prevent damage to beveled pipe ends. Contractor shall give notification to Company before this
work begins.
Trucking of pipe by Contractor shall comply with the following:
           The maximum pipe overhang from either end of the trailer shall be four (4) metres.
           A minimum of three (3) padded tie downs on each load shall be used. All pipe shall be
            protected from such objects which in the opinion of Company, will cause damage to the
            pipe or pipe coating.
           Pipe in excess of sixteen (16) metres shall be transported using pole trailers or Company
            approved equivalent.
           Pipe placed on trailers for transportation shall be properly supported with adequate padded
            supports in a manner approved by Company.
           Precoated pipe which will be nested on other pipe shall be separated by neoprene spacers
            or ropes to ensure contact does not occur between adjacent pipes.
           The truck and trailer must be equipped with mud guards and protectors to prevent stones
            from impacting the load.
           During Summer Construction, when trucking pre-coated pipe, pipe loads shall be completely
            tarped if hauling will occur on two (2) kilometres (or more) of road with loose gravel or road
            material, or if in Company's opinion coating damage is occurring.
           During winter construction pipe loads will be completely tarped.
           Contractor shall haul pipe only on those roads and access trails approved and developed for
            the Project. Truck drivers determined to have deliberately used access roads not approved
            for the Project or operating outside the staked working boundaries of the ROW shall be
            released from the Project.
Contractor shall ensure that minimum disturbance is made to other traffic using existing roads or access
roads.
6.1.3   Stringing



                                             Page 43 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                            OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


All pipe hauled to the ROW shall be unloaded and strung from stringing trucks using Company approved
lifting devices. Contractor shall take adequate precautions during stringing operations to avoid
damaging of pipe ends, or the denting, gouging, grooving or flattening of the pipe. Pipe shall be strung
onto wooden skids and shall be lapped, not butted. The pipe shall be strung on an adequate number of
skids to protect the pipe and coating against damage from uneven terrain. At no time shall the pipe be
allowed to contact the ground surface or protruding rocks.
Contractor is advised that a joint of heavy wall pipe, minimum of twenty (20) metres in length, is
required at both ends of each pipeline hydrostatic test section.
Pipe shorter than five (5) metres in length shall be separated by one full length pipe joint unless
otherwise approved by Company.
Pipe shall be strung only on ROW that is cleared and graded. In those areas where blasting is
anticipated, the pipe shall not be strung until after blasting.
Contractor shall string pipe in such a manner so as to leave up to a ten (10) metre wide access across
the ROW to correspond with gaps in the snow, topsoil, and ditch and spoil piles to facilitate the passage
of farm equipment, livestock and wildlife.
Contractor must collect all rope encirclement separators removed from the pipe and dispose of them in
accordance with the clean-up requirements of this Attachment B-2.4 – Construction Specifications.
Pipe strung on the ROW during the winter shall be kept capped to keep snow out of each pipe joint.
Garbage bags shall not be used as caps.
7.0 Trenching
7.1   General Requirements
Contractor shall excavate the pipeline trench on the surveyed line as staked by Company to a depth and
width sufficient to provide the required installation cover depth while accommodating all required
padding and all required appurtenances.
Contractor shall eliminate unnecessary bending wherever practical by varying the depth of the trench.
This will include excavating the trench deeper at the crest of ridges and by gradually deepening the
trench at approaches to crossings of roads, railroads, highways, ditches, creeks, rivers, coulees and other
water courses.
The bottom of the trench shall be uniformly graded in proper depths to prevent unnecessary bending of
the pipe and shall be free from loose rock and other objects which might damage the pipe or pipe
coating. All tree roots shall be cut flush with the sides and the bottom of the trench to prevent damage
to pipe coating.
Contractor's attention is directed to marshy and high water table conditions which may require
dewatering and/or concrete weighting, bag style weights or mechanical screw anchors as specified by
Company. At locations where concrete weighting, bag style weights or screw anchors or other
appurtenances are to be installed, Contractor shall provide a trench wide and deep enough to permit
installation, with the minimum specified depth of cover over the top of the weight or anchor. Company
will make best efforts to identify the start/stop location of buoyancy control devices in advance of
trenching operations but there may be instances where it is not possible to identify the weighting



                                              Page 44 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                            OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


requirements until after the trench is open. All costs for trenching requirements to accommodate the
installation of buoyancy control devices shall be included in the applicable Unit Price Item or the Base
Lay Price.
The trench shall be finished to the minimum dimensions shown on Appendix B-1- Drawings. Contractor
shall provide adequate trench depth to accommodate one hundred and fifty (150) millimetres of pipe
bedding material while still maintaining minimum cover requirements in those areas where soil
conditions will not allow laying the coated pipe on the trench bottom.
The trench bottom shall be excavated to ensure there are no rocks embedded just at or below the
finished trench bottom elevation. This can be accomplished by “raking” the trench bottom with the
teeth on the hoe bucket.
The grade of the final trench bottom shall be level and provide consistent and uniform support for the
pipe.
Contractor shall make all efforts to schedule operations such that freezing of the backfill is minimized.
Frozen lumps from ripping shall be separated from the trench spoil. Particular care shall be taken to
remove all lumps from the ditch bottom to provide a smooth flat bottom.
Contractor shall leave soil plugs in the trench to coincide with those breaks left in the topsoil pile or
where the trench will impede feeding or watering of livestock, to permit the Land Owner to move his
stock and equipment across and allow access for wildlife across the trench.
Contractor shall maintain the trench in stable and a safe condition until the pipe is installed. Contractor
shall dewater, shore or do what else may be required to excavate the trench, install the pipe and backfill
the trench in accordance with the Contract Documents. The cost for provision of all devices and
techniques required to ensure the trench is developed and maintained in a stable and safe condition
shall be included in the Base Lay Price.
Contractor shall have written approval from Land Owner or occupants and Company permission prior to
pumping water from the pipeline trench or ROW. Contractor is responsible for, and shall bear the costs
for damages or claims resulting from, the disposal of such water from the trench.
Under winter conditions, Contractor shall protect the trench line from frost penetration by roaching the
trench line with snow or other approved material and make all efforts to minimize the risk of frost
penetrating the trench line in areas of dry soil conditions, this includes keeping construction traffic from
driving on or near the proposed trenchline. On crown land the frost barrier roach may be constructed
with USM or snow. On private agricultural land the frost barrier roach must be constructed with clean
snow in areas where the topsoil stripping width is blade width or less. In areas topsoil stripped wider
than blade width subsoil or snow may be used to create the roach. Contractor will not be paid extra to
contend with frost penetration on ditch line, or elsewhere on the ROW. Where Contractor has not taken
reasonable precautions to protect the trench line against frost penetration and pipe protection is
required solely to protect the pipe and coating from frozen backfill, Contractor will be responsible for
costs associated with pipe protection measures requested by Company.
Unless otherwise approved in writing by Company, the trench at any given location shall not remain
open for longer than forty-eight (48) hours during summer construction and forty-eight (48) hours
during winter conditions, with the exception of specific tie-in and test point locations.
7.1.1   Muskegs with Mineral Soil at Depth


                                              Page 45 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                         OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Muskegs with mineral soil at depth may require two stage excavation. The top organic layer is removed
first and placed further to the right of the spoil placement area. The mineral soil is placed against the
organic material closer to the trench. This allows for the separate replacement of these materials during
backfill.
7.1.2   Rock Trench Excavation
“Rock” means a hard mineral material of the earth’s crust, exposed on the surface or underlying the soil,
a mass of rock projecting out of the ground or water and having natural material with a distinctive
composition of minerals.
Provided that Contractor adheres to the following procedure, compensation for Rock trench excavation
shall be in accordance with Schedule C – Commercial Terms for the amount of rock trench excavated as
recorded by Company.
           A prior written request is made to Company by Contractor for classification of trench
            material as Rock for the purpose of payment.
           Contractor first performs a test for Rock in the presence of the Company consisting of an
            attempt to rip the hard material using a single shank ripper equipped Caterpillar model D8
            dozer or equivalent.
           If as determined by Company, the ripper equipped dozed is unable to penetrate the ground
            and make reasonable forward progress or the ripped ditch material cannot be excavated
            with a backhoe or one of equivalent capability as utilized for trench excavation to the
            location of the rock test.
           Contractor repeats the test for Rock without delay as requested by Company.
           Contractor utilizes drilling and blasting or mechanical methods including a backhoe
            equipped with a hydraulic ram or other Company approved device to remove the rock.
           The location and length of rock excavation shall be recorded daily by both Company and
            Contractor and a concerted effort shall be made to reconcile any differences in the two
            records by the close of the day.
In the event Contractor fails to follow the above procedure and obtain the required approvals by
Company no compensation for rock excavation shall be made.
Excavation of boulders that can reasonably be removed from the trench with a backhoe (Caterpillar 320
or equivalent) is not considered to be rock trench excavation.
Frozen trench excavation or hard/compacted soils shall not be considered rock trench, regardless of the
ripping requirements.
Where rock, stones, boulders, gravel and/or other hard materials are in the bottom of the trench and in
the opinion of Company will damage the pipe or pipe coating, Contractor shall provide a trench deep
enough and wide enough to accommodate padding.
The disposal of rock arising from rock excavation shall be done in accordance with this Attachment B-2.4
– Construction Specifications, at no additional compensation to Contractor.
7.1.3   Depth of Cover
The minimum depth of finished soil cover over the top of pipe and appurtenances shall be in accordance
with alignment sheets, typical and site specific drawings. There shall be a minimum as specified in the

ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Drawings and Specifications of trench wall above the top of pipe and appurtenances on both sides of the
excavated trench, all in native soil that has not been previously disturbed.
NOTE: minimum depth of cover shall be measured from the top of pipe to the construction grade (i.e.
after topsoil removal and/or to graded surface.
The minimum depth of burial may be reduced to 0.6 m of cover in continuous depth bedrock. Additional
trench depth is required under the following conditions:
            Where additional depth is required within the Contract Documents.

             pipe bedding.
            At mainline block valve assemblies adjacent to existing roadways where additional depth is
             required to meet the municipal district road crossing depth requirement.
7.1.4    Landowner Access
Contractor shall provide temporary trench crossings and/or plugs to coincide with those openings left in
the topsoil pile to permit the Land Owner to move his livestock and equipment across the ROW.
8.0 Blasting
8.1     General
Contractor's handling, transporting, storage and use of explosives and all other hazardous materials shall
be accomplished in accordance with all applicable laws, regulations and orders of Authorities Having
Jurisdiction. Contractor will be responsible for, and shall at its expense make good any damage caused
by its handling, transporting, storing or use of explosives.
Any necessary permits for blasting shall be obtained by Company. Contractor will supply Company with
a Blasting Plan as required in this Attachment B-2.4 – Construction Specifications. No blasting shall be
permitted without prior written authorization from Company, and unless Company is present.
Contractor shall notify the public, owners and occupants of nearby buildings and lands, and the R.C.M.P.
at least forty eight (48) hours prior to the commencement of any blasting operations.
Only workers thoroughly experienced and certified where required, in handling explosives shall be
permitted to supervise, handle, haul or detonate explosives. Contractor shall ensure that no person shall
be allowed to conduct or direct a blasting operation unless that person is the holder of a valid blaster's
certificate.
Explosives shall be stored in locked magazines in accordance with practices specified by the Authorities
Having Jurisdiction.
Smoking, matches, firearms, open flames and other fire, spark or heat producing devices shall be
prohibited in or near the explosive magazine or while explosives are being handled, transported or used.
Any vehicle used to transport explosives from the magazine to the blast site shall have signs installed on
all four sides of the vehicle with the word "EXPLOSIVES" in red letters at least one hundred (150)
millimetres high.




                                             Page 47 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                            OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


No loaded holes shall be left unattended or unprotected. No explosives or blasting agents shall be
abandoned on the Worksite. Explosives shall not be primed or tied in until immediately before use and
shall not be left overnight in drilled holes.
After every blast, Contractor shall inspect the site for cut-offs and misfires and shall take appropriate
action to ensure that any un-detonated explosives are properly destroyed by detonating prior to
proceeding with the normal work routine.
Upon the approach of an electrical storm, Contractor shall discontinue all blasting related operations
and move the workers to secure positions away from the loaded holes. Furthermore, workers shall not
return to the worksite until the hazard has ceased. Contractor shall use lightning detectors (Electronics
Dir. Model SD-250B or approved equivalent) to detect the presence of lightning hazard.
Contractor shall, at all times, protect the Contractor Parties, Company ,Other Parties and the public from
any injury or harm that might arise from drilling dust and/or the use of explosives.
Where blasting will be performed adjacent to a road or other location accessible to the general public,
Contractor shall place suitable warning signs. Flag persons shall be posted on all road, rail, and water
access points within five hundred (500) metres of the blasting location. All road and river traffic shall be
halted to prevent any approach within five hundred (500) metres of the blasting location. Blasting shall
not be conducted when any road, railway or river traffic is within five hundred (500) metres of the
blasting operation.
Contractor shall use appropriate procedures, which may include blasting mats, where approved by
Company, blast design and adequate collaring, to preclude the possibility of damage due to flyrock, air
blast or vibrations when blasting is performed within five hundred (500) metres of roads, railroads,
canals, overhead or underground facilities or structures.
Only the blaster and Contractor's blasting supervisor shall be allowed closer than five hundred (500)
metres to the blast during blast firing.
Where blasting has taken place during previous construction or where grade blasting precedes ditch
blasting, an extreme hazard exists of un-detonated explosive being present in rock, rubble or boot legs.
Contractor shall comply with Worker's Compensation Board regulations and establish procedures for
locating, cleaning and inspecting of old drill holes and positioning and drilling of new drill holes.
All backhoes used in excavating rock after a blast shall be equipped with a blast shield in front of the
operator's position to protect the operator from flyrock should the hoe encounter an un-
detonated charge.
All surplus and un-detonated explosives shall be promptly removed from the Site after blasting
operations have been completed.
Proper deposition shall be made of all refuse from explosive material containers and in no case shall it
be disposed of in the trench backfill. Such refuse shall be disposed of in a manner that is satisfactory to
Company and Authorities Having Jurisdiction.
Contractor shall adhere to the blasting safety conditions within the Contractor’s Blasting Plan, Project
Safety Plan and Schedule D – HSE along with all other safety requirements of the Contract Documents.




                                              Page 48 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                                OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Approval by Company of any of the matters associated with blasting shall not relieve Contractor from
liability for any loss, costs, damages or expenses which may be caused by or result from Contractor's use
of explosives.
8.1.1   Blasting Near Buried Utilities
No drilling or blasting shall be permitted within three (3) metres of any buried utilities.
Contractor shall provide a fully operational seismograph (Instantel Model 477 or equivalent) at each
blast location where blasting will take place closer than eight (8) metres from any buried utility.
The intensity of the ground vibrations emanating from the blasting point shall be limited to a peak
particle velocity of fifty (50) milimetres per second on the ground above the buried utility at the nearest
point to the location of the blasting.
8.1.2   Blasting in or Near Watercourses
All blasting in, or within fifty (50) metre of the wetted perimeter of any watercourse shall be considered
part of the crossing activity. Such blasting shall be subject to the construction windows in Attachment A-
1.6 – Watercourse List, and subject to procedure requirements of Company and the Authorities Having
Jurisdiction.
All blasting shall comply with the procedures and safety precautions required by the Authorities Having
Jurisdiction, and shall comply with the requirements of this Attachment B-2.4 – Construction
Specifications.
Contractor shall employ measures such as pre-blast scare tactics and bubble curtains to move fish away
from the blasting zone prior to each blast within a named and sensitive unnamed watercourse.
The specific blasting plan for watercourse crossings must meet regulatory and Company requirements.
When blasting is required at any water crossing, Company will be responsible for securing any necessary
approvals from Authorities Having Jurisdiction for the watercourse. Contractor shall submit its proposed
procedures and safety precautions for blasting in a water body, and shall provide such proposal
document to Company at least sixty (60) days before watercourse blasting is scheduled to commence.
Upon approval by Company and the Authorities Having Jurisdiction, Contractor shall comply with these
procedures and safety precautions. Contractor shall, in any case, be responsible for the performance
and safety of all blasting in accordance with the blasting procedures elected for use. Contractor shall
notify Company thirty (30) days prior to commencement of this work, unless otherwise approved in
writing from Company and be in possession of a Company approved blasting plan.


8.1.3   Blasting Plan
Contractor Blasting Plan shall detail the items indicated below (“Blasting Plan”) and shall be submitted
to Company for approval thirty (30) days in advance of any blasting. The Blasting Plan shall include the
following:
           The type, characteristics and quantity of explosives which Contractor proposes to use;
           The proposed methods of transporting, storing, handling and using such explosives;

ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


            The proposed location of magazines and other storage facilities for explosives and
             detonators;
            The dates and hours during which Contractor proposes to carry out blasting operations;
            The safety procedures proposed to be followed including, without limitation, matting or
             other protective materials, signs, flag persons, and warning systems;
            The qualifications and permits held by Contractor's personnel who shall be directly
             responsible for handling and using such explosives;

Contractor shall conduct a small scale trial of the rock blast design proposed for use in each specific area

notification to Company before proceeding with any blasting.
The trial blast shall be performed in the presence of Company. The ground vibration, flyrock and
damage to nearby rock emanating from the trial blast shall be monitored by Company.
9.0 Bending
9.1     General
Contractor shall make all necessary pipe field bends required in the construction of the pipeline, but
Company, in accordance with Schedule A - Scope of Work, may authorize and furnish induction bends.
For field bending, as a minimum, Contractor shall comply with all conditions within the CSA-Z662.
No bending of pipe shall occur when the ambient temperature reaches negative thirty degrees (-30°)
Celsius or colder.
Pipe shall be lifted and carried and not be dragged along the ground. All precoated pipe shall be handled
using nylon rope chokers, padded slings or Company-approved equal.
Following the pipe bending operation, pipe shall be set up on skids in such a manner that gaps occur at
points along the ROW which coincide with animal passages previously constructed during the grading
and trenching operations.
9.1.1    Equipment
All field bends shall be made by the cold stretch, smooth bending method, using a bending machine with
a full solid-wall retaining shoe and an "internal mandrel" as manufactured by C.R.C. or equivalent. The
drive rollers, pin-up shoe and die shall be padded with urethane or neoprene as acceptable to Company.
9.1.2    Bending Requirements
All field bends shall be made to as long a radius as possible. No field bend shall be made within 1.2
metres of the end of a length of pipe. If the pipe is double jointed or triple jointed, field bends shall not
be closer than 0.6 metres to the circumferential weld creating the double pipe joint or triple pipe joint.
All over bends shall be made in such a manner that the crotch of the bend shall clear the high point of
the bottom of trench. All sag bends shall be made in such a manner that the pipe through the bend shall


                                               Page 50 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                            OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


be firmly supported on the trench bottom. All side bends shall be laid with a sufficient clearance from
trench wall.
Pipe bendability shall be confirmed through Contractor performed bend tests prior to production
bending. Bending parameters shall be confirmed through bend tests, but at no time shall the bending
radius exceed one to one and one-half degrees (1.0° - 1.5°) of arc per pipe diameter of length.
Pipe shall be bent so that the longitudinal seam when placed in the trench shall be in the upper one
hundred and eighty degrees (180°), and shall be bent so that the longitudinal seams of adjacent pipe
joints shall be offset by a minimum fifty (50) millimetres. In all bends, the longitudinal seams shall be on
the neutral axis, with the neutral axis being defined as within thirty degrees (30°) of the 12 o'clock
position for side bends and within thirty degrees (30°) of either the 3 o'clock and 9 o'clock positions for
sag and overbends.
Prior to bending any pipe for use in the Work, unless otherwise approved by Company, Contractor shall
bend specimens of pipe, wall thickness and grade to be used, including specimens having additional
protective coatings, for the purpose of determining the maximum degree of bending and the
distortional limitations to be permitted in the pipe. For such tests Contractor shall furnish the necessary
labour, equipment, materials and supplies and Company will furnish the pipe. Costs associated with this
bend test shall be included in the Base Lay Price.
Bends with buckles, wrinkles, flat spots or other mechanical damage exceeding the requirements of CSA
Z662 or this Specification will not be permitted in the pipeline. Bends with ripples are acceptable
providing the ripple is smoothly contoured throughout and there is no coating damage evident, peak-to-
trough measurement of any wave height does not exceed seventy five (75) percent of the pipe wall
thickness and the distance from the center of a ripple to the center of the closest ripple is no closer than
15 times the height of the ripple. Any bend, other than a test specimen, which is deemed by Company to
be unacceptable shall be cut and replaced at Contractor's expense. This shall also include the cutting
and re-beveling of all straight pipe sections from all unacceptable bends and the welding of the straight
pipe sections into the line. Contractor shall be charged by Company for all such damaged pipe at cost.
10.0 Pipeline Welding
10.1 Scope
This Section 10 applies to cross country pipeline welding of pipe to pipe butt joints using manual
welding techniques. This Section 10 does not apply to field and shop fabrication of pipeline assemblies
and facilities.
These welding specifications are based upon but not limited to those of CSA Z662 "Oil and Gas Pipeline
Systems" and the Alberta Pipeline Act and Regulations.
These welding specifications cover the requirements for:
           Bevel Preparation
           Equipment
           Materials
           Welding Procedure Qualification
           Welder Qualification
           Welding Consumables



                                              Page 51 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                          OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


           Production Welding
           Weld Inspection and Acceptance
           Repairs
           Fabrication
10.2 Definitions Related to Pipeline Welding Specification Requirements
Welding terms and definitions shall be in accordance with CSA Z662 and these welding specifications.
Arc Strikes - Localized areas where an electrical arc has heated an area away from the weld joint bevel
and weld heated affected zone (“H.A.Z”).
Controlled Cooling -A method of preventing accelerated cooling of a weld.
Controlled Welding Section - A section of welds consisting of a defined number of welds which
demonstrate Contractor's ability to establish and maintain a consistent workmanship standard as
defined by Company. See Section 10.10.2 of this Attachment B-2.4 – Construction Specifications.
Counterbore and Taper - A method of transitioning unequal pipe wall thicknesses.
Essential Change - A welding change that may affect the mechanical properties or quality of the weld. As
defined in CSA Z662 and this specification.
Inclement Weather - Weather conditions which prevent Contractor from operating safely or within the
scope of these welding specifications.
Latent Defects - Welding defects, which take time to initiate and propagate e.g. hydrogen cold cracks.
Minimum Interpass Temperature - The minimum temperature of the weldment at any time between
weld passes measured at a location fifty (50) millimetres from a production weld joint, or one hundred
and fifty (150) millimetres from the edge of a repair weld.
Maximum Interpass Temperature - The maximum temperature of the weldment between weld passes
measured immediately before the start of any weld pass, at a location 12.7 millimetres from the edge of
the weld.
Minimum Preheat Temperature - The minimum temperature that the pipe and weld area must be
immediately before welding is performed measured at a location fifty (50) millimetres from a production
weld joint, or one hundred and fifty (150) millimetre from the edge of a repair weld.
Maximum Preheat Temperature - The maximum temperature that the pipe and weld area can be heated
to at any location any time before or during welding.
Procedure Compliance - Compliance to all welding essential changes as defined by these welding
specifications and CSA Z662.
Procedure Qualification Record - Procedure Qualification Records are the actual documented variables
recorded during the qualification welding of test coupons to demonstrate the compatibility of
consumables and techniques in the joining of materials typical for a given application. It also contains
the mechanical test results of the tested specimens.




                                             Page 52 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                         OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Weld Repair Rate - The percentage of welds, which do not meet specified weld acceptance criteria. The
Weld Repair Rate is calculated by dividing the total number of welds produced during a given period by
the number of welds that require repair over the same period.
Winter Construction – Subject to the Project Construction Schedule.
Tie-In - The joining of pipe sections by welding completed in the ditch
Tack Welds – A temporary weld segment designed to hold a weldment in alignment prior to and during
welding.
Welding Data Sheet - A single page summary of the Welding Procedure Specification intended as quick
reference for the welders and inspectors to ensure familiarization of all the essential changes for
welding. Each welder shall receive a data sheet that applies to their particular welding application to
ensure they are aware of what practices must be followed.
Welding Procedure Specification - (WPS) The WPS identifies the essential changes recorded during the
development of the PQR and extends these into a range of essential changes to be followed for a
specific task. Welding requirements such as preheat temperatures, consumables and heat inputs are
identified in the WPS.
Welding Procedure - A summary of documents that includes:
           A Welding Procedure Specification describing all essential changes required to apply the
            procedure;
           Procedure Qualification Records describing all essential changes actually used during the
            preparation of test welds supporting qualification of a welding procedure; and all
            associated non-destructive and destructive examination results obtained for each test weld.
           Welding Production - This term extends to all the welding completed in the performance of
            the Work including mainline welding, tie-in welding and repair welding.
10.2.1 General
Contractor shall supply all labour, equipment and materials not specified as being supplied by Company
and shall perform all welding necessary to produce a continuous pipeline in accordance with the
requirements of the Contract Documents.
Welding shall be done by shielded metal arc welding (“SMAW”). Welds shall be produced by position
welding.
Contractor shall submit proposed welding and repair procedures to Company for approval thirty (30)
days prior to the start of any production welding. No welding shall be done unless the appropriate
approved welding specification is on site. The requirements of the welding procedure specification are
detailed within these welding specifications.
Welding procedure specifications and welder qualifications shall be in accordance with the
requirements of CSA Z662, these welding specifications and those of the Provincial Acts and Regulations
(BC Oil and Gas Activities Act or Alberta Pipeline Act).
Contractor shall monitor and document welding changes and shall provide this documentation to
Company. The frequency of checking and form of documentation shall be established by Contractor and
shall be submitted for approval by Company prior to production welding.


                                              Page 53 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                           OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Contractor shall ensure that all persons under its direction involved with welding are fully aware of
requirements for welding and all welders and related foremen are in possession of the appropriate
welding procedure data sheets.
10.3 Weld Classification
Butt joints shall be of the single Vee type of groove. End preparations shall be approved by Company
prior to qualification of welding procedures.
10.4 Bevel Preparation
Bevel preparation shall be as shown on Company approved welding procedure specification. Bevel
dimensions shall remain as specified on Company approved welding specification and shall be checked
and documented by Contractor on a regular basis. The frequency of checking and form of
documentation shall be established by Contractor and shall be submitted for approval by Company prior
to production welding.
In addition to the requirements of CSA Z662 Figure 7.2, the following supplementary requirements are
applicable.
           If the difference in nominal wall thickness of adjoining pipes exceeds 1.6 millimetres,
            transitioning of the thicker pipe down to the thinner pipe shall be required. The design of
            such transitioning shall accommodate the welding technique and the non-
            destructive examination technique without additional setup or delays.
           For final tie-ins, a minimum fifty (50) millimetres length counterbore with thirty degree (30°)
            taper shall be used, subject to compliance with strength and thickness requirements.
The taper angle shall not be greater than thirty degrees (30°). All transitioning designs shall be approved
prior to production welding.
During pipe end preparation work, bevel shavings pose a significant hazard to livestock and wildlife; all
waste metal shall be collected during the work activity and removed from the ROW at the end of each
day for appropriate disposal. When a counterbore machine or a beveling machine tool is being used, this
work shall be done over a tarpaulin laid out to collect the shavings. When a beveling torch is used, the
debris metal pieces shall be picked up after each cut. Company may require an alternative magnetic pick
up procedure if the tarpaulin collection method is not deemed by Company to be successful.
10.5 Equipment
Contractor shall supply all necessary equipment for the satisfactory completion of the Work, and the
equipment shall be maintained in such condition as to provide continuity of operation, and safety of
personnel.
Welding equipment shall be of a size and type suitable to produce welds in accordance with these
welding specifications and at rate required to meet the Project Schedule.
Arc welding equipment shall be operated within the amperage, voltage, travel speed and heat input
ranges specified in Company approved welding procedure specifications.
Welding and line-up clamps shall be designed to avoid mechanical damage to the piping and to maintain
alignment to within specified dimensions.

PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                          OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Sufficient spare parts and/or equipment shall be provided and maintained by Contractor to ensure
consistent weld quality and continuity of welding production.
Grounding devices shall be securely fastened to ensure freedom from arcing during welding and shall be
designed such that the grounding location is inside the joint bevel.
Company reserves the right to prohibit the use of equipment, which it deems unsuitable for proper
performance of the Work.
10.6 Materials
10.6.1 General
Only new filler metals and shielding gases having prior approval from Company shall be used.
10.6.2 Filler Metals
Filler metals shall be certified as conforming to CSA W48-14; or having mechanical properties that meet
the requirements of the aforementioned standard.
Filler metals shall be stored and handled so as to avoid damage to the filler metals and to the containers
in which they are shipped. Filler metals in opened containers shall be protected from deterioration and
those that show signs of deterioration shall be disposed of. Any portion of a box or container found to
be damaged or damp shall cause rejection of the entire box or container. As well, all welds found to be
welded using suspect electrodes may be cut out and replaced at Contractor's expense. Storage,
exposure periods and re-conditioning of electrodes shall be in accordance with manufacturer's
recommendations.
Low hydrogen shielded metal arc welding electrodes (EXX18), when removed from sealed containers,
shall be stored in cabinets at temperatures in the hundred and twenty degrees (120°) Celsius to hundred
and fifty degrees (150°) Celsius range prior to use. Low hydrogen SMAW electrodes that have been
exposed to atmospheric conditions for more than one (1) hour shall be discarded.
Company reserves the right to prohibit the use of materials, which it deems unsuitable for proper
performance of the Work.
10.7 Qualification of Welding Procedure Specification
10.7.1 General
Weld procedures are required for mainline, tie-in and repair welding, as applicable to the scope of work
of Contractor. For weld procedure qualification purposes, welding operations have been classified as
follows:
           Mainline welding, tie-in welding, and
           Mainline and tie-in repair welding
Prior to the start of work, welding procedures shall be developed, qualified, and documented by
Contractor for each welding operation within the scope of work of Contractor. Welding procedures shall
cover the entire range of materials and welding variables within Contractor scope of work. This may
necessitate the preparation and testing of several qualification test coupons.

Depending upon the final construction organization and Work detail, it is possible that one welding

with governing essential changes, it may be possible for Contractor to use the same welding procedure
for site fabrication and tie-in welding.
Each welding procedure shall be approved in writing by Company prior to production use.
Contractor may submit previously qualified welding procedure qualifications for approval by Company.

preheat/interpass temperatures shall be utilized to verify compliance. Documentation of compliance
verifications shall be made and shall be submitted to Company. The frequency of checking and form of
documentation shall be established by Contractor and shall be submitted for approval by Company prior
to production welding.

10.7.4 Mainline Weld Procedure Qualification
Mainline welding procedures may be qualified on pipe supplied for the Project, according to these
welding specifications and CSA Z662. Qualifications shall consider the effect of worst- case interpass
cooling times that could occur during production welding.


10.7.5 Mainline & Tie-In Repair Weld Procedure Qualification
Mainline and tie-in repair weld procedures may be qualified on pipe supplied for the Project according
to these welding specifications and CSA Z662. The repair weld procedures shall consist of a simulated
through wall repair of a girth weld.
Repair welds shall be completed as follows:
           Greater Than Grade three hundred and eighty six (386) MPa
            o a through wall repair simulation, where the root and hot pass are deposited in the
               downhill direction using E6010 and E8010 cellulose electrodes. Fill and cap passes shall
               be completed in the uphill direction with low hydrogen consumables.
           Less Than Grade three hundred and eighty six (386) MPa
            o a through wall repair simulation, where all passes are deposited using cellulose
                electrodes in the downhill direction.
            o   all weld repair procedures shall be completed using one hundred and twenty degrees
                (120°) Celsius minimum preheat, and interpass temperature. Each repair weld shall
                be non-destructively tested by radiographic methods and magnetic particle methods
                after the weld has cooled to ambient temperature and destructively tested.
           Two tensile tests, two root bends, two face bends, weld metal impact tests, HAZ impact
            tests, and a hardness survey shall be carried out on samples removed. Impact testing is not
            required for welds in pipe with a nominal wall thickness of less than six (6) millimetres.
10.7.6 Tie-In Weld Procedure Qualification
If mainline welding procedures are deemed unsuitable for tie-in welding, then tie-in welding procedures
shall be developed and qualified.
10.7.7 Non-Destructive Testing of Weld Procedure Qualification Test Coupons
Immediately after welding, each weld procedure qualification test coupon shall be visually examined
and fully radiographically inspected. Acceptance criteria shall be as stated in CSA Z662.
Each weld procedure qualification test coupon shall be left for at least forty eight (48) hours. After this
time period:
           the weld procedure qualification test coupon shall be completely re- radiographed and shall
            be interpreted to the requirements of CSA Z662, and
           each root bead shall be examined for evidence of cracking by the magnetic particle method,
            using a wet fluorescent or black and white colour contrast indicating mediums.

10.7.8 Destructive Testing of Weld Procedure Qualification Test Coupons
Following successful completion of non-destructive examinations, weld procedure test coupons shall be
destructively tested according to the requirements of CSA Z662 and the following requirements.
           The facility chosen by Contractor for mechanical testing shall be approved by Company.
           If the procedure is approved, Contractor shall have an appropriately qualified individual
            prepare a Welding Data Sheet and provide it to Company for approval.
           Contractor shall be responsible for the performance and quality of all welding, in accordance
            with the welding procedures approved for use. Contractor shall signify its acceptance of this
            responsibility by signing the Welding Data Sheet.
           Copies of the applicable approved welding procedures shall be on-site during production
            welding. All production welding shall be in accordance with the approved procedures.
Each Procedure Qualification Record shall include testing of at three weld metal and three heat affected
zone Charpy impact specimens removed from each procedure qualification test coupon. Weld metal
specimens shall be notched on the centerline of the weld and normal to the surface. Heat affected zone
specimens shall be etched and notched so that the root of the notch is located in as much of the heat
affected zone as practical, and normal to the surface.
Proven notch toughness properties shall not be required for pipe with a nominal wall thickness of less
than six (6) millimetres.
Impact tests shall be conducted in accordance with ASTM E23 at or below the minimum design
temperature for the pipe to be welded. Typically the minimum design temperature will be:
           Five degrees (5°) Celsius for below ground and indoor piping assemblies; and
           Forty five degrees (45°) Celsius for above ground and outdoor piping assemblies.
Absorbed energy shall be reported for each specimen, and shear area or lateral expansion should be
reported. The absorbed energy of weld metal and heat affected zones shall be:
           Twenty seven (27) Joules minimum average for three full size specimens; and
           Twenty (20) Joules minimum for any full size individual specimen.
Percent shear and lateral expansion for each specimen should be reported. Each Procedure Qualification
Record shall include at least one Vickers hardness survey on a cross section of the qualification weld.
The hardness survey shall be conducted in accordance with ASTM E92 or E384, using a load in the range
of one (1) to ten (10) kilograms or two hundred and fifty (250) to one thousand (1000) grams,
respectively.
The hardness survey shall include at least two (2) ROWs of readings across the weld metal, both coarse
grained heat affected zones, and the parent metal on each side of the weld, within two (2) millimetres
of each surface. HAZ indentations shall be placed in the hardest appearing structures, such as those
located adjacent to the toe of the cap or root pass, even if these structures do not coincide precisely
with the line of survey.
Maximum hardness shall be three hundred and twenty five (325) HV, except that isolated readings up to
three hundred and fifty (350) HV may be accepted provided that two additional tests in the same area
are three hundred and twenty five (325) HV or less.
