10.8 Welder Qualification
10.8.1 General
Contractor shall use only skilled and qualified welders. Welders shall qualify by demonstrating their
ability to produce acceptable welds in accordance with Company approved welding procedure
specifications for the particular welding configuration or application to be used in production welding.
No welder shall carry out any phase or type of welding for which he has not been tested and accepted
by Company as qualified.
10.8.2 Test Requirements
All welder qualification test costs shall be borne by Contractor. Pipe material used for welder
qualification testing will be provided by Company. The pipe coupons shall be at least fifty (50)
centimetres in length.
For pipe diameters greater than 323.9 millimetres OD, for the purpose of the welder qualification
testing, terminology “weld”, shall mean one half of the total pipe circumference.
For pipe diameters less than 323.9 millimetres OD, for the purpose of the welder qualification testing,
terminology “weld” shall mean the entire pipe circumference.
When internal line-up clamps are to be used for the work, welder qualification testing shall be
completed using internal line-up clamps.
Tie-in welders shall also be tested for repair welding. Tie-in welders that have not tested for repair
welding may not be permitted to weld tie-ins.
Before starting qualification tests, welders shall be given training sufficient to allow them to obtain
adequate skills to produce acceptable welds on a consistent basis.
Welders performing repairs shall be qualified in accordance with the approved full through wall repair
welding procedure. This test shall qualify them for partial through wall repairs and back-weld repairs.
The repair-welding test shall consist of simulating two full-through-wall repair welds on a previously
completed test weld, with the pipe in the horizontal - fixed position. Two sections, one located
approximately at the 12 – 2 o’clock position and one located approximately at the 4 – 6 o’clock position,
shall have the weld metal removed by grinding to a depth that permits-welding of the root pass. The
width of the repair section shall be that of the original groove. Each section ground out shall be
subsequently repaired from the root pass through to the cap pass using an approved welding procedure.
The length of each repair segment shall be a minimum of one hundred (100) millimetres.
Test welds shall be produced in accordance with Company approved welding procedure, by each
welder, and shall be visually and radiographically inspected using techniques similar to those to be used
for inspection of production welding. Acceptance criteria shall be as stated in CSA Z662. Each weld
procedure qualification test coupon shall then be set aside and retained for further examination by
Company. Such further examinations are not considered part of the performance qualification tests.
All test welds shall be witnessed by Company and failure to comply with the welding procedure
specifications shall be cause for rejection.


                                              Page 61 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                            OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Contractor shall prepare and maintain a list of welders and their qualifications, which shall be updated
after any change of welding personnel and submitted to Company.
Each welder shall be assigned a unique number to identify their welding. No other welder shall receive
the same number and if a welder is terminated or leaves the Project the number shall not be reassigned.
Contractor shall provide a list of qualified welders with corresponding numbers to Company.
If, in the opinion of Company, failure of a welder to pass a test was because of unavoidable conditions or
conditions beyond his control, such a welder may be given a second opportunity to qualify. No further
tests shall be given.
A welder may be required to re-qualify at any time if there is any reasonable doubt about the ability to
produce acceptable welds.
Contractor shall notify Company twenty four (24) hours in advance of carrying out welder qualification
tests to allow Company to witness the welding and subsequent testing and arrange for an NDT unit to
be available.
10.8.3 Welding Consumables
The maximum SMAW electrode diameter shall be four (4) millimetres for the root and four point eight
(4.8) millimetres for all other passes.
E8010 electrodes shall not be used for root passes. The root pass shall be completed with E6010
electrodes.
For pipe grades greater than Grade 386, all other passes shall be completed with E8010 electrodes. For
pipe grades less than Grade 386, all other passes shall be completed with E7010 electrodes.
The fill and cap passes of mainline repair or tie-in repair welds for pipe grades greater than Grade 386
shall be completed with E8018-C3 electrodes. The fill and cap passes of mainline repair or tie-in repair
welds for pipe grades less than Grade 386 may be completed using cellulose electrodes.
The specified tensile strength of filler metals and fluxes shall not exceed five hundred and fifty (550)
MPa.
If changes to filler metal or flux brand name or AWS/ASME classification are necessary, complete
requalification of the welding procedure with the new filler metal is required. Company shall be
informed of any changes of electrode brand name from that used for procedure qualifications. Company
reserves the right to require requalification of a welding procedure based on electrode brand name
change.
10.9 Production Welding
10.9.1 General
The welding of piping shall be performed using qualified welders in accordance with Company approved
qualified welding procedure specifications. Production welding shall not be performed when conditions
encountered exceed the limits stated in the procedure specification.
Contractor shall continuously monitor welding to ensure compliance with the welding requirements.
Documentation of compliance verifications shall be made and shall be submitted to Company. The



                                              Page 62 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                           OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


frequency of checking and form of documentation shall be established by Contractor and shall be
submitted for approval by Company prior to production welding.
To facilitate non-destructive testing and to allow access across the ROW to animals and Land Owner,
Contractor shall be required to leave gaps in the pipe sections to correspond with the gaps left in topsoil
piles and plugs in the trench unless otherwise approved by Company.
For pipe grades greater than three hundred and eighty-six (386), internal line-up clamps shall not be
removed until the second pass has been made for at least two hundred and fifty (250) millimetres on
the bottom of the weld.
The hot pass shall follow the root bead as closely as possible. Not more than ten (10) minutes shall be
permitted between completion of the root bead and start of hot pass. If this cannot occur due to
unavoidable conditions, the minimum interpass temperature shall be maintained and at no time shall
the weldment be allowed to drop below the minimum interpass temperature until the second pass is
completed. Under no circumstances shall the minimum temperature be below the interpass
temperature until the completion of the hot pass. Re-heating is permitted prior to the start of the
fill/cap pass.
When welding externally coated pipe, Contractor shall place a sheet of non-flammable material with a
minimum width of six hundred (600) millimetres on each side of the weld to prevent weld spatter from
damaging the coating. Contractor shall be responsible for correction of damage to coating caused by
welding or cutting bands.
Internal back welding shall not be permitted unless Company approved welding procedure qualification
of such welds expressly meets the requirements specified in CSA Z662.
Company reserves the right to complete post welding inspections up to twenty four (24) hours after
welding if in the opinion of Company the welds may be susceptible to cracking.
10.9.2 Pipeline Production Welding Start-Up Demonstration
Prior to the start of full production welding Contractor shall demonstrate its ability to execute
acceptable welding by welding up to a maximum of two sections of each pipe diameter, each containing
approximately twenty welds. Company will inspect these welds promptly and advise Contractor of the
results. If, prior to repair, two percent (2%) or more of these welds are unacceptable according to the
requirements of CSA Z662 and this specification, Contractor shall identify the cause and make necessary
changes prior to attempting another demonstration. All demonstration tests shall be done at no
additional compensation to Contractor.
10.9.3 Preparation of Pipe
Preparation of pipe shall require that all piping ends which are to form a part of the welded joint shall be
cleaned to sound metal immediately prior to welding to ensure complete removal of all paint, grease,
oxide, rust and any other extraneous matter. Cleaning shall extend for at least twenty-five (25)
millimetres from the piping edges on both internal and external surfaces.
Beveled ends shall be smooth and uniform and shall comply with the dimensions and geometry
specified in the qualified and approved welding procedure specifications. Small score marks,
indentations or other small defects within the joint preparation area shall, at the discretion of Company




                                              Page 63 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                            OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


may be blended out by grinding, otherwise the bevel shall be re- prepared. No welding repair of bevels
shall be permitted.
All shavings from beveling or transitioning shall be collected on a tarp followed by magnet rolling the
area. The shavings will then be transferred to containment prior to the next bevel cut, and removed
from the ROW upon completion of each day, and disposed in accordance with the Authorities Having
Jurisdiction.
If applicable, Contractor shall supply suitable labour to train in the use of the facing/bevel machine prior
to starting production welding.
Preparation for welding of pipes of different wall thickness shall be in accordance with this Specification,
and the latest approved version of CSA Z662.
Manufacturer's pipe joint numbers, pup length and heat numbers shall be transferred by Contractor to
each length of pipe cut from any joint of pipe. Identification shall be made by suitable marking using
indelible permanent marking crayons.
Contractor will be required to restore the coating cut back and grind these seams on pipe ends that have
had the factory end cut off.
All welding rod stubs, wire spools or other refuse remaining from welding work shall immediately be
removed from the pipe or surrounding area and disposed of from the right-of- way in accordance with
the Authorities Having Jurisdiction.
10.9.4 Alignment & Fit Up
Pipe joints shall be thoroughly cleaned and bevel shavings, dirt, snow, ice, water and other foreign
substances shall be removed from the pipe prior to alignment for welding.
Internal line-up clamps shall be used for all pipeline production welding for pipes with an outside
diameter greater than 323.9 mm, and shall not be removed until, at a minimum, the root bead has been
one hundred percent (100%) completed. For pipe grades greater than three hundred and eighty-six
(386) MPa, pipe movement is not permitted until completion of a one hundred and fifty (150)
millimetres second (hot) pass on the bottom of the pipe.
External line-up clamps shall be used for tie-in welds. Root bead segments shall be spaced uniformly
around the full circumference of the joint and, where practical, shall have a cumulative length of at least
50% of the joint circumference prior to clamp removal.
Longitudinal pipe manufacturing welds in adjacent lengths of welded pipe shall be offset by a minimum
of fifty (50) millimetres. Longitudinal seams should be located at approximately the 10 o'clock and 2
o'clock positions, except in the case of bends.
Where approved by Company, at crossing locations such as roads, streams and utility crossings,
Contractor may weld up to eight (8) pipe joints together as a separate operation using external line-
up clamps.
Line-up clamps shall be used in accordance with the approved welding specification. Care shall be taken
when using internal line-up clamps to minimize stress at the pipe ends.




                                              Page 64 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                            OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


The welded pipe shall be laid on skids after welding so that no portion of the pipe is allowed to touch
the ground. The pipe shall be blocked and secured from rolling off skids in a manner acceptable to
Company. The spacing of skids shall be adequate to prevent undue stress on the free spanning pipe and
on partly completed welds, (two support locations per full length joint would normally be expected).
Field welds shall be left accessible for their full circumference.
Should a section of the line fall off the skids, Contractor shall immediately report this fact to Company.
Company shall be allowed reasonable time to inspect the pipe section involved and Contractor shall cut
out any defects and damaged pipe at no additional compensation to Contractor.
During the final weld at a tie-in section, the pipe shall be fully supported such that the pipe is not moved
until all of the weld fill passes are complete.
All tie-ins shall be finished the same day they were started.
10.9.5 Weather Conditions
Welding shall not be done when the quality of completed welds would be impaired by prevailing
weather conditions including but not limited to: extreme cold, rain and snow, blowing sand or high
winds. Contractor shall provide wind breaks of a type that will give adequate protection to the welder
and the weld when in the judgment of Company such equipment is required.
Welding shall not be continued when the weld quality could be impaired by the prevailing weather
conditions.
10.9.6 Preheating
Preheating shall be performed using Company approved methods as specified on the approved welding
procedure specifications.
The minimum preheat temperature shall extend around the entire circumference of the pipe and at
least fifty (50) millimetres on each side of the weld joint.
During completion of the weld, the joint shall be maintained at a temperature between the minimum
and maximum interpass temperatures and shall be checked using temperature indicating crayons or
other suitable method immediately prior to, and during the full welding operation. No welding shall take
place unless the minimum interpass temperature is maintained. The heating of local areas above the
upper limit of preheating, as identified on the approved Welding Procedures, is not permitted.
Contractor shall ensure that the pipe coating is not damaged by the application of preheat. Care should
be taken to prevent overheating, and no part of the area shall be heated in excess of two hundred
degrees (200°) Celsius.
Contractor shall take precautions to avoid accelerated cooling of the weld. Insulating blankets or other
appropriate methods shall be used to control the weld cooling rate until it has reached ambient
temperature. If interpass temperature cannot be maintained, blanketing shall be required
10.9.7 Welding Sequence
Root bead welding shall only commence after ensuring that the parts to be joined are adequately
secured against movement. Movement of the pipe joint shall not be permitted until the root pass is one
hundred percent (100%) completed. For pipe grades greater than three hundred and eighty-six (386)



                                              Page 65 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                           OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


MPa, pipe movement is not permitted until completion of a one hundred and fifty (150) millimetres
second (hot) pass on the bottom of the pipe.
The second pass shall start as soon as possible after the root pass and in any case within the specified
time period stated on Company approved welding procedure specification.
Weld sequencing shall be such that consecutive stop/start locations are staggered by a minimum of fifty
(50) millimetres.
Clusters of surface porosity, bead starts, heavy glass deposits and high points shall be removed by
grinding prior to depositing weld metal over them. Cleaning shall be done by power or hand tools or
both to the satisfaction of Company.
The approved welding procedure shall be such that the completed weld shall have a uniform cross
section around the entire circumference of the pipe. At no point shall the top of the cap pass be below
the surface of the pipe or above the pipe surface by more than two and a half (2.5) millimetres for pipe
nominal wall thickness less than ten (10) millimetres and three and a half (3.5) millimetres for pipe
nominal wall thickness greater than (10) millimetres.
The completed surface of the weld shall be thoroughly power brushed clean of all spatter and the
reinforcement shall blend smoothly with the adjacent pipe surface. The top cap button shall be ground
to blend smoothly into the remaining weld pass and shall not be permitted to exceed the maximum
stated above.
Continuity of the pipe welding operation shall be maintained and at no time shall the root pass and hot
pass operation be more than sixty (60) minutes ahead of the remaining weld passes.
Welding shall continue until a minimum of three (3) weld passes are completed or two thirds (2/3) of
the weld thickness is filled, whichever is the greatest and shall not be left unfilled longer than twenty
four (24) hours. Where it can be anticipated that welds would be left longer than twenty four (24) hours
they shall be filled to completion. The number of uncapped welds shall be limited to one set-up unless
otherwise directed by Company.
Partially completed cap passes shall be completed before the end of each day.
Each welder shall identify his work by marking the pipe adjacent to the weld with his unique
identification number using an indelible permanent marking crayon.
Winter Construction (defined as all welding on pipe OD greater than 323.9 millimetres OD, completed
after October 31 or otherwise defined by the Company)
The following requirements shall apply for all winter welding:
           Minimum of two welders shall be used for all weld passes.
           Incomplete welds are not permitted (i.e., welds shall be completed including the cap pass).
Completed welds and an area extending fifty (50) millimetres on each side of the weld shall be re-
heated to a temperature between one hundred and twenty degrees (120°) Celsius minimum and one
hundred and seventy nine degrees (179°) Celsius maximum after the cap pass and shall be tightly
wrapped with Company approved thermal blankets. Care shall be taken to ensure that no coating or
pipe damage occurs because of the re-heating. Blankets shall not be removed until the temperature of



                                              Page 66 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                            OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


the weld and surrounding fifty (50) millimetres of pipe has reached a temperature of fifty degrees (50°)
Celsius or less.
10.9.8 Night Capping
The open end of welded sections of pipe shall be securely closed at the end of each day's work by
suitable covers over the ends to prevent the entrance of trash, animals or other obstructions, and these
shall not be opened until work at that location is to be resumed. Where the line is left open at intervals
for pigging, testing or future tie-ins at roads, railroads, rivers, etc. both ends shall likewise be capped.
Temporary night caps shall not be tack welded to the pipe and shall be more robust than garbage bags.
10.9.9 Pipe Pups
Pipe pups three (3) metres and over shall be moved ahead daily and welded into the line. Pipe pups less
than five (5) metres in length shall be separated by a full joint of pipe. Pipe pups shall not be allowed to
accumulate on the ROW and a reasonable attempt shall be made to weld all pipe pups into the line.
Company may stop Contractor's mainline welding operation prior to completion of mainline welding in
order that accumulated pipe pups can be moved ahead and welded into the line. Pups less than three
(3) metres in length shall be hauled to Company designated storage area.
For tracking purposes, Contractor shall transfer pipe and heat numbers and pup lengths to both ends of
pipe cut from any joints of pipe. Identification shall be made by suitable marking using indelible
permanent marking crayons.
10.9.10 Welding Refuse
Welding electrode stubs or other refuse produced by the welding operator shall be removed from
the ROW immediately. Contractor shall ensure that refuse shall not be left inside the pipe or trench.
10.10 Welding Inspection & Acceptance
10.10.1 Right to Inspect
Company shall have the right to inspect and monitor all aspects of production welding to ensure that
the welding procedures are being adhered to, and shall have the right to reject any welds in which the
details of the welding procedure are not adhered to.
All reasonable attempts will be made to provide non-destructive test results of all welds except tie-
in welds to Contractor approximately one hour before the start of the next working day. Non-
destructive test results for tie-in welds will be provided to Contractor on the same day as weld
completed unless otherwise advised by Company. Contractor shall cooperate fully with the crews
carrying out the tests. Welds made under undue stress conditions may be left one full day before final
inspection.
Contractor shall be responsible for cleaning of the weld area in a manner sufficient to permit proper
inspection.
Company shall perform visual inspection on completed welds and welds shall be assessed for the
presence of defects in accordance with the requirements of this Specification and the requirements of
CSA Z662.




                                              Page 67 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                            OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Other methods of non-destructive testing may also be used on production welds at the option of
Company.
Company, at its option, may cut out all questionable welds or additional welds for production test
purposes. If the weld is proven unsatisfactory by not meeting CSA Z662 requirements, or the
requirements herein, Contractor shall bear the cost of the cut-out and the replacement weld.
All welds that fail testing shall be replaced at no additional compensation to Contractor. Company will,
whenever possible, select test welds to be cut from the pipeline in such a manner or at such a time so as
to result in a minimum replacement cost. If it is not possible to pull the pipe back into a position after a
weld has been removed, a pup joint with a minimum length of 1.22 metres shall be set in and two (2)
welds shall be required to close the line. Company reserves the right to have Contractor cut any of these
replacement welds from the pipe if it so desires.
Welds that do not comply with the Standards of Acceptability as set forth herein shall be removed or
repaired at Company's discretion. Repairs will not be permitted if the defective segment has been
repaired previously.
10.10.2 Methods of Inspection
Visual inspection shall be performed on all welds and shall be assessed in accordance with the
workmanship standards in CSA Z662. Company has the right to reject any and all welds that in its
opinion, although marginally satisfy the above regulations, could still prove to be detrimental to the long
term security of the pipeline.
All welds shall be inspected for one hundred percent (100%) of their circumference using radiographic
techniques. Defect acceptance criteria shall be based upon the defect acceptance criteria outlined in
CSA Z662 "Standards of Acceptability".
If non-destructive testing results indicate a weld defect rate greater than fifteen percent (15%), based
on Contractor's actual welding rate for each day, then Company reserves the right to cease all welding
operations until Company is satisfied that the welding problem has been defined and corrected.
On resumption of welding operations, Contractor shall produce a "Controlled Welding Section" of
twenty (20) welds, which Company shall promptly inspect. During the period that the controlled welding
section is being inspected, Contractor may continue with production welding but should the results of
Company's inspection of the controlled welding section prove the welding to be unacceptable,
Contractor shall suspend welding operations on notification of same by Company. Contractor shall then
again identify and submit additional corrective measures for Company approval, following which;
Contractor may be allowed to produce another controlled welding section of twenty (20) welds. On
completion of this latter controlled welding section, instructions will be issued by Company regarding
future welding operations. All costs associated with unsatisfactory welding shall be entirely at no
additional compensation to Contractor.
Weld conditions that prevent proper interpretation of radiographic evaluations shall be cause for
rejection of the welds affected, unless they can be inspected by other Company approved methods.
Arcs shall be struck only in the weld groove. Arc strikes on the pipe shall be removed by cutting out a
ring of pipe containing the arc strike or at the discretion of Company shall be repaired as detailed below.
10.11 Repairs


                                              Page 68 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                            OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


10.11.1 General
Oxygen cutting or gouging of weld defects is not permitted. Grinding entirely through the weld thickness
is only permitted if specified in Company approved repair welding procedure specification. Air arc
gouging may be permitted with Company approval.
Remedial work on the cap pass may be completed prior to non-destructive testing, but only with prior
approval from Company, and then only in accordance with the requirements of the approved repair
welding specification.
For pipe grades greater than three hundred and eighty six (386) MPa, all repairs shall be made using a
low hydrogen process; except for through wall repairs where the root pass may be completed using
E6010 electrodes and the second (hot) pass may be welded with E8010 electrodes.
For pipe grades three hundred and eighty-six (386) and less, cellulose electrodes may be used for all
welding passes.
Through thickness weld repairs performed from the outside are limited to twenty five percent (25%) of
pipe circumference. Partial through wall weld repairs may be over the full circumference.
All cut-outs shall be the property of Company and shall be promptly delivered to Company after cut out.
10.11.2 Repair & Removal of Defects
Any weld that does not meet the defect acceptance criteria of CSA Z662 shall be repaired or removed at
Contractor's expense. All repair welding shall be in accordance with the approved repair welding
procedure specification.
The minimum length of any repair shall be fifty (50) millimetres. The minimum preheat established in
the approved welding procedure specification shall be applied prior to removing the defect by grinding.
The minimum preheat temperature shall extend a minimum of one hundred and fifty (150) millimetres
in any direction extending from the repair and shall be maintained throughout the entire preparation
and welding operation.
Grinding grooves for weld repair shall be at least six (6) millimetres wide or one and a half (1.5) times as
wide as its depth, whichever is greater.
Single and multiple passes may be used for repair welding. When multiple passes are used, the start and
stop each repair pass shall not be superimposed over the start and stop of the preceding repair pass.
The start and stop of a repair weld shall be ground smooth to conform to the contour of the original
weld, with a smooth transition to the adjacent base or weld metal.
Weld repairs shall be completed in a full operation without stopping. Weld repairs shall not be started if
prevailing weather conditions or other conditions indicate that full completion of the weld repair may be
interrupted.
Following completion of welding, the entire repair area shall be covered with a cooling blanket so that
the deposit will cool down slowly.
Only a single repair attempt is permitted without Company approval.
10.11.3 Removal of Arc Strikes in Weld Areas



                                              Page 69 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                              OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Arc Strikes are not permitted and are a cut out. In special circumstances, authorization by the Company
for repair of arc strikes may be allowed. An Arc Strike will not be granted until Contractor submits
detailed written repair procedures to Company, and these procedures have been accepted by Company.
As a minimum, repair procedures shall address:
           Method of surface preparation;
           Required surface finish;
           Type and concentration of etchant to be used;
           Safety procedures for handling chemical reagents;
           Method of etchant preparation;
           Etchant application method and application time, which must address the effect of metal
            surface temperature on reaction rate, and the methods of metal heating and temperature
            measurement if required to improve reaction time;
           Periodic testing of the effectiveness of the etchant (i.e., frequency of testing and method of
            testing);
           Equipment and procedures for ultrasonic thickness testing;
           Qualifications of ultrasonic thickness testing personnel; and
           Forms for recording the results of each arc strike evaluation, including space for
            identification of weld number, pipe number containing the arc strike, circumferential
            location of the arc strike, remaining wall thickness after removal of the arc strike, and the
            final result of the evaluation.
The written repair procedure shall be available at the construction location. Company reserves the right
to witness removal of arc strikes, and to perform any other checks or tests necessary to verify complete
removal of arc strikes.
Grinding for the removal of arc strikes shall not reduce the wall thickness of the pipe by more than five
percent (5%) of the nominal wall thickness.
10.11.4 Removal of Cracks in Circumferential Butt Welds
Cracked welds shall be removed from the line. All weld cracks shall be reported to Company for
investigation. Weld rings containing the cracked weld, and a minimum of fifty (50) millimetres either
side of the weld, shall be removed from the pipe and sent to Company for investigation.
Company shall have the opportunity to define markings to be applied on the weld cut out rings prior to
weld crack removal.
10.11.5 Inspection of Repairs
Weld repairs may be inspected using any method Company feels would best determine the acceptability
of the weld. The non-destructive method used to originally identify the defect must be used in the
assessment of acceptability.
10.12 Fabrication Welding
10.12.1 Scope
This specification applies to field and shop fabrication of pipeline assemblies and facilities. This
specification section does not apply to cross country pipeline welding.



                                               Page 70 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                          OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


The welding specifications are based upon but not limited to those of CSA Z662 "Oil and Gas Pipeline
Systems" and the Provincial Acts and Regulations (BC Oil and Gas Activities Act or Alberta Pipeline Act).
This specification is based on CSA Z662, which permits the collective use of ASME SECTION IX for welding
procedure and welder qualifications, and ASME B31.3 for standards of acceptability. When a Fabricator
elects to use ASME SECTION IX welding qualifications, welding qualifications and all welds completed in
accordance with these qualifications, shall be subject to the same additional requirements as detailed in
this specification. Welding qualifications for materials with SMYS greater than three hundred and eighty
six (386) MPa shall include carbon equivalent as an essential change as specified by CSA Z662.
These welding specifications cover the requirements for:
           Pre-Inspection Meetings
           Submittals
           Release Notice
           Witness/Hold Points
           Bevel Preparation
           Equipment
           Materials
           Welding Procedure Qualification
           Welder Qualification
           Welding Consumables
           Production Welding
           Weld Inspection and Acceptance
           Repairs
10.12.2 Definitions Related to Fabrication Welding Specification Requirements
Welding terms and definitions shall be in accordance with CSA Z662 and these welding specifications.
Arc Strikes - Localized areas where an electrical arc has heated an area away from the weld joint bevel
and weld H.A.Z.
Controlled Cooling -A method of preventing accelerated cooling of a weld.
Counterbore and Taper - A method of transitioning unequal pipe wall thicknesses.
Essential Change - A welding change that may affect the mechanical properties or quality of the weld. As
defined in CSA Z662 and this specification.
Fabricator – An organization specializing in the supply and fabrication of piping assemblies or
equipment, either directly for Company or as a subcontractor, and may also mean pipeline Contractor, if
fabrication included in its scope of work.
Fabrication Facility - A temporary or permanent location intended for construction of piping assemblies
or equipment.
Fabrication Welding – Welding of piping and assemblies’ remote from the final location of the welds.




                                              Page 71 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                           OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Hold Point - A mandatory notification point for the Fabricator to notify Company and allow him to
attend prior to proceeding with any further sequences in fabrication. Attendance at this point is
mandatory for Company.
Internal (back weld) repair – Any repair from the internal surface of the original weld. Note that internal
(back weld) repair is not permitted unless Company approved welding procedure qualification of such
welds expressly meets the requirements specified in CSA Z662 or ASME SECTION IX, as appropriate.
Latent Defects - Welding defects that take time to initiate and propagate e.g. hydrogen cold cracks.
Minimum Interpass Temperature - The minimum temperature of the weldment at any time between
weld passes measured at a location fifty (50) millimetres from a production weld joint, or one hundred
and fifty (150) millimetres from the edge of a repair weld.
Maximum Interpass Temperature - The maximum temperature of the weldment between weld passes
measured immediately before the start of any weld pass, at a location 12.7 millimetres from the edge of
the weld.
Minimum Preheat Temperature - The minimum temperature that the pipe and weld area must be
immediately before welding is performed measured at a location fifty (50) millimetres from a production
weld joint, or one hundred and fifty (150) millimetres from the edge of a repair weld.
Maximum Preheat Temperature - The maximum temperature that the pipe and weld area can be heated
to at any location any time before or during welding.
Piping Assembly – A group of pipe or components, or both, joined by one or more circumferential welds.
Procedure Compliance - Compliance to all welding essential variables or changes as defined by these
welding specifications and CSA Z662 and/or ASME SECTION IX.
Procedure Qualification Record - (PQR) Procedure Qualification Records are the actual documented
variables recorded during the qualification welding of test coupons to demonstrate the compatibility of
consumables and techniques in the joining of materials typical for a given application. It also contains
the mechanical test results of the tested specimens.
Weld Repair Rate - The percentage of welds that do not meet a specified weld acceptance criteria. The
Weld Repair Rate is calculated by dividing the total number of welds produced during a given period by
the number of welds that require repair over the same period of time.
SMTS - Specified Minimum Tensile Strength
SMYS - Specified Minimum Yield Strength
Tack Welds – A temporary weld segment designed to hold a weldment in alignment prior to welding.
Witness Point - A mandatory notification point for the Fabricator to notify Company and allow him to
attend prior to proceeding with any further sequences in the fabrication. Attendance at this point will be
left up to the discretion of Company.
Welding Data Sheet (WDS) - A single page summary of the Welding Procedure Specification intended as
quick reference for the welders and inspectors to ensure familiarization of all the essential changes for
welding. It is intended that all welders receive a copy of each data sheet that applies to their particular
application to ensure they are aware of what practices must be followed.


                                              Page 72 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                           OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Welding Procedure Specification - (WPS) The WPS takes the essential changes recorded during the
development of the PQR and extends these into a range of essential changes to be followed for a
specific task. Guidelines are given for the application of the welding i.e. preheats, consumables, heat
inputs.
Welding Procedure - A collection of documents that includes:
           A Welding Procedure Specification (WPS) describing all essential changes required to apply
            the procedure;
           Procedure Qualification Records (PQRs) describing all essential changes actually used during
            the preparation of test welds supporting qualification of a welding procedure; and
           All associated non-destructive and destructive examination results obtained for each test
            weld
           Welding Production - This term extends to all the welding completed in the performance of
            the Work including fabrication welding and repair welding.
10.12.3 Fabrication
The Fabricator shall supply all labour, equipment and materials not specified as being supplied by
Company and shall perform all welding necessary to produce welded assemblies (“Fabricator”) in
accordance with the requirements of the Contract Documents.
All welding shall be in accordance with CSA Z662 and those additional requirements specified herein.
Welding shall be done by one or more of the following processes, either singly or in combination;
SMAW, gas metal arc welding (“GMAW”), flux cored arc welding (“FCAW”) or submerged arc welding
(SAW). The welding technique used shall be a manual, semi-automatic or automatic arc welding process
or combination of processes. Welds may be produced by position welding, roll welding or a combination
of position and roll welding.
The Fabricator shall submit proposed welding procedures to Company for approval before the start of
any production welding. No welding shall be done unless the appropriate approved welding
specification is on site. The requirements of the welding procedure specification are detailed within this
specification. The Fabricator shall submit the proposed welding procedures to Company fifteen (15) days
before the scheduled start of production welding.
Welding procedure specifications and welder qualifications shall be in accordance with the
requirements of CSA Z662, these welding specifications and those of the Provincial Acts and Regulations
(BC Oil and Gas Activities Act or Alberta Pipeline Act).
The Fabricator shall monitor and document welding changes and shall provide this documentation to
Company. The frequency of checking and form of documentation shall be established by the Fabricator
and shall be submitted for approval by Company prior to production welding.
The Fabricator shall ensure that all persons under its direction involved with welding are fully aware of
requirements for welding and all welders and related foremen are in possession of the appropriate
welding data sheets.

Specific objectives for the meeting include identification of potential conflicts between contract
requirements and understanding of fabricator plans regarding specifications, codes, standards,
drawings, fabrication techniques and processes, and examination and testing of assemblies.

10.12.6 Release Notice
Prior to any shipment of welded assemblies, the Fabricator will provide Company with a Release for
Shipping Notice (“RSN”). The RSN will not relieve the Fabricator from responsibility for quality,
workmanship and any other requirements of the contract and associated documents.
10.12.7 Witness/Hold Points
The following points are the witness and hold points in fabrication:
           Witness Point - Any new welder qualification testing;
           Witness Point - Prior to any repairs being performed;
           Hold Point - Any heat treatment;
           Hold Point - Any pressure testing;
           Hold Point - Prior to shipping any loads of completed spools or fabrications to site; and
           Hold Point - Any specification non-compliance.
10.12.8 Weld Classification
For pipe and components NPS 2 and larger, where practical, welded joints shall be made with single or
double groove butt joints.



                                             Page 74 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                              OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


It shall be permissible to use fillet welds in the form of socket welds for piping up to NPS 1.5 only. When
this method is used, gap-o-lets or their equivalent shall be used in accordance with the manufacturer's
recommended practices. Fillet welds shall also be used as reinforcement for branch connection groove
welds. The weld faces being joined shall be at an angle of 90° +/- 3° to each other unless otherwise
specified by Company. Socket welds shall have at least two weld passes and shall be completed using a
low hydrogen welding process. Fillet welds shall be concave to slightly convex.
Welded outlets shall be attached using fillet reinforced groove welds. Low hydrogen welding process
shall be used, except the first weld pass (root) shall be welded using cellulose electrodes. All subsequent
weld passes shall be completed using a low hydrogen welding process. At the discretion of Company,
the second pass (hot pass) may also be welded using cellulose electrodes.
Tack welds shall be done by qualified welders and shall be preheated in accordance with the
requirements of Company approved qualified welding procedure specification to be used for the
completed weld.
Tack Welds
            Shall be made using a low hydrogen welding process;
            Tack welds shall be of sufficient number, size and quality, as to maintain alignment without
             danger of breaking or otherwise compromising safety;
            If a tack weld cracks or breaks, it shall be completely removed and the joint in the area of
             the broken tack shall be restored to its original condition without any addition of weld
             metal;
            Bridge tacks shall be used for piping assemblies NPS 16 and larger. When bridge tack welds
             are used, they shall be completed using a Company approved low hydrogen weld procedure.
             Bridge tacks shall not be incorporated in the final weld. They shall be completely removed
             by grinding prior to filling of the joint. Bridging material shall be low carbon steel generically
             similar to the base metals to be welded;
            Root tacks may be used for piping assemblies’ small than NPS 16. Root tacks shall not be
             incorporated in the final weld. They shall be completely removed by grinding prior to filling
             the joint; and
            Root bead segments deposited using external line up clamps in accordance with a Company
             approved welding procedure, are not considered to be tack welds.
10.12.9 Bevel Preparation
Joint preparation shall require that all piping ends which are to form a part of the welded joint shall be
cleaned to sound metal immediately prior to welding to ensure complete removal of all paint, grease,
oxide, rust and any other extraneous matter. Cleaning shall extend for at least twenty five (25)
millimetres from the piping edges on both internal and external surfaces.
When factory bevels do not conform to the requirements of the welding procedure specification, but
are in accordance with purchase specifications, the Fabricator shall:
            Revise and, if necessary, requalify the procedure specification; or
            Prepare bevels on ends as required by the procedure specification at no additional cost to
             Company.




                                               Page 75 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                             OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


If the nominal wall thickness of the adjoining piping ends do not vary by more than 1.6 millimetres, no
special treatment is necessary, provided that full penetration and fusion is accomplished in welding.
If the nominal wall thickness of the adjoining piping ends vary by more than 1.6 millimetres a taper cut
shall be made on the inside of the thicker pipe. The taper angle shall not be greater than thirty degrees
(30°) nor less than fourteen degrees (14°). Particular attention shall be paid to proper alignment under
these conditions. Internal back welding / tapering shall not be permitted without written permission
from Company.
Fabricator shall prepare bevels using machine tools, or automatic or semi-automatic oxyfuel gas cutting
equipment, so that the finished ends are square within 1.6 millimetres. Free-hand manual oxygen
cutting is not permitted.
Beveled ends shall be smooth and uniform and shall comply with the dimensions and geometry
specified in the qualified and approved welding specifications. Bums, small score marks and other small
imperfections shall be blended out by grinding. No welding repair of bevels shall be permitted.
Piping heat numbers and/or item numbers shall be transferred to both ends of lengths of pipe cut from
any joint of pipe by the Fabricator and shall be recorded on the shop sheets. Identification shall be made
by suitable marking using indelible permanent marking crayons, metal stamping shall not be permitted.
Longitudinal and spiral seam welds in pipe and piping components shall be ground to within 0.4
millimetres of both interior and exterior surfaces, for a minimum distance of 12.7 millimetres from the
bevel edge. The grind area shall merge smoothly with weld reinforcement at the end of the grind, and
shall not be reduced the wall thickness of the pipe or component below the specified thickness.
The use of wedges to correct minor out-of-roundness and hi-low shall be permitted when approved by
Company.
Where possible all seams shall be aligned to ensure that the seam of the pipe does not line up with the
seam of the component.
All branch type attachments shall be located at least fifty (50) millimetres from circumferential or
longitudinal seam welds unless otherwise approved by Company.
Line-up of parts shall be such that the weld axis is within three degrees (3°) of being at right angles to
the longitudinal axis of the piping.
Pipe supports shall be used to minimize stress and sag in the assemblies. The practice of tack welding
supports, bracing bars or counter balance weights onto the fabricated assemblies is not permitted.
Grounding devices shall be securely attached and of sufficient size to avoid overheating and arc strikes
and shall not be welded to the base metals being joined. Ground clamps shall be insulated on all
locations touching the base metals being joined, except for the point of contact intended for transfer of
welding current. Roll welding techniques shall use a swivel- type ground device securely attached to the
piping assembly, unless otherwise approved by Company. Grounding devices shall not be attached to
fittings or valves unless approved by Company.
10.12.10        Equipment
Wire feeders shall protect the wire from the elements such as rain or any source of hydrogen pick-up.



                                               Page 76 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                          OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Welding equipment shall have a calibrated means of displaying welding current, voltage, wire-
feed speed and heat input shall be available either as a part of the welding machine or by suitable
instrumentation for monitoring welding arc essential variables for compliance with the approved
welding procedure.
Arc welding equipment shall be operated within the amperage, voltage, travel speed and heat input
ranges specified in Company approved welding procedure specifications.
Welding and line-up clamps shall be designed to avoid mechanical damage to the piping and to maintain
alignment to within specified dimensions.
Company reserves the right to prohibit the use of equipment, which it deems unsuitable for proper
performance of the Work.
10.12.11        Materials
10.12.11.1      General
This Section 10.12.11 applies to welding of steel base metals conforming to Company specifications to
appropriate material standards listed in CSA Z662, and to any other material designated by Company.
Company supplied large diameter fittings, pipe bends, and pipe may be manufactured under standards
having tolerances that may result in mismatch of weld ends due to variations in diameter, wall thickness
and out of roundness. The amount of mismatch may be sufficient to require back welding. This is not an
abnormal condition, particularly on heavy wall thickness material. No additional compensation will be
provided for additional fit-up time or back welding unless the Fabricator can clearly demonstrate that
the materials supplied are outside the tolerances given in the applicable codes and standards. Note that
internal (back weld) repair is not permitted unless Company approved welding procedure qualification
of such welds expressly meets the qualification requirements specified in CSA Z662 or ASME SECTION IX,
as appropriate.
On receiving materials from Company, as part of the custody transfer, the Fabricator shall be
responsible for ensuring that all materials conform to the bills of material for quantity, quality, and
physical conformance. A record shall be kept of the heat number, pipe number and test pressure for any
high pressure pipe, and the heat number, and/or purchase order numbers plus part number or item
number (i.e. unique identification number) for all pressure piping and components that are NPS 2 and
larger. The record shall be traceable to the actual pipe or components. Any non-conformance shall be
reported to Company for acceptance or rejection of Fabricators proposed disposition.
Any discrepancies or damage discovered after the Fabricator has received and accepted the materials,
including dents, gouges, and arc strikes, will be the responsibility of the Fabricator.
10.12.11.2      Filler Metals
Filler metals shall be certified by the Canadian Welding Bureau as conforming to CSA Standard W48 or
having mechanical properties that meet the requirements of the aforementioned standards.
Filler metals shall be stored and handled so as to avoid damage to them and to the containers in which
they are shipped. Filler metals in opened containers shall be protected from deterioration and those
that show signs of deterioration shall be disposed of. Any portion of a box or container found to be
damaged or damp shall cause rejection of the entire box or container. As well, all welds found to be



                                             Page 77 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                              OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT

welded using suspect electrodes will be cut out and replaced at Fabricator's expense. Storage, exposure
periods and re-conditioning of electrodes shall be in accordance with manufacturer's recommendations.
Low hydrogen shielded metal arc welding electrodes (EXX18), when removed from sealed containers,
shall be immediately transferred to heated ovens maintained at a temperature between a hundred and
twenty degrees (120º) Celsius to one hundred and fifty (150º) Celsius , unless there are specific written
electrode manufacturer recommendations that would indicate otherwise. Low hydrogen SMAW
electrodes that have been exposed to atmospheric conditions for more than 1 hour shall be
reconditioned by rebaking according to written instructions provided by the electrode manufacturer, or
they shall not be used for the work. Maximum number of rebake cycles for any electrode is two.
All fabrication welds including butt welds, fillet welds, repair welds and branch connection welds shall
be made using a low hydrogen process, except that cellulose coated electrodes may be used for:
            The root and hot pass of butt welds;
            The root and hot pass of through-wall weld repairs;
            All passes of butt welds joining pipe to pipe; and
            All passes of pipe to component, and component to component welds where:
            Base metals are plain carbon ASME P No. 1 steels with SMYS less than three hundred and
             eighty six (386) MPa ;
            Electrode SMTS is less than or equal to 480 MPa; and
            System pressure rating is PN 50 (ANSI Class 300) or lower.
When cellulose coated electrodes are used for the root pass of SMAW welding procedures, they shall be
of the E6010 or E7010-P1 classification, and the minimum heat input for the root pass shall be 0.6
kJ/mm.
Company reserves the right to prohibit the use of materials that it deems unsuitable for proper
performance of the Work.
All other welding procedure qualifications, other than those qualified in accordance with ASME SECTION
IX shall be limited by the essential changes given in CSA Z662 Table 7.2 and this specification.
10.12.12         Shielding Gases
Shielding gases shall be approved by Company.
If carbon dioxide is used as a shielding gas it shall have a purity of at least ninety nine and a half percent
(99.5%) and shall have a dew point of negative thirty four degrees (-34°) Celsius or lower.
Shielding gases shall be kept in the containers in which they are supplied and shall be stored adequately
to prevent exposure to extremes of temperature. Gases shall not be intermixed in their containers and
those that have questionable quality or are in containers that show damage shall not be used.
Gas flow regulators for the appropriate shielding gas shall be used and shall be kept in good working
condition such that the correct shielding gas flow rate is as required by the approved welding procedure
specification.

10.12.13.1       General

Weld procedures are required for fabrication welding, as applicable to the scope of work of Fabricator.
For weld procedure qualification purposes, welding operations have been classified as follows:
       site and shop fabrication welding, and
       site and shop fabrication repair welding
Fabricator shall submit all welding procedures for approval in writing by Company prior to use for
production, repair, or back welding. Fabricator may submit previously qualified welding procedures that
are suitable for the work.
Each weld procedure submission shall include a meaningful description of the intended scope of work
applicable to the procedure. For a Project work scope requiring multiple procedures, with each
submission, the Fabricator shall include an updated weld matrix listing all procedures to be used on the
work, the Project specific base metals and applications intended for use with each procedure, and the
approval status of each procedure.
For material with SMYS greater than three hundred and eighty-six (386) MPa, the heat number of the
materials used for procedure qualification shall be recorded and Material Test Reports shall be attached.
Company approval of welding procedures shall be based on qualification in accordance with this
specification, and the requirements of governing codes and standards applicable to the work.
Prior to the start of work, welding procedures shall be developed, qualified, documented and submitted
by Fabricator for each welding operation within the scope of work of Fabricator. Welding procedures
shall cover the entire range of materials and welding variables within Fabricator scope of work. This may
necessitate the preparation and testing of several qualification test coupons.
Fabricator shall simulate production welding as closely as practical during the qualification of Welding
Procedure Specifications that shall include pipe fit-up, clamping and the effects of ambient conditions
and pipe stresses.
In addition to the requirements for essential changes for qualification of welding procedure
specifications detailed in CSA Z662 Table 7.3 or ASME SECTION IX as applicable, the following variables
shall be used for qualification welds.
10.12.13.2      Composition of Welding Consumables
A change of the manufacturer of consumables used for qualification welds shall not be permitted
without written consent from Company.

to production welding.
10.12.13.5      Fabrication Weld Procedure Qualification
Welding processes used for fabrication welding are restricted to SMAW, GMAW, FCAW, and SAW.
Fabrication welding procedures shall be qualified according to this specification and:
        CSA Z662, or
        ASME IX with CSA Z662 compliance.
Fabrication weld procedure qualification tests shall include full radiographic examination, impact testing
of weld material and HAZ's and cross-section hardness surveys for each procedure qualification test.
10.12.13.6      Fabrication Repair Weld Procedure Qualification
If the Fabricator proposes a fabrication repair weld procedure, which is different from that qualified by
the Fabricator for use on fabrication welds, Fabricator shall qualify the proposed fabrication repair weld
procedure in the same manner as, shown for fabrication weld procedures.
Minimum preheat and interpass temperature for fabrication repair weld procedures shall be one
hundred and twenty degrees (120°) Celsius.
10.12.13.7      Non-Destructive Testing of Weld Procedure Qualification Test Coupons
Immediately after welding, each weld procedure qualification test coupon shall be visually examined
and fully radiographed. Acceptance criteria shall be as stated in CSA Z662. Note that welding procedures
qualified in accordance with the requirements of ASME IX shall use acceptance criteria as stated in
ASME B31.3.
10.12.13.8      Destructive Testing of Weld Procedure Qualification Test Coupons
Following successful completion of non-destructive examinations, weld procedure test coupons shall be
destructively tested according to the requirements of CSA Z662, and the following requirements.
        The facility chosen by the Fabricator for mechanical testing shall be approved by Company.

PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                            OCTOBER 4TH 2015

       If the procedure is approved, Fabricator shall have an appropriately qualified individual prepare
        a Welding Data Sheet and provide it to Company. Company will approve the format and use of
        the data sheet in writing.
       Fabricator shall be responsible for the performance and quality of all welding, in accordance
        with the welding procedures approved for use. Fabricator shall signify its acceptance of this
        responsibility by signing the Welding Data Sheet.
       Copies of the applicable approved welding procedures shall be on-site during production
        welding. All production welding shall be in accordance with the approved procedures. Deviation
        from the procedures shall require the welding operation to be discontinued and welding
        resumed after resolving the reasons for the deviation or the welding procedure shall be re-
        qualified with approval of Company.
Each Procedure Qualification Record on material with specified thickness over six (6) millimetres shall
include testing of at least three weld metal and three heat affected zone Charpy impact specimens
removed from each procedure qualification test coupon. Weld metal specimens shall be notched on the
centerline of the weld and normal to the surface. Heat affected zone specimens shall be etched and
notched so that the root of the notch is located in as much of the heat affected zone as practical, and
normal to the surface. When full size specimens cannot be obtained, the largest obtainable
standard sub-size specimen shall be used.
Impact tests shall be conducted in accordance with ASTM E23 at or below the minimum design
temperature for the components to be welded. Typically the minimum design temperature will be:
       Negative five degrees (-5°) Celsius for below ground and indoor piping assemblies; and
       Negative forty five degree (-45°) Celsius for above ground and outdoor piping assemblies.

Absorbed energy shall be reported for each specimen, and shear area or lateral expansion should be
reported. The absorbed energy of weld metal and heat affected zones for pressure containing parts NPS
20 and larger shall be the same as required for the base metals to be joined during production welding,
or as otherwise specified by Company.
Percent shear and lateral expansion for each specimen should be reported.
For pressure containing parts less than NPS 20, the absorbed energy of weld metal and heat affected
zones shall meet or exceed the requirements specified in the applicable governing industry standards
for the pressure containing part.
Required absorbed energy for sub-size specimens shall be determined by multiplying the required
energy for full size specimens by the sub size specimen thickness, and dividing the result by the full-
size specimen thickness of ten (10) millimetres.
Each Procedure Qualification Record shall include at least one Vickers hardness survey on a cross section
of the qualification weld. The hardness survey shall be conducted in accordance with ASTM E92 or E384,
using a load in the range of one (1) to ten (10) kilograms or two hundred and fifty (250) to one thousand
(1000) grams, respectively.
The hardness survey shall include at least two ROWs of readings across the weld metal, both coarse
grained heat affected zones, and the parent metal on each side of the weld, within two (2) millimetres
of each surface. HAZ indentations shall be placed in the hardest appearing structures, such as those
