located adjacent to the toe of the cap or root pass, even if these structures do not coincide precisely
with the line of survey.
Maximum hardness shall be three hundred and twenty five (325) HV, except that isolated readings up to
three hundred and fifty (350) HV may be accepted provided that two additional tests in the same area
are three hundred and twenty five (325) HV or less.
10.12.14        Welder Qualification
10.12.14.1      General
Fabricator shall use only skilled and qualified welders. Welders shall qualify by demonstrating their
ability to produce acceptable welds in accordance with Company approved welding procedure
specifications for the particular welding configuration or application to be used in production welding.
No welder shall carry out any phase or type of welding for which he has not been tested and accepted
by Company as qualified.
10.12.14.2      Test Requirements
All welder qualification test costs shall be borne by Fabricator. Pipe material used for welder
qualification testing may be provided by Company.
Welders that will qualify using welding procedures qualified in accordance with ASME SECTION IX, as
permitted by CSA Z662, shall be qualified in accordance with the requirements of ASME SECTION IX. The
qualification ranges for these qualifications shall be in accordance with ASME SECTION IX.
Before starting qualification tests, welders shall be given training sufficient to allow them to obtain
adequate skills to produce acceptable welds on a consistent basis.
Welders performing repairs shall be qualified in accordance with the approved full through wall repair
welding procedure. This test shall qualify them for partial through wall repairs and back-weld repairs.
The repair-welding test shall consist of simulating two full-through-wall repair welds on a previously
completed test weld, with the pipe in the horizontal - fixed position. Two sections, one located
approximately at the 12 – 2 o’clock position and one located approximately at the 4 – 6 o’clock position,
shall have the weld metal removed by grinding to a depth that permits re-welding of the root pass. The
width of the repair section shall be that of the original groove. Each section ground out shall be
subsequently repaired from the root pass through to the cap pass using an approved welding procedure.
The length of each repair segment shall be a minimum of one hundred and fifty (150) millimetres.
Test welds shall be produced in accordance with Company approved welding procedure specifications,
by each welder, and shall be visually inspected and radiographed or ultrasonically inspected using
techniques similar to those to be used for inspection of production welding. Acceptance criteria shall be
as stated in CSA Z662 except for welders that qualify in accordance with the requirements of ASME IX.
Such welder qualification tests shall meet the acceptance criteria specified in ASME B31.3. All test welds
shall be witnessed by Company and failure to comply with the welding procedure specifications shall be
cause for rejection.
Fabricator shall prepare and maintain a list of welders and their qualifications, which shall be updated
after any change of welding personnel and submitted to Company.



                                              Page 83 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                            OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Each welder shall be assigned a unique number or letter(s) to identify their welding. No other welder
shall receive the same identification and if a welder is terminated or leaves the Project the identification
shall not be reassigned. Fabricator shall provide a list of qualified welders with corresponding numbers
to Company.
If, in the opinion of Company, failure of a welder to pass a test was because of unavoidable conditions or
conditions beyond his control, such a welder may be given a second opportunity to qualify. No further
tests shall be given.
A welder may be required to re-qualify at any time if there is any reasonable doubt about the ability to
produce acceptable welds.
Fabricator shall notify Company twenty four (24) hours in advance of carrying out welder qualification
tests to allow Company to witness the welding.
10.12.15        Welding Consumables
The maximum SMAW electrode diameter shall be four (4) millimetres for the root pass, and 4.8
millimetres for all other passes.
Internal back welding repair welds shall be completed with E8018-C3 or suitable FCAW or GMAW
consumables.
The specified tensile strength of filler metals and fluxes shall not exceed 550 MPa.
For the FCAW, GMAW and SAW processes, production welds shall be completed using the same brand
name and AWS/ASME filler metal and flux classifications as used during procedure qualification. If
changes to filler metal or flux brand name or AWS/ASME classification are necessary, complete
requalification of the welding procedure with the new filler metal and/or flux is required. For the SMAW
process, Company shall be informed of any changes of electrode brand name from that used for
procedure qualifications. Company reserves the right to require requalification of an SMAW welding
procedure based on electrode brand name change. Only neutral fluxes are permitted for SAW welding
unless approved by Company.
10.12.16        Fabrication Production Welding
10.12.16.1      General
The welding of piping shall be performed using qualified welders in accordance with Company approved
qualified welding procedure specifications. Production welding shall not be performed when conditions
encountered exceed the limits stated in the procedure specification.
Fabricator shall continuously monitor welding to ensure compliance with the welding requirements.
Documentation of compliance verifications shall be made and shall be submitted to Company. The
frequency of checking and form of documentation shall be established by the Fabricator and shall be
submitted for approval by Company prior to production welding.
Under no circumstances shall the minimum temperature be below the preheat temperature until the
completion of the second pass. Reheating is permitted prior to the start of the fill/cap pass.
When welding externally coated pipe, the Fabricator, shall place a sheet of non-flammable material with
a minimum width of six hundred (600) millimetres on each side of the weld in order to prevent weld



                                              Page 84 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                            OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


spatter from damaging the coating. Fabricator shall be responsible for correction of damage to coating
caused by welding or cutting bands.
Internal back welding shall not be permitted unless Company approved welding procedure qualification
of such welds expressly meets the requirements specified in CSA Z662 or ASME SECTION IX, as
appropriate.
Company reserves the right to complete post welding inspections up to twenty four (24) hours after
welding if in the opinion of Company the welds may be susceptible to cracking.
10.12.16.2      Preparation of Pipe
Preparation of pipe shall require. that all piping ends which are to form a part of the welded joint shall
be cleaned to sound metal immediately prior to welding to ensure complete removal of all paint, grease,
oxide, rust and any other extraneous matter. Cleaning shall extend for at least twenty five (25)
millimetres from the piping edges on both internal and external surfaces.
Beveled ends shall be smooth and uniform and shall comply with the dimensions and geometry
specified in the qualified and approved welding procedure specifications. Small score marks,
indentations or other small defects within the joint preparation area shall, at the discretion of Company
or inspector, be blended out by grinding, otherwise the bevel shall be re- prepared. No welding repair of
bevels shall be permitted.
Preparation for welding of pipes of different wall thickness shall be in accordance with this Specification,
Appendix B-1 - Drawings, and CSA Z662.
When pups are required, minimum pup length shall be:
       One hundred (100) millimetres for pipe under NPS 12;
       Three hundred (300) millimetres for pipe over NPS 12 but less than or equal to NPS 24; and
       One half (0.5) times the outside diameter for pipe greater than NPS 24.
Manufacturer's pipe joint numbers, pup length and heat numbers shall be transferred to each length of
pipe cut from any joint of pipe. Identification shall be made by suitable marking using indelible
permanent marking crayons.
10.12.16.3      Alignment & Fit-Up
For pipe of the same wall thickness, the maximum allowable offset shall be 1.6 mm, except that any
greater offset, provided that it is caused by dimensional variations of the pipe end, shall be permissible,
provided that it is distributed around the circumference of the pipe in a uniform manner.
Bolt holes on flanges shall straddle established centerlines and shall match the orientation of flanges
connections on matching connections.
Final dimensions of completed assemblies shall match Fabricators spool drawings.
10.12.16.4      Valves with Butt Welding Ends
Valves with butt welding ends shall be welded to pups (or other specified components) according to
instructions obtained from the valve manufacturer. Before the start of any welding of valve ends, the
Fabricator shall provide for approval by Company, a written fabrication, welding, cleaning and testing
procedure that includes descriptions of all equipment used and precautions to prevent damage to


                                              Page 85 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                           OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


sealing elements. Each procedure shall provide for proper control and monitoring of preheat
temperature, interpass temperature, and heat input for each weld pass. As a minimum, a dam of clean
non- flammable material shall be securely placed in both ends of the valve bore in a manner that
protects seals, seats, body cavity and operating elements from weld spatter, slag, heat, and other debris.
Unless otherwise approved by Company, valves NPS 16 and larger shall be butt welded to pups by roll
welding with an automatic (machine) welding process. Stem extensions shall not be removed, so roll
welding may require that the Fabricator provide special equipment or facilities to turn the valves. Valves
less than NPS 16 may be roll or position welded using manual or semi-automatic welding methods, but
roll welding with an automatic welding process is preferred.
When preheat is required, it shall be applied from the outside only. During valve preheating and welding
operations, the temperature of the valve bore at a distance from the weld end equal to six (6) times
thickness of matching pups, shall not exceed one hundred and seventy five degrees (175°) Celsius, or
such lower critical distance or temperature as may be specified by the valve manufacturer. The actual
maximum temperature at this location and adjacent to the seal shall be measured and recorded by the
Fabricator for each weld pass, to ensure that it does not exceed the preceding maximum temperature
limits. This documentation shall be provided to Company.
10.12.16.5      Preheating
Preheating shall be performed using Company approved methods as specified on the approved welding
procedure specifications.
The minimum preheat temperature shall extend around the entire circumference of the pipe and at
least fifty (50) millimetres on each side of the weld joint.
During completion of the weld, the joint shall be maintained at a temperature between the minimum
and maximum interpass temperatures and shall be checked using temperature indicating crayons or
other suitable method immediately prior to, and during the full welding operation. No welding shall take
place unless the minimum interpass temperature is maintained. The heating of local areas (hot spots)
above the upper limit of preheating, as identified on the stamped and approved Welding Procedures, is
not permitted.
Preheat and interpass temperatures shall be restricted to the weld zone to ensure that valve seats are
not damaged.
Preheating of valves shall be applied on the outside surface of the valve. Heating from the inside shall
not be permitted.
Fabricator shall ensure that the pipe coating is not damaged by the application of preheat. Care should
be taken to prevent overheating, and no part of the area shall be heated in excess of two hundred
degrees (200°) Celsius.
Fabricator shall take precautions to avoid accelerated cooling of the weld. If required, insulating
blankets or other appropriate methods may be used to control the weld cooling rate until it has reached
ambient temperature.
10.12.16.6      Welding Sequence




                                              Page 86 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                           OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Root bead welding shall only commence after ensuring that the parts to be joined are adequately
secured against movement. Except for roll welding, movement of the parts to be joined shall not be
permitted until the entire completion of the root pass.
The second pass shall start as soon as possible after the root pass and in any case within the specified
time period stated on Company’s approved welding procedure specification.
Weld passes shall not commence before the preceding pass has been completed. Weld sequencing shall
be such that consecutive start stop locations are staggered a minimum of fifty (50) millimetres.
Clusters of surface porosity, bead starts, heavy glass deposits and high points shall be removed by
grinding prior to depositing weld metal over them. Cleaning shall be done by power or hand tools or
both to the satisfaction of Company.
The completed weld shall have a uniform cross section around the entire circumference of the pipe. At
no point shall the top of the cap pass be below the surface of the pipe or above the pipe surface by
more than 3.5 millimetres.
The completed surface of the weld shall be thoroughly power brushed clean of all spatter and the
reinforcement shall blend smoothly with the adjacent pipe surface. The top cap button shall be ground
to blend smoothly into the remaining weld pass and shall not be permitted to exceed the 3.5 millimetres
maximum stated above.
Whenever practical, welds shall be completed on the day they are started. Production shall be arranged
to minimize the number of incomplete welds left at the end of each workday. When incomplete welds
must be left at the end of a workday, they shall have sufficient deposited weld metal as to preclude the
formation of cracks. As a minimum, the amount of deposited weld metal in incomplete joints shall not
be less than:
       Three (3) weld passes for weld throats less than or equal to 15.8 millimetres; and
       Four (4) weld passes for weld throats greater than 15.8 millimetres.
Partially completed cap passes shall be completed before the end of each day.
Each welder shall identify his work by marking the pipe adjacent to the weld with his unique
identification number or letter using an indelible permanent marking crayon.
10.12.17        Weld Inspection & Acceptance
10.12.17.1      Right to Inspect
Company shall have the right to inspect and monitor all aspects of production welding to ensure that
the welding procedures are being adhered to, and shall have the right to reject any welds in which the
details of the welding procedure are not adhered to.
Welds that do not comply with the Standards of Acceptability as set forth herein shall be removed or
repaired at Company's discretion. Repairs will not be permitted if the defective segment has been
repaired previously.
10.12.17.2      Methods of Inspection
All welds shall be inspected for one hundred percent (100%) of their circumference using radiographic
and/or ultrasonic techniques except fillet welds, which shall be inspected using a magnetic particle


                                              Page 87 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                           OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


method, using a wet fluorescent or black and white colour contrast indicating medium. Defect
acceptance criteria shall be based upon the defect acceptance criteria outlined in CSA Z662 "Standards
of Acceptability" for welds completed using procedures qualified in accordance with the requirements
of CSA Z662. Welds produced using procedures qualified in accordance with the requirements of ASME
IX shall be sentenced according to the weld acceptance criteria specified in ASME B31.3.
Weld conditions that prevent proper interpretation of evaluations shall be cause for rejection of the
welds affected, unless they can be inspected by other Company approved methods.
Arcs shall be struck only in the weld groove. Arc strikes on the pipe shall be removed by cutting out a
ring of pipe containing the arc strike or at the discretion of Company shall be repaired as detailed below.
10.12.18        Repairs
10.12.18.1      General
Grinding entirely through the weld thickness is only permitted if specified in Company approved repair
welding procedure specification.
Remedial work on the cap pass may be completed prior to non-destructive testing, but only with prior
approval from Company, and then only in accordance with the requirements of the approved repair
welding specification.
All repairs shall be made using a low hydrogen process; except for through wall repairs where the root
pass may be completed using E6010 electrodes and the second (hot) pass may be welded with cellulose
electrodes. Low hydrogen welding processes shall be used for all back welding, i.e. root repairs.
Through thickness weld repairs performed from the outside are limited to twenty five (25%) of pipe
circumference. Partial through wall weld repairs or weld repairs performed by back welding may be over
the full circumference. All cut-outs shall be the property of Company.
10.12.18.2      Repair & Removal of Defects
Any weld, which does not meet the defect acceptance criteria of CSA Z662 or ASME B31.3 as applicable,
shall be repaired or removed at Fabricator's expense. All repair welding shall be in accordance with the
approved repair welding procedure specification.
Defects other than cracks shall be completely removed by grinding. For material over 12.7 milimetres in
thickness, defect removal by other means may be permitted subject to submission of a detailed written
procedure and Company’s approval of the procedure prior to any excavation.
The minimum length of any repair shall be fifty (50) millimetre. The minimum preheat established in the
approved welding procedure specification shall be applied prior to removing the defect by grinding or
other approved methods. The minimum preheat temperature shall extend a minimum of 150
millimetres in any direction extending from the repair and shall be maintained throughout the entire
preparation and welding operation.
Grinding grooves for weld repair should be at least six (6) millimetres wide or one and half (1.5) times as
wide as its depth, whichever is greater.
Single and multiple passes may be used for repair welding. When multiple passes are used, the start and
stop each repair pass shall not be superimposed over the start and stop of the preceding repair pass.



                                              Page 88 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                           OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


The start and stop of a repair weld shall be ground smooth to conform to the contour of the original
weld, with a smooth transition to the adjacent base or weld metal.
Weld repairs shall be completed in a full operation without stopping. Weld repairs shall not be started if
conditions indicate that full completion of the weld repair may be interrupted.
Where practical, backwelding (internal welding) shall be used for repair welding of root bead defects.
Backwelding shall only be done in strict accordance with the Fabricator’s safety procedures.
Backwelding repair procedures for the root bead shall include:
       Removal of the defect by grinding, the grinding groove should be at least as wide as the weld
        deposit of the root bead applied.
       Re-welding of the grooved area using low hydrogen filler metal. (e.g., 2.4 millimetres or 3.2
        millimetres E8018 electrodes)
Remedial work necessary to the cap or root pass may be carried out prior to further non- destructive
testing, but only if approved by Company and then only in accordance with Company approved repair
welding procedure specification. Only a single repair attempt is permitted without Company approval.
10.12.18.3       Removal of Arc Strikes in Weld Areas
Authorization for repair of arc strikes will not be granted until the Fabricator submits detailed written
repair procedures to Company, and these procedures have been thoroughly reviewed and accepted by
Company. As a minimum, repair procedures shall address:
            Method of surface preparation;
            Required surface finish;
            Type and concentration of etchant to be used;
            Safety procedures for handling chemical reagents;
            Method of etchant preparation;
            Etchant application method and application time, which must address the effect of metal
             surface temperature on reaction rate, and the methods of metal heating and temperature
             measurement if required to improve reaction time;
            Periodic testing of the effectiveness of the etchant (i.e., frequency of testing and method of
             testing);
            Equipment and procedures for ultrasonic thickness testing;
            Qualifications of ultrasonic thickness testing personnel; and
            Forms for recording the results of each arc strike evaluation, including space for
             identification of weld number, pipe number containing the arc strike, circumferential
             location of the arc strike, remaining wall thickness after removal of the arc strike, and the
             final result of the evaluation.
The written repair procedure shall be available at the construction location. Company reserves the right
to witness removal of arc strikes, and to perform any other checks or tests necessary to verify complete
removal of arc strikes.
Grinding for the removal of arc strikes shall not reduce the wall thickness of the pipe by more than 5% of
the specified wall thickness.
10.12.18.4       Removal of Cracks in Circumferential Butt Welds


                                              Page 89 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                             OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT

Cracked welds shall be removed from the line. All weld cracks shall be reported to Company for
investigation. Documentation of all cracking shall be in format provided by Company.
10.12.18.5      Inspection of Repairs
Weld repairs may be inspected using any method Company feels would best determine the acceptability
of the weld. The non-destructive method used to originally identify the defect must be used in the
assessment of acceptability.
10.12.18.6      Loading & Transportation
The Fabricator shall be responsible for ensuring that all work and material is properly:
            Prepared and loaded for shipment, with all openings adequately sealed to prevent ingress of
             dirt, dust or other contaminants;
            Identified for field installation;
            Secured against movement using non-damaging materials and devices;
            Released by Company for shipment; and
            Transported in a safe and secure manner that avoids any surface damage or structural
             degradation.
All plug and ball valves shall be stored and shipped in the fully open position and all gate valves shall be
stored and shipped in the fully closed position.
Prior to shipment of piping assemblies, at a clearly visible location on the spool the Fabricator shall show
using an indelible marker and lettering at least fifty (50) millimetres:
            Tie-in Piping Heat Numbers
            Tie-in Piping Pipe Numbers
            Spool Number
            Any other Company required identification
10.12.19        QC Turnover Package
The Fabricator shall prepare a complete turnover package of Quality Control information. The package
shall include all material test reports for pressure containing materials, radiographs, NDE reports,
pressure test reports, as-built drawings, and such other drawings as may be necessary to demonstrate
required material traceability. The package shall be provided to Company within two weeks of
completion of the work, or at such other time as may be mutually agreed with Company.
A complete set of radiographs and reports shall be shipped along with appropriate as built drawings to
Company.
The Fabricator shall provide a system for assigning a unique weld number to each completed weld, and
for tracing the identity of base metals to mill test certificates, welding procedures, welders or welding
operators, NDE results, and pressure test results of the spool or system. The system shall be acceptable
and approved by Company.
For Company supplied materials, traceability shall extend to include pipe numbers and heat numbers of
supplied pipe and component tag numbers of supplied components.

11.0 Coating
11.1 General
All field coating and coating repairs on line pipe shall be done in accordance with this Specification, and
all coating applicators shall be competent, adequately trained, and have attended a presentation by the
manufacturer's representative on the application procedures for that coating.
Contractor's cost for supplying weld joint coating products, coating weld joints and repair of Contractor
damaged coating in accordance with Schedule A - Scope of Work, and shall be included in the Base Lay
Price.
11.2 Materials
Company will provide Contractor with pre-coated pipe in accordance with Schedule A - Scope of Work
and Appendix A-3 Company Supplied Materials. Abrasion coated pipe will be provided for bored
crossings and Directional Drills as indicated on the Contract Documents and summarized in Appendix A-
3 - Company Supplied Materials.
Pipe supplied by Company for fabricated assemblies will be provided uncoated and shall be coated in
accordance with this Specification
At time of Bid, Contractor shall inform Company of the weld joint coating product it chooses to use.
Acceptable products are referenced in Schedule A – Scope of Work.
Prior to starting coating activities Contractor shall identify for Company's approval the method of
disposal for empty coating containers and surplus waste coating materials. The disposal of empty
coating containers and surplus waste coating materials shall be conducted in accordance with the
acceptable environmental standards of the Authorities Having Jurisdiction.
All coating materials shall be stored in accordance with the manufacturer's specifications.
11.3 Field Coating




                                              Page 91 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                            OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Contractor shall coat all field weld joints and shall repair all damage, bare spots and holidays so that the
pipeline is installed with a continuous defect free external coating. Contractor shall perform a final
electronic holiday inspection on the finished coating and repair all defects in accordance with Section
11.4 of this Attachment B-2.4 – Construction Specifications.
All field welds shall be field-coated with Company approved coating material in accordance with
Schedule A - Scope of Work. Such coating shall be done after acceptable radiographic inspection of
welds. Refer to ESS 5.82.
Contractor shall not apply weld joint coating on welds within a pipeline section that still contains
unrepaired or non assessed weld repairs. Contractor shall, unless otherwise approved by Company,
remain a distance of one pipe section behind weld repairs with the application of weld joint coating.
Contractor shall ensure that overspray or other coating material not be deposited on the ground. This
shall be accomplished by using tarps or spatter boards under each weld joint during the coating
operation.
Each weld joint coating shall be tested with a holiday detector supplied by Contractor and approved by
Company in accordance with Section 11.4 of this Attachment B-2.4 – Construction Specifications.
11.4 Holiday Inspection & Repair
Holiday detectors approved by Company shall be supplied by Contractor and during the lowering-
in operation Contractor shall, in the presence of Company, inspect all coated pipe.
Prior to commencement of holiday detection, Contractor shall submit to Company for approval:
           Type and make of holiday detector;
           Type and make of calibrating volt meter; and
           Grounding techniques for detector and pipe.
The volt meter supplied by Contractor shall have a range such that the required voltage setting of the
holiday detector shall result in a gauge deflection of between twenty percent (20%) and ninety percent
(90%) of the volt meter range or in accordance with the coating manufacturer’s specification.
Holiday detectors shall be calibrated at the start of the working day and every four hours thereafter
unless otherwise specified by Company. Calibration shall be done in accordance with a procedure
approved by Company. The voltage applied by the holiday detector shall be direct current. The actual
operating voltage shall be established by Company on the basis of the calibration results. Any holiday
detector identified as defective shall be removed and replaced immediately.
The search electrode will be a rolling steel spring and the rod/spring connection will be within the upper
quadrant of the pipe 10 o’clock to 2 o’clock. The rate of travel of the holiday detector shall not exceed
0.75 metres per second and the holiday detector shall not remain stationary on the pipe while
energized.
Contractor shall remove ice and or other debris prior to conducting holiday testing per Company
approved Contractor procedure. Holidays and defects detected shall be repaired and retested in
accordance with this Attachment B-2.4 – Construction Specifications.




                                              Page 92 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                          OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Prior to the installation of bolt on weights or continuous coat concrete Contractor shall ensure that a
holiday detection survey is completed on the section to be weighted and all necessary coating repairs
are completed.
12.0 Lowering-in
All coated pipe shall be subject to a visual inspection and checked with a holiday detector immediately
prior to lower-in (behind last cradle tractor) to ensure that the coating is undamaged, and if found
damaged shall be repaired in accordance with this Attachment B-2.4 – Construction Specifications. The
ground cable shall be attached to a lowering in boom when possible for optimum grounding, rather than
just trailing on the ground.
Contractor shall check the trench each morning for wildlife prior to commencing lowering in operations.
Wildlife found in the trench shall be reported to Company and a method of their removed shall be
agreed upon.
All brush, skids, pipe, metal of any kind, rocks, large clods, sticks, and other hard objects shall be
removed from the trench into which the pipeline is to be lowered, so that the protective coating shall
not be damaged.
Pipe shall not be lowered into the trench until it has been inspected and holiday tested approved by
Company for lowering-in and pipe installation operations shall proceed only when an Inspector is
present and in daylight hours only. Should a section of pipe be lowered-in without Company approval,
the section of pipe shall be removed and re-inspected by Contractor in presence of Company at no
additional compensation to Contractor.
Contractor shall ensure that material clammed from the trench is not placed in a location that will allow
it to mix with topsoil piles. As approved by Company, additional stripping may be required to allow
placement of this material on subsoil.
Water shall be pumped from the trench prior to the pipe being lowered-in, except at open-cut crossings
through flowing water, unless otherwise approved by Company at specific locations. Water shall not be
pumped off the ROW without permission of the Land Owner or tenant. Water shall not be pumped
directly into any watercourses, and water pumped adjacent to a watercourse shall be filtered (filter
cloth or Company approved alternative). Care shall be taken to prevent erosion and flooding of crops.
Pre-coated pipe shall be lowered-in with a technique that will not cause damage to the coating, using
wide belts or rubber tired-neoprene lined cradles as approved by Company. These shall be kept free of
sand, mud, stones or any foreign objects. During shutdown periods, the cradles shall be separated from
the coated pipe by use of rubber sheaths or padded wooden skids. The coated pipe shall be lifted and
not dragged off the support skid.
Contractor shall use sufficient and proper equipment during the installation of the pipeline into the
trench to allow proportionate distribution of the total weight of pipe to prevent undue stress ,or strain
on the pipe and to prevent damage to the pipe coating. The pipe when in the trench shall have a
continuous bearing on the bottom of the trench with sufficient slack to the satisfaction of Company. The
pipe shall not be dropped or subjected to jarring or sudden impacts. Lowering in methods shall be used
that are satisfactory to Company.




                                             Page 93 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                           OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Once lowering in commences on a pipe section, the full pipeline section shall be installed in the trench
prior to shutting down for the day. Pipe sections shall not be left overnight or while operators are not at
the controls of equipment holding suspended pipe.
 Should a section of the pipeline fall from the skids, Contractor shall immediately report the same to
Company. Company reserves the right to perform any tests or inspections deemed necessary to verify
that no serious defects have occurred to the pipe, or in any girth weld. Such tests and any remedial work
required shall be at the expense of Contractor.
Contractor shall provide sufficient time between lower-in and backfill operations to allow Company's
survey crews to conduct an as-built survey of the lowered-in pipe.
In rock ditch and wherever the bottom of the trench contains projecting rocks or other hard objects
which might damage the pipe or coating in the opinion of Company, the bottom of the trench shall be
bedded with a minimum of one hundred and fifty (150) millimetres of earth or select material or other
methods as approved by Company, in accordance with Section 13.0 of this Attachment B-2.4 –
Construction Specifications.
If Contractor elects to use foam pillows or other intermediate supports as approved by Company to
support the pipe above the bottom of the trench prior to bedding material being placed these supports
shall be constructed and spaced in accordance with the drawings. Company may require changes to the
spacing of these intermediate supports contingent on a trial section of pipe being lowered in and
minimum clearance checks between the bottom of pipe and the trench bottom being confirmed.
In the event that damage to the protective coating occurs after the pipe has been lowered into the
trench the pipe shall be raised from the trench and all damaged coating shall be repaired in accordance
with this Attachment B-2.4 – Construction Specifications.
Depth of cover over the lowered-in pipeline shall be maintained as described in Schedule B –
Specifications and Drawings.
13.0 Pipe & Coating Protection
13.1 General
When lowering in the pipe or backfilling is not achievable due to the coarseness of the spoil or the
condition of the trench bottom and as requested by Company, Contractor shall protect the pipe and
pipe coating in accordance with one of the methods noted in this Article 13.
The method of pipe protection to be used will be contingent on trench conditions, ROW access, traffic
control concerns and cost. Company will determine which method is best suited for the area.
Company will provide Contractor with a pipe protection “punch list” which will be a preliminary
assessment of pipe protection requirements to allow Contractor to organize his pipe protection and
backfill resources. This punch list will be preliminary only and the actual pipe protection requirements
will be determined and finalized in the field by Company.
13.2 Bedding & Padding
13.2.1 Bedding




                                              Page 94 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                           OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Where requested by Company, the bottom of the trench shall be bedded. Bedding shall be done to a
smooth and even finish with a minimum thickness of one hundred and fifty (150) millimetres of well
graded non angular mineral material with a maximum particle size of forty (40) millimetres, between the
bottom of pipe and the closest point to the trench bottom.
Contractor may elect to use foam pillows or other intermediate supports as approved by Company to
support the pipe above the bottom of the trench prior to bedding material being placed. Company may
request additional supports (sand or other material approved by Company) between the foam pillows to
adequately support the pipe at pressure points. Support plugs and pillows shall be at least 0.8 metres in
width and provide even support across the lower quadrant of the pipe, and shall maintain a finished
clearance of 0.15 metres minimum between the trench bottom and the pipe. The maximum center-to-
center spacing between such supports shall be four (4) metres.
Foam supports shall have a thirty two (32) kg/m3 minimum density and a 0.207 MPa minimum
compressive strength. Company may require changes to the spacing of these supports contingent on a
trial section of pipe being lowered in and clearances between trench bottom and bottom of pipe being
checked to ensure that the minimum clearance of one hundred and fifty (150) millimetres is maintained.
The use of support plugs with or without foam pillows, shall be included in the applicable Unit Price Item
for pipe protection.
13.2.2 Padding
Where directed by Company, Contractor shall pad the top and sides of the pipe so that only padding
material are within one hundred and fifty (150) millimetres of the pipe. The material to be used for
padding shall be well graded non-angular mineral material, with a maximum particle size of forty (40)
millimetres. This material shall be placed on the pipe using a procedure that does not damage the
coating and is acceptable to Company.
Bedding and Padding when requested by Company, with select material can be accomplished in two
ways:
13.2.2.1 Mechanical Padder Placement
Screens on mechanical padders shall be of a size to provide material that does not damage the coating
on the pipe upon impact and as a minimum shall not allow particles that exceed forty (40) millimetres in
size to pass through the screens. If for any reason this criteria is not achieved, Contractor will be
required to change screens and/or revise the process to ensure screened material dropping on the pipe
does not damage the coating, all to the satisfaction of Company.
13.2.2.2 Hauled in Material Placement
Where Company requires that material be imported from external sources Contractor shall be
responsible for acquiring approval for the use of these sources from all municipal and provincial
authorities including all associated permits. Contractor shall comply with all applicable permit conditions
and provide Company with a copy of all permits.
If in Company's opinion, Contractor unnecessarily permits the trench spoil to freeze and bedding and
padding is required, Contractor shall receive no additional compensation for the provision, hauling and
placement of the bedding and padding material.




                                              Page 95 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                           OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Disposal of surplus material (rock or boulders) remaining from the bedding and padding operation shall
be done in accordance with one of the alternatives identified in Section 22.0 of this Attachment B-2.4 –
Construction Specifications, and as approved by Company. The costs associated with disposal of surplus
material (rock or boulders) remaining from the bedding and padding operation shall be included with
Contractor’s applicable Unit Price Item for bedding and padding.
Where bedding and padding is requested by Company, Contractor shall be compensated in accordance
with the applicable Unit Price Item in Schedule C - Commercial Terms.
13.3 Alternate Methods of Pipe Protection
Under certain trench conditions and areas on the ROW Company may request one of the following
methods of pipe protection.
13.3.1 Rock Shield
At certain locations, to protect the coated pipe, Company may request that the coated pipe be wrapped
with full circumference 11mm Tuff-N-Nuff rock shield outer guard. Contractor shall comply with such
request and shall be compensated at the Unit Price Item set out in Schedule C - Commercial Terms.
14.0 Road & Railway Crossings
14.1 General
Highway, road, and trail crossings shall be installed in accordance with Appendix B-1 - Drawings, and in a
manner which meets all the requirements of the crossing permit and agreement or approval and the
Authorities Having Jurisdiction.
All road, highway and railroad crossings shall be made in strict accordance with all requirements of the
Transportation Safety Board of Canada, the applicable Provincial Regulator (AER/OGC), and any other
Authorities Having Jurisdiction. The method for constructing each crossing shall be in accordance with
the Contract Documents or as requested by Company.
It is Contractor's responsibility to become familiar with the requirements of the crossing
permits/agreements, pertaining to notices that must be provided to Authorities Having Jurisdiction prior
to commencing work on the crossing.
Contractor shall notify the proper authorities, in writing, at least seventy two (72) hours before starting
this work (or such greater notification as may be identified in Attachment A-1.5 -Line List or on Crossing
Agreements) so that their representatives may be present during the installation, if desired.
Contractor shall make contacts in writing where possible and maintain a contact log. The contact log
shall as a minimum record name of company, person contacted, time and date of call and brief summary
of discussion. Confirmation of these notifications shall be provided to Company.
Contractor shall obtain the specific approval from Company prior to commencing excavation at any
crossing.
Crossings requiring heavy wall pipe as defined on the Drawings shall have the minimum amount
installed as indicated on the Drawings. Contractor shall cut and move ahead any heavy wall pipe pups in
excess of three (3) metres in addition to that shown on the Drawings.

PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                            OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT

ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


The method required for the construction of each crossing shall be shown on Schedule A – Scope of
Work or elsewhere within the Contract Documents. Company does, however, reserve the right to
change its specified method for the construction of any crossing.
All work performed at each crossing shall be done in such a manner as to prevent undue obstruction,
delay or interference with traffic at the crossing. Contractor shall provide barricades, warning signs,
flares, lanterns, flagmen and other such protective measures as may be required to maintain traffic and
to safeguard the public at all times as directed by Company. All excavations adjacent to highways, roads
and trails must be fenced with safety fence or snow fence in a manner acceptable to Company. Such
fence shall remain in place until the excavation is backfilled.
Excavation in close proximity to railroads, canals and roads shall be in accordance with Appendix B-1
Drawings and the Crossing Agreement. For those roads that have no setback stipulation within the
drawing or Crossing Agreement, generally excavations shall not be made closer than two (2) metres
from the toe of the slope of a road/highway or railway fill nor closer than three (3) metres from the
edge of the railway grade. These distances may be increased depending on soil conditions. If so
warranted by soil conditions, Contractor may be required to reinforce the excavation by means of
shoring or sheet piling to prevent the possibility of undermining the crossing.
Shoring and sheet piling shall be installed and maintained in accordance with the Contractor’s Shoring
and Sheet Piling Plan, the Authorities Having Jurisdiction, and the Contractor’s Project Specific Health,
Safety and Environmental Plan. Prior to installation of sheet piling or shoring Contractor shall provide
Company with a plan for the installation and maintenance of same. The plan shall include the type,
manufacturer and installation procedures and specifications. Costs associated with the supply,
installation, maintenance and removal of sheet piling or shoring shall be included in the Base Lay Price.
Suitable measures shall be used at all times to prevent damage to roads and railroads when crossing
with construction equipment.
The shoulders, ditches, banks and slopes of all roads and railroads crossed shall be restored to their
former condition unless otherwise directed by Company. These crossings shall be properly rip rapped
with sacks filled with earth, sand, or other suitable material and shall be properly seeded to prevent
failure of the slope. Such restoration shall be as required by the Authorities Having Jurisdiction and in
accordance with the Specifications.
All road and railroad crossings are to be continuously maintained until the completion of the Work. No
additional compensation shall be paid for Contractor's repair or maintenance of crossings.
The carrier pipe coating shall be inspected prior to installation with an approved electronic holiday
detector and repaired all in accordance with this Attachment B-2.4 – construction Specifications.
All costs associated with the excavation and installation of crossings of railways, roads and highways, in
accordance with the Contract Documents and the Authorities Having Jurisdiction, shall be included in
the Base Lay Price, unless a specific Lump Sum is requested in Schedule C – Commercial Terms.
14.2 Trenchless Crossings
Where required by the Contract Documents, and at all railways, Contractor shall install various crossings
using the slip bore, track bore or directional drill method. Bores or drills shall be made accurately in
accordance with the requirements of Appendix B-1 - Drawings and of this Attachment B-2.4 –
Construction Specifications.

14.3 Open Cut Crossings
All roads and trails not shown on Appendix B-1- Drawings or identified in Attachment A-1.3 – Master
Crossing List provided as a bore can be installed using the open cut procedure in accordance with this
Specification. Contractor's costs for all open cut crossing work, including the supply and installation of
sand, pit run gravel and other re surfacing materials, shall be included in the Base Lay Price.
Contractor shall, in all cases where the trench will be open cut across public or private roads, ensure
that a detour exists, provide a shoofly suitable for automobile traffic or install temporary bridgework of
adequate strength and width to ensure the safe passage of traffic.
Prior to implementation these measures shall have the approval of Company and the Authorities Having
Jurisdiction.
Whenever possible, Contractor shall arrange to complete the trenching, laying and backfilling of road
crossings and removal of bridging before the end of the workday so as to avoid hazards to night traffic.
Contractor may be required to complete the crossing in sections to facilitate the continuous flow of
traffic.
Where the trench has been open cut through driveways, streets, roads or highways, the initial backfill
material shall be wetted sand placed evenly and carefully around and over the pipe, in one hundred and
fifty (150) millimeter layers. Each layer shall be carefully compacted by further wetting as required and
by tamping until three hundred (300) millimetres of cover exists over the pipe. The balance of backfill
material shall be placed in one hundred and fifty (150) millimetre layers and shall be compacted by the
use of mechanical tampers so that each layer has a density equal to or greater than that of the adjacent
original material. For driveways, streets, gravel roads and highways this shall be compacted to ninety
five percent (95%) of Standard Proctor Density. The upper 0.30 m of the travel surface shall be replaced
with material that is equivalent to, or better than, the original surface material of the road such as
gravel, crushed rock or other material and compacted to ninety five percent (95%) Standard Proctor
Density and surfaces previously paved be repaved.
Contractor shall provide Company with compaction test records for all open cut driveways, streets,
improved gravel roads and highways to comply with the above requirements upon completed backfill.

15.1 General

Company or other Authorities Having Jurisdiction.
The method for constructing each crossing shall be in accordance with the Contract Documents or as
requested by Company.
It is Contractor's responsibility to become familiar with the requirements of the crossing
permits/agreements, pertaining to notices that must be provided to authorities prior to commencing
work on the crossing.

Contractors ground disturbance supervisor shall ensure all buried facilities within five (5) metres of the
work area have been positively identified by hand digging or hydro-vac methods prior to any mechanical
excavation.
Contractor shall be solely responsible for determining the existence and location of, and shall take all
precautions to avoid damage to other pipelines, water mains, sewers, underground telephone cables,
telegraph and power conduits, poles and guy wires, railroads, highways, bridges or other underground
structures crossing or adjacent to the pipeline being constructed.
Contractor shall be solely liable for all expenses for repairs to any damage caused to such underground
and above ground facilities or structures.
Contractor shall provide typical procedures (written) for installing the new pipeline under buried
facilities, for Company approval, one week prior to the start of any facility crossing installations. If for
any reason Contractor wishes to deviate from the approved typical installation procedure(s), Contractor
shall re-submit a revised procedure, a minimum of one week prior to the proposed work.
Where requested by Company, for any specific facility crossing location (e.g. multiple facility crossings or
any that present a unique safety hazard), Contractor shall provide a detailed sketch one week prior to
the start of any work at the specified location. As a minimum, the sketch shall include a description of
the facilities (i.e. size, material type, type of service, etc.), the vertical and horizontal location(s) of the
facilities and the proposed alignment of the new pipeline in relation to the facilities to be crossed.
Prior to any Ground Disturbance work within five (5) metres of any buried facility a Ground Disturbance
Checklist/Hazard Assessment shall be completed. In addition, Contractor shall be in possession of a Safe
Work Permit, unless otherwise approved by Company.
All buried facilities shall have been located and fully exposed in accordance with this Specification and,
in addition, the following conditions apply:
           To confirm whether multiple facilities may exist within a common trench, expose a slot on
            either side of the facility. The slot must extend for a minimum distance of one and one half
            (1.5) metres from each side of the facility, when measured perpendicular to the facility, to a
            minimum of 0.15 metres below the bottom of the facility; and
           Small diameter pipelines (NPS 12 or less) and all cables (electrical, communication, etc.)
            shall be exposed (hand or hydrovac) across the full width of the proposed trench or
            excavation.
Contractor shall give proper notice, not less than seventy two (72) hours, or as specified in the Crossing
Agreement, to the respective facility owner(s), prior to any trenching or boring/drilling at these
locations. Confirmation of such notice shall be provided to Company.
Company shall be on site at all times during buried facility crossing operations. Excavation and/or
boring/drilling in the vicinity of a buried facility shall not commence until the facility owner
representative is present, unless approval is otherwise provided to Company.
Before excavating within five (5) metres of buried facilities, the designated equipment operator and all
others (i.e., Supervisor, Inspector and spotter) involved in the work must:
           Review the Ground Disturbance/Hazard Assessment Checklist;
           Verify the location of all above and below-grade facilities in the work area;

           Discuss and agree on hand signals with the designated spotter, and ensure the spotter
            understands their responsibilities;
           Ensure everyone understands appropriate procedures for exposing and excavating buried
            facilities safely; and
           Ensure Company or facility Company issues a Safe Work Permit and the Supervisor retains a

           In addition, the equipment operator must:

           Ensure a designated spotter is utilized for all excavation including clean-out, trim and backfill
            activities;
           Use extreme caution when excavating in high-risk areas containing buried facilities (e.g.,
            limits the size or depth of cuts);
           Maintain safe clearances as required in this section; and
           Use extreme caution if buried flagging, planking or concrete is uncovered, as this often
            indicates a power cable or pipe is located below.
No mechanical excavation is to be done within five (5) metres of a buried facility, or as specified in the
Crossing Agreement, unless otherwise approved by the facility owner and/or Company.
           Contractor prepares a detailed written procedure, for approval by Company;
           The facility owner grants written approval for such excavation, in accordance with the
            approved procedure;
           The facility owner representative must be on site during execution of the work;
           Only designated backhoe operators will be permitted to perform the excavation; and
           Contractor assumes all responsibility for safe conduct of the work and any damage to
            facilities that may occur.
Equipment excavating within five (5) metres of a buried facility, or on a Company facility site, shall be
equipped with a clean-up bucket or Company approved equal.
Contractor shall ensure that exposed facilities are adequately supported to prevent damage to the
facility, in accordance with the facility owner’s requirements and to the satisfaction of Company. At
crossings of buried pipelines, the maximum length of unsupported pipe spans and the maximum vertical
deflection of these pipelines shall be in accordance with the requirements stipulated by the facility
owner.
In compliance with this Attachment B-2.4 – construction Specifications and as approved by the owner of
the buried facility, buried facilities may be crossed using the open cut, slip-bore or drilling techniques.
Free boring (i.e. uncased) is not permitted under any circumstances. Alternate techniques, shall be
approved by Company prior to being used. Open Cut, Slip-Bore and Drilling are defined as follows:
           Trenchless
            o Slip-Bore refers to using a boring machine, with the auger surrounded by a casing pipe.
                The minimum separation between the existing facility and the new pipeline shall be one
                (1) metre, unless otherwise specified.




                                              Page 100 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                             OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


            o   Drilling refers to using a horizontal directional drilling rig. The minimum separation
                between the existing facility and the new pipeline shall be as specified by the facility
                Company. Refer to ESS 2.10 Horizontal Directional Drilling (HDD).
           Open Cut refers to mechanically excavating a pipeline trench to cross another facility. The
            minimum separation between the existing facility and the new pipeline shall be 0.6 metres,
            unless otherwise specified.
15.2 Trenchless Crossings
Where required by the Contract Documents, Contractor shall install various crossings using the slip bore,
track bore or directional drill method. Bores or drills shall be made accurately in accordance with the
requirements of the Appendix B-1 Drawings and this Attachment B-2.4 – Construction Specifications.
Where existing facilities (e.g. pipelines, cables) are located within the bored segment of a road, highway,
buried facility corridor or railway, which will be slip-bored or drilled for the crossing, Contractor shall
ensure that sufficient depth is maintained during the boring or drilling operation to ensure that the
minimum separation required will be maintained between the existing facility and the completed
pipeline.
Diligent monitoring of the "slip-bore or drilling" techniques during crossing operations is considered
critical to worker safety and the integrity of existing facilities. The term "crossing operation" refers to
the operation of boring or drilling the crossing and includes pulling the carrier pipe under/over the
facility to complete the crossing. When conducting slip- bore/drilled crossings, the requirements listed
below shall be followed without exception.
           Sight holes shall be centered over the facility at the location where it is to be bored or
            drilled.
           Sight holes must expose the full circumference of the facility and, shall be adequate to
            clearly see the pipe and any dirt or rock movement beneath the facility, indicating deviation
            from the bore/drill or pull line. In addition, sight holes must be deep enough to enable
            confirmation of the minimum separation requirements between the bottom of the existing
            facility and the new pipe being installed. Sight hole excavation shall be carried out to the
            satisfaction of the facility owner and Company.
           Sight holes shall be kept clear of sloughed soil and debris and shall be unobstructed by
            equipment during the crossing operation.
           When boring/drilling under or over a buried facility and the start of the bore/drill is greater
            than five (5) metres from the facility, a sight hole shall be excavated three (3) to five (5)
            metres in front of the facility or as otherwise approved by Company or owner of the facility;
           When crossing two or more facilities in a single operation, additional sight holes shall be
            positioned between crossings (the facilities), adequate to monitor the crossing operation, to
            the satisfaction of Company. Space permitting and in compliance with Company practices
            and procedures, a mechanically excavated trench, parallel to the facility to be crossed, may
            be substituted for additional sight hole(s).
           An appropriate survey method shall be used to constantly monitor the direction and
            elevation of the bore casing or drill stem during crossing operations.
           An observer (i.e. safety watch), who is in constant communication with, or clearly visible to
            the boring machine operator or driller, shall be stationed at appropriate sight holes during
            the crossing operation.


                                              Page 101 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                            OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


           If there is any indication of deviation from the planned path of the cased bore or drill, the
            operation shall be stopped immediately. The crossing operation shall not be resumed until
            the source of the problem is identified and resolved to the satisfaction of Company.
In sand/sandy soils, Contractor shall take preventative steps to ensure the integrity of the feature being
bored is not jeopardized. The following are some of the preventative measures that should be
considered prior to starting boring work;
           Cutting head to not extend beyond/past the end of the bore casing, i.e. retain auger within
            the casing.
           Stopping rotation of the cutting head and auger assembly if for any reason forward
            movement of the bore casing is stopped, e.g. for maintenance, repairs or if stuck in the bore
            hole.
           Continuous and diligent monitoring during boring operations to watch for any signs that
            may indicate “settling” of the trail, road, highway or railway bed that may indicate potential
            undermining, which could affect the integrity of the trail, road, highway or railway.
           During slip bore operations, if there is any reason to believe undermining may have and/or
            may be occurring, boring operations must cease immediately. The Contractor must notify
            the Inspector and roadway or rail Authorities immediately; boring operations shall not re-
            commence until the source of the problem is determined and corrected to the satisfaction
            of the Authorities Having Jurisdiction and the Company Inspector.
           Contractor shall monitor returns to ensure that boring operations do not undermine the
            facility being bored and potentially cause “caving-in” of the bed of any trail, road, highway
            or railway, during boring operations.
           In unstable soils, as determined by Company, Contractor shall not attempt to pull the carrier
            pipe through an unsupported bored hole. In unstable soils the carrier pipe shall be welded
            to the bore casing pipe (or attached by other means as acceptable to Company) and pulled
            through while extracting the boring machine.
15.3 Open Cut Crossings
Contractor, after exposing the buried facility across the full width of the trench, shall fully support those
facilities that require support due to span width or unstable soil conditions. Prior to supporting buried
facilities the method and procedure for supporting buried facilities shall be approved by the Company of
the facility and to the satisfaction of Company. Contractor shall exercise extreme care to prevent any
damage to buried facilities and shall repair any damage to exposed pipelines or cables to the satisfaction
of Company and the applicable facility owner, all at no additional compensation to Contractor.
The trench depth necessary to achieve the required minimum separation between the existing and new
facilities shall be maintained for the full width of the facility ROW, or to a minimum of (5) metres on
either side of the facility, if a ROW does not exist.
Refer to Appendix B-1 Drawings for minimum spacing requirements when more than one pipe is
installed in a common trench.
15.4 Backfilling Existing Buried Facilities

A minimum of twenty-four (24) hours, prior to the shading and/or backfilling of any buried facilities,
Contractor shall ensure that the facility owner has been notified so they may be present for backfilling
operations, unless approval is otherwise provided to Company.
Prior to any shading/backfilling of any buried facility, Contractor shall be in possession of a Safe Work
Permit.
During backfilling operations within three (3) metres of an existing facility, Contractor shall support the
exposed facility to the satisfaction of Company and the facility owner, to minimize risk of damage.
Backfill procedures as described above shall be implemented to the extent practical when backfilling
buried facilities to the facility owner’s satisfaction.
Contractor shall note that mechanical devices or equipment will not be allowed within 0.60 metres of
the buried facility. Backfill material within two (2) metres of either side of any buried facility shall be
deposited in lifts not exceeding 0.30 metres. Contractor shall compact each lift using mechanical
compaction equipment to the satisfaction of Company to ensure the buried facility is properly
supported on a firm foundation.
Contractor shall ensure that appropriate measures are taken to ensure facilities are not damaged during
backfilling operations.
Contractor's cost for all work associated with the installation of the new pipeline under/over all facility
crossings identified in the Contract shall be included in the Base Lay Price.
16.0 Watercourse Crossings
16.1 General
Rivers, creeks and other watercourse crossings shall be installed in accordance with the Contract
Document. In addition, watercourse crossings shall be made in a manner which meets all the
requirements of the Department of Fisheries and Oceans, crossing permit and agreement or approval of
the Authorities Having Jurisdiction.
The method for constructing each crossing shall be in accordance with the Drawings, the Construction
Line List, the alignment sheets, or as defined within the Contract Documents or as requested by
Company.
It is Contractor's responsibility to become familiar with the requirements of the crossing
permits/agreements, pertaining to notices that must be provided to authorities prior to commencing
work on the crossing.
Note: non-toxic hydraulic fluid (e.g., vegetable oil based) may be required to be used in excavation
equipment used for crossing watercourses (including the associated sag bends). This will be at
Company’s discretion at no additional cost to Company.
Contractor is reminded that flexibilities indicated in the EPP will be exercised at Company’s discretion.
The flexibilities are written into the EPP documents to prevent inappropriate application of protection
measures outside of regulatory approval requirements. An important distinction in this document is
that the ephemeral draws are considered water courses by Company for the purposes of the
environmental protection associated with vehicle crossings, splash guards, silt guards and setbacks.



                                              Page 103 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                          OCTOBER 4TH 2015
