ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Costs associated with the installation of water crossings shall be included in the Base Lay Price unless
there is a specific Lump Sum Price requested for a specific crossing in Schedule C - Commercial Terms.
Two (2) weeks prior to commencement of any work at a crossing, Contractor shall submit to Company
for review and approval, a plan of its proposed method for the installation of the crossing, to meet the
following requirements.
           Where specified in Attachment A-1.3 – Master Crossing List, Contractor shall provide a
            detailed crossing plan which as a minimum shall include grading requirements, installation
            procedure, trenching method, trench spoil temporary storage location, mitigative measures
            to control sediment and prevent its infiltration into the watercourse, location for
            dewatering any dirty trench water, method of back-filling and restoration process, and
            timing to complete bank restoration as soon as practical.
           Contractor shall provide a typical installation procedure which would be used for the pipe
            installation in those watercourses not specified as requiring a detailed crossing installation
            plan in the watercourse table in Attachment A-1.6 – Watercourse List. The typical crossing
            installation plan shall include as a minimum, trenching method, trench spoil temporary
            storage location, mitigative measures to control sediment and prevent its infiltration into
            the watercourse, location for dewatering any dirty trench water, method of back-filling and
            restoration process, and timing to complete bank restoration as soon as practical.
The approval by Company of the procedure or procedures to be used by Contractor shall not relieve
Contractor from sole responsibility for the crossing installation, and complying with all requirements in
accordance with the Contract Documents.
Contractor shall give ten (10) days notification before commencement of crossing work.
All water crossing regardless of size must have all the required equipment, men and materials on site
prior to the commencement of the instream isolation and excavation. No instream work will be allowed
to commence after ten (10:00) AM, unless the Contractor has demonstrated on the same Project the
ability complete a similar crossing in the time remaining in the day.
Once instream activities begin at fisheries sensitive water crossings, the work must proceed
continuously to the restoration of normal instream water flow. Company may allow exceptions on a
case specific basis.
In all water bodies, excavated materials shall not be stockpiled within the wetted perimeter of the
watercourse, except where otherwise approved in writing by Company Representative.
The required method of damming for isolations at water crossings up to five (5) metres wide will be
plate steel for both the upstream and downstream dams unless specifically exempted by Company.
Contractor shall restrict grubbing and grading activities at watercourse crossings to the ditchline and
required Work Space and shall minimize the removal of side-stream vegetation. Hand clear all slopes
leading to watercourses and within ten (10) metres of all watercourses, in accordance with Section 5.0,
Clearing, Grubbing, Grading and Upper Surface Material Management of this Specification and the EPP.
At watercourse crossings, Contractor shall leave an un-grubbed buffer setbacks, extending ten (10) to
twenty (20) metres back from the top of the immediate stream banks, until actual crossing construction
commences. Contractor shall salvage merchantable trees from this buffer strip at time of salvage and



                                             Page 104 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                          OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


clearing operation but shall not remove understory vegetation or grub within this buffer strip. Trees
shall be felled away from the stream and any debris introduced shall be immediately removed from the
stream. This setback may be reduced by Company Representative to three (3) to five (5) metres by
recognition of steep slopes.
Feller bunchers may be allowed to do work in place of hand clearing if specifically approved by Company
on an individual site basis.
Vehicle and equipment crossings of watercourses shall be in accordance with Attachment A-1.6 –
Watercourse List. Where culverts and ramps are allowed as a crossing method, culverts shall be sized as
follows:
           During winter construction the minimum culvert diameter allowed is 0.3 metres and the
            maximum culvert size is one and a half (1.5) metres; and
           During summer construction the minimum culvert diameter is 0.3 metres with a maximum
            diameter of one and a half (1.5) metres.
           Pipe can be used in place of culverts.
Contractor shall minimize disturbance to the watercourse bed when installing culverts. To keep ramp
material from entering the watercourse on private lands, geotextile shall be placed over the culvert
prior to adding grade material. On forest lands, geotextile shall be placed over the culvert and logfill
prior to placing ramp material. An adequate amount of geotextile shall be used such that the material
can be folded over the side of the ramps to keep material from running into the watercourse during the
time the ramp will remain in place. Ramping material must be clean clay or approved matting material.
Ramping material can be logs, mats, snirt or clay. Contractor shall monitor all culverts to ensure they
remain functional during the course of the Work. Contractor shall also ensure the ramp material does
not enter watercourses during the course of the Work. Repairs to the culvert installation shall be carried
out in the presence of Company and in accordance with the Contract Document and the Authorities
Having Jurisdiction.
Vehicle crossings in certain streams may need to be installed and removed by using dam and pump
around procedures (refer to Attachment A-1.6 – Watercourse List for requirements).
Equipment shall not be washed in or within one hundred (100) metres of any watercourse.
Equipment or vehicles shall not be fueled or serviced within one hundred (100) metres of a watercourse.
All combustion engine driven equipment including pumps, generators and their fuel supply that are
within one hundred (100) metres of a watercourse shall be bermed or contained in plastic sumps. The
berms shall have an impermeable liner, and shall be constructed and equipped to contain potential
pump fluid spills.
No debris of any kind or any harmful substance shall be placed or left where it will enter the stream.
16.2 Trenchless Crossings
Where required by the Contract Documents, Contractor shall install various crossings using the slip bore,
track bore or directional drill method. Bores or drills shall be made accurately in accordance with the
requirements of the Drawings and Section 17.0, Trenchless Crossings of this Specification.
16.3 Open Cut Crossings



                                             Page 105 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                            OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Where conventional open cut crossings are permitted (refer to Attachment A-1.6 – Watercourse
List), no in-stream trenching activity shall take place until the required materials and equipment
are on-site and pipe for the crossing has been welded, radiographed, welds joint coated and
weighted, as required. Activities including in-stream ditching and pipe layouts shall be preplanned to
minimize in-stream construction time to twelve (12) hours. At such watercourse crossings which
have no standing or running water at the time of construction, continuous welding and trenching
through the watercourse will be allowed. Where water is flowing at non fish sensitive watercourses
continuous welding of the pipe and continuous trenching will be allowed provided the isolation
requirements are maintained 24 hours a day. Tie-in requirements at all watercourses must be
resolved by contractor as a matter of pre planning and included in the Base Lay Price. This must
include tie-ins required due to maintaining setbacks for vegetation buffers.
All pumps and generators used within twenty (20) metres of watercourses must be contained within a
plastic impermeable tub with sides high enough to contain all leaks and spray from the unit. Virtually all
sizes of this type of tub are now available. Plastic sheeting with sand bags will only be allowed at large
hydrostatic fill installations, under special permission from Company Representative.
At open cut fish sensitive crossings, hard plugs may be specified by Company on both banks until the
main channel and floodplain trench have been excavated and the pipe is ready for installation. Soft
plugs may not be used for this application, except at specific locations where Company so approves.
At fish sensitive watercourses, excavated materials that are unstable or draining water must be
contained a minimum of twenty (20) meters back from the water course. If EWS is cleared for water
crossing spoil containment a thirty (30) meter setback and vegetation buffer must be maintained. The
30 meters maybe reduced to 10 or 20 meters by Company’s approved representative.
Soils shall not be stockpiled on creek banks of ten degree (10°) slope or greater, if potentially unstable,
in Company's opinion. Mitigative measures as approved by Company shall be implemented to restrict
the migration of spoil materials back into the creek, all at no additional cost to Company.
Where instream placement of ditch spoil is approved, at no time shall more than two thirds (2/3) of the
water body width be blocked by construction activity (unless isolation methods are used), so that water
flow is maintained.
Where present, surface gravel from the bed of the watercourse must be salvaged and stockpiled
separately for later placement. Stream bed gravel shall not be removed from the watercourse for
construction use.
Contractor shall confirm to the satisfaction of Company that the trench is of appropriate depth prior to
installing the pipe section. Contractor shall also assist Authorities Having Jurisdiction's survey crew in
confirming that the installed section has the required cover. Crossings determined to have inadequate
cover will be removed and the trench deepened prior to reinstallation of the section.
To prevent soil and bank erosion, watercourse banks shall be backfilled immediately, re-contoured and
fully compacted to the satisfaction of the Authorities Having Jurisdiction and Company. Approach slopes
to watercourse shall be cleaned-up, have surface water diversion berms installed, and shall be ready for
revegetation as soon as practical. Silt fences shall be installed as required and installed in accordance
with the Drawings and Specifications.

Water crossings and banks shall be backfilled in accordance with the applicable water crossing drawing.
Once the depth of cover has been confirmed and complied with the minimum requirements of the
Drawings or this Specification and accepted by Company, Contractor shall commence backfill operations
immediately.
Following backfilling, streambeds shall be graded to conform as closely as possible to preconstruction
profiles.
16.4 Water Crossings with Restricted Access Period (RAP)
Contractor shall notify Company a minimum of ten (10) days prior to any work on any watercourse
crossing (refer to Attachment A-1.6 – Watercourse List).
For traffic access, vehicle crossing ramps shall be installed in accordance with Appendix B-1 Drawings
and in accordance with Attachment A-1.6 – Watercourse List.
Where permitted, culverts shall be installed by isolating the location of the crossing using a dam
and pump-around procedure in accordance with the drawings unless otherwise approved by Company.
Where watercourses either have adequate ice thickness or are frozen to the bottom, log fills and ice
bridges may be approved by Company as vehicle crossings.
At certain watercourse crossings designated in Attachment A-1.6 – Watercourse List, Contractor shall
place warning signs upstream and downstream to comply with all special precautionary measures
required by federal and provincial authorities, and shall work closely with such authorities to prevent or
minimize obstructions to navigation. Boaters and snowmobilers must be notified/protected as required
by approvals and regulatory requirements.
Contractor is advised that water courses must receive consistent protection against the introduction of
silt by down ROW flow of water, and by the splashing of mud as vehicles cross over the watercourse.
The Contractor is responsible for identifying during weather events where on ROW water flow is directly
entering water courses. Once identified, diversion trenches, diversion berms, and/or silt fencing must be
maintained or newly installed. The size and length must be sufficient to direct water off of the ROW into
undisturbed vegetation a minimum of twenty (20) metres prior to the water reaching the water course.
All vehicle water course crossings must be equipped with splash/siltation guards that are wrapped
into the bottom of the crossing installation. The guards may be made of plywood or geotextile. They
must be at least one (1) metre high and have wings on the entrance to the crossing. The guards must
be regularly maintained, especially after snowfall events. The remainder of the ROW width must be
protected with silt run off guards consisting of a grade lip, or silt fence
If mud has accumulated, or formed by thawing on vehicle crossings, the contractor must institute speed
controls that are slow enough to prevent splash over, by all vehicles into the water course.
All water course siltation control structures and actions, must be included in the Base Lay price.
Contractor is advised that if the corrections to control watercourse siltation are not immediate,
sustained, and sufficient, Company may stop all work until the corrective actions are taken. Contractor
will not be entitled to payment for such work stoppages.

PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                             OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Passage for construction vehicles and equipment across all watercourses shall be in accordance with
Attachment A-1.6 – Watercourse List.
Contractor shall install temporary bridges in accordance with the Appendix B-1 - Drawings and
requirements of Company and Authorities Having Jurisdiction, or may submit an alternative bridge
proposal for Company's approval.
Contractor shall ensure that the approach fill or support structures do not intrude into the stream unless
otherwise approved by Company or the Authorities Having Jurisdiction. Contractor shall ensure that
there is adequate free-board to handle anticipated stream flows or water traffic. Temporary bridges
shall be installed in advance of grading activities and shall be removed in conjunction with clean-
up activities. Bridge abutments shall not extend into the wetted perimeter of the watercourse unless
otherwise specifically approved by Company and the Authorities Having Jurisdiction.
Where a clear span bridge is required for construction and is to be installed during clearing, the
Contractor is responsible for the installation costs. This includes; stripping and grading the access trail to
the water crossing, trucking of the bridge to the site, excavation and placement of logs for the
abutments, positioning of the bridge, construction of the approach wings, and grading the approaches
as per the environmental protection plan and regulatory requirements. Should the Contractor hire the
clearing contractor to perform bridge installations, the Contractor is responsible for the bridge integrity
and safety.
Where the contractor directs the clearing contractor to build a native timber bridge for mainline use, the
contractor must have a representative on site during bridge construction, or be prepared to accept or
rebuild the bridge at no further cost to the Company. The decision as to whether a vehicle crossing type
built by the clearing contractor, can be used by the contractor as per environmental requirements, will
be made by the Company Representative.
Clearing and grading activities shall be conducted so as to minimize disturbance to root systems through
the valleys of named streams.
Contractor shall hydrostatically test certain water crossing sections prior to installation of the pipe, for
those streams identified by Company, and for those water bodies under which the crossing is drilled as
described in Schedule A - Scope of Work. Contractor should refer to Schedule A - Scope of Work for the
list of crossings that require pre-tests.
The pipe shall be tested for a minimum of one (1) hour during daylight hours and otherwise in
accordance with the requirements of this Attachment B-2.4 – construction Specifications. Should a loss
in pressure occur which cannot be correlated to temperature, the cause of such loss in pressure shall be
found and remedied. Immediately following successful completion of the hydrostatic test, the pipe shall
be completely dewatered. Special care shall be taken during cold weather conditions to ensure that all
of the test water has been removed prior to installing the crossing section. Contractor shall give
Company a minimum of forty eight (48) hours’ notice prior to commencement of the test.
All water crossings identified as ‘isolated’ in Attachment A-1.6 – Watercourse List shall be installed by
either dam and pump-around or by dam and flume procedures in accordance with the Drawings. Pump
intake screens shall be installed in accordance with DFO’s Freshwater Intake End-of-Pipe Fish Screen
Guideline and any applicable Provincial guidelines. Back- up pumps and gensets shall also be present at
time of crossing, and during flash flood events Company will consider proposals on crossing techniques
that do not isolate the stream flow from the construction activities.

The top fifty (50) centimetres (granular material if present) of the excavated trench within the wetted
perimeter of the watercourse shall be removed and stockpiled separately for replacement at a similar
location during backfilling unless otherwise approved by Company.
The pipeline water crossing section shall not be pulled in until Contractor has demonstrated to Company
that the trench depth is adequate. Contractor shall give Company at least twenty four (24) hours’ notice
prior to pulling in the water crossing section.
At the river crossings Company may retain a diver or use any other suitable method to inspect the
bottom of the trench prior to pipe installation and prior to the backfilling of the trench. Contractor shall
facilitate the work of the diver and shall furnish the necessary equipment and helpers, other than the
actual diving equipment necessary for the diver to perform his work.
Contractor shall take depth soundings/or measurements of the bottom of the pipeline trench at
intervals along the crossing immediately prior to installation of the pipe to ensure adequate trench
depth has been excavated to achieve the design depth of cover. After pipe installation Contractor shall
confirm the depth of cover on the pipe meets the minimum design depth of cover and fits the trench as
excavated. Contractor shall assist Company surveyors in establishing a final top of pipe profile of each
crossing. The taking of soundings or measurements shall be witnessed by and subject to the approval of
the Company.
After the depth of cover over the pipe and the pipe alignment have been inspected and approved by
Company, the pipe trench shall be backfilled to its original contours with excavated material to the
satisfaction of the government Authorities Having Jurisdiction and Company.
16.5 Blasting in or Near Water Bodies
All blasting in, or within fifty (50) metres of the wetted perimeter of, any named watercourses shall be
carried out in accordance with the requirements of this Attachment B-2.4 – construction Specifications.
16.6 Watercourse Bank Protection & Restoration
Water crossing banks shall be re-contoured and restored to their original condition unless otherwise
approved or requested by Company and revegetated as soon as practical after backfilling.
Where specialized bank protection such as rock rip rap or geo-grid stream bank installation has been
specified on the Contract Documents, Contractor shall implement these measures as per Company's
request. Contractor shall be compensated for specialized restoration items in accordance with the
applicable Unit Price Item in Schedule C – Commercial Terms.
Under winter conditions in poor access locations the contractor will be prepared to perform bank
restorations concurrent with mainline activities.
17.0 Trenchless Crossings
Where required by the Contract Documents, Contractor shall install various crossings using the slip bore,
track bore or directional drill method. Bores or drills shall be made accurately in accordance with the
requirements of the Drawings and this Specification.
17.1 Bored Crossings




                                              Page 109 of 148

AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


When installing an uncased bored crossing, Contractor shall accomplish the boring or augering through a
pilot section of pipe of the same diameter as the carrier pipe. Contractor shall supply the pipe to be used
for this purpose and in no case shall the bore size be larger than one pipe size greater than the carrier
pipe. To prevent subsequent settling of the crossing, voids in excess of one hundred and fifty (150)
millimetres shall be filled with grout or other Company approved material.
Under no circumstances shall boring or augering take place through the carrier pipe which is to become
a part of the permanent installation.
The start and end points for slip-bored crossings shall be in accordance with the Drawings, and in any
event shall not be closer to the road than the centerlines of the bar ditches or, where there is no bar
ditch, the toe of the road embankment, unless written approval to do otherwise is obtained from
Company.
Where obstructions or rock formations render boring at crossings specified to be bored hazardous or
impractical, Contractor may propose an alternate procedure for approval by Company and the
Authorities Having Jurisdiction over the crossing fifteen (15) days in advance of the work. If approved by
the authority, the open cut technique can be constructed in accordance with this 0of Attachment B-2.4
– Construction Specifications. In the event that open cutting is not an option, Contractor shall provide
Company with an alternate procedure for approval such as tunneling. Contractor shall notify Company
prior to the start of this work.
An adjustment in compensation paid to Contractor, due to a change in crossing installation methodology
from a bored crossing to an open cut crossing will be calculated as part of the Price Adjustments for
Changes as identified Schedule C – Commercial Terms.
Pipe to be supplied to Contractor for installing in bored or drilled sections requested by Company (refer
to Appendix A-3 - Company Supplied Material) will be abrasion coated and supplied by Company. Refer
to Appendix A-3 - Company Supplied Materials, for information regarding the abrasion coating.
Contractor shall cut and move ahead any abrasion coated pipe that is greater than three (3) metres in
length of that length required on the Alignment Sheets. Should Contractor elect to bore or drill any
additional crossings not required by Company, Contractor shall pre-coat the pipe for such crossings with
an additional protective layer approved by Company and supplied by Contractor. Refer to Appendix A-3 -
Company Supplied Material for approximate amount of abrasion coated pipe to be provided to
Contractor.
Once the carrier pipe has been installed, Company shall measure the coating resistance. Contractor
shall co-operate with this requirement and ensure that each end of the section is clean, dry and not in
contact with the ground while the measurement is taken. If the measurements indicate that the coating
has been damaged during the installation process, the section shall be removed and the coating
repaired. Contractor shall take preventative measures prior to re-installing the pipe in the bore hole.
These measures may include reaming of the hole. Removal of pipe sections determined to have coating
damage, coating repair, preventative measures and re-installation of the pipe shall be at no additional
compensation to Contractor.
After the bored section has been tied in, Contractor shall ensure the pipe is adequately supported prior
to completing backfilling. Compaction of native material or imported material and/or sandbag supports,
each a minimum length of one (1) metre along the pipe shall be utilized, in accordance with the
Drawings or as required by Company, all at no additional compensation to Contractor.

17.2 Horizontal Directional Drills
HDDs identified as required by Company will be listed in the Contract Documents. Required HDDs will
also have design information supplied in the contract.
Contractors bid will include all costs for the HDD contractor including mobilization, daily travel to site
regardless of distance, accommodations, and subsistence.
Contractor is responsible for assuring that the bore pads for required HDDs and discretionary HDDs are
positioned properly during grade planning, and cleared properly. The initial clearing must allow
sufficient space in front of the bore entry and exit points to allow for the over bend and tie-in to the line
pipe.
Contractor must present to Company a diagram for each HDD entry pad equipment layout.
Company reserves the right to suspend any HDD at any time and revert to open cut.
Contractor, unless directed otherwise, must prepare a cost for the open cut of all Company planned
HDDs.
Contractor is responsible for locating the bore entry and exit points and ensuring that the
drilling equipment is positioned properly on bore pads. Consideration must be given to
maintain access thru the pad if a vehicle watercourse crossing has been installed.
The Contractor must strip topsoil and or USM from the bore entry and exit pads and grade the pads with
a one meter high subsoil packed berm around the perimeter of the pads.
Contractor is responsible for clearing, stripping and excavating on pad, close to pad, or at other
locations, mud containment sumps sufficient to address expected mud returns and artesian water
returns. Contractor is advised that all drilling mud sumps require either regulatoryor Land Owner
approval.
Contractor is responsible for all bore tripping costs regardless of build ups in annular pressure.
Contractor must be prepared to address without undue delay, the encountering of solid rock in any bore
path. Company will not pay for any wait times associated with transporting rock drilling equipment on
site.
Company will pay for approved drilling muds, when significant lost circulation to formation occurs.
All drilling muds and additives the contractor intends to use must be approved by Company prior to the
commencement of the Work. Any new muds or additives the Contractor wishes to introduce after
commencement of the Work will be considered for approval by Company without an approval time
guarantee. No costs to Company can result.
Drilling mud additives that have toxic potential cannot be added to the drilling muds without Company’s
infield approval. No costs can be attributed to Company for the delay of any approval to use additives.
Contractor is advised on smaller HDDs, to drill with straight water as long as possible, to increase the
flexibility for disposal of the fluid and cuttings, and dealing with surface fracs.

All vac trucks and hydrovac trucks that are called to the ROW to perform mud return handling in the
entry pit, or for surface fracs, must be equipped with chains. If the trucks cannot access the required site
due a lack of chains, Company will not pay for any part of the truck costs.
Contractor will be responsible for all frac walking costs. On all HDD’s, frac walking will be continuous
while drilling is underway or any time annular pressure is present. Two people, that do not have other
duties, must be appointed to the frac walking at all times. Frac walking will be focused in relation to the
location of the drill head and mud pressure.
In the event of upland surface fracs, drilling will be stopped until the frac is contained and controlled.
Drilling will then be allowed to immediately resume. Contractor must be prepared to install water
course isolation measures as directed by Company to control near and instream surface frac releases.
In the event of in-stream or near-stream surface fracs drilling will be suspended until Company’s
Representative provides approval to do so.
Company will provide direction to the contractor as to the appropriate method of frac clean-up and mud
disposal.
Company may appoint a mud disposal specialist to the Project. Contractor must cooperate with the
directions of this representative.
All unanticipated costs associated with HDDs that the contractor submits to Company for payment must
be at the same rates the contractor pays for the work. Agreed upon administrative costs are additional.
Contractor must supply a suitable representative to coordinate the infield execution of the required
HDDs and the discretionary HDDs. This person will be responsible as a minimum for directing water and
vac trucks, supervising frac walkers, facilitating frac clean-up, and mud disposal preparations, in
cooperation with Company representatives as the situation demands.
Company understands the engineering and environmental benefits associated with HDDs, and
encourages and supports the decision process of the contractor to HDD several types of smaller
crossings. However, HDDs to be performed at the contractors’ discretion must be included in the Base
Lay price. Company reserves the right to suspend any discretionary HDD, and revert to open cut, within
the Base Lay price.
Discretionary HDDs must be approved by Company for the depth of the bore path in relation to the
expected annular pressures. As a minimum industry standards of good practice must be followed to
reduce the possibility for surface fracs. Contractor is advised that 10 m is the minimum bore depth of
cover for initial design unless approved or designed by Company.
Separate from the Grade plan the contractor must prepare a discretionary HDD plan that indicates the
details of all proposed HDDs. Schedule, length, entry and exit pad locations, vehicle crossing
requirements and bore path depths.
Except for the HDDs listed in the contract, Contractor will not specify any additional HDDs without a
signed letter from the Company Representative. There is no in-field process of HDD specification or
approval for additional HDDs, by grade planning or otherwise.
In the event Contractor elects to directionally drill certain road, railway, buried facility corridors or road
crossings these crossings shall be drilled in accordance with the applicable typical drawings.

17.3 Drilling Fluid Disposal
Contractor is advised that the handling of pipeline drilling fluids is coming under increasing regulatory
scrutiny, especially in relation to watercourses and general toxicity assurances. Methodologies used on
previous projects may not be valid.
Company will have expertise available to the Project to determine the appropriate methods of dealing
with HDD drilling fluids either returned to the entry pit or resulting from surface fracs. Interpretation of
AER Directive 50 and BC OGC Drilling and Production Regulation is solely the prerogative of the
Company Representative. Contractor must participate in the identification of sumps and land spread
locations. Regulatory permissions required for sump construction, land spraying, and land spreading will
be obtained by the Company. A minimum of 14 days is required to gain sump location approval.
Contractor is advised that requested areas may not be approved and no additional costs to The
Company will result.
The Contractors’ HDD representative and drilling contractor must cooperate with the drilling fluid
disposal requirements as determined by the Company Representative.
Contractors HDD representative will be responsible for engaging the appropriate number of vac trucks
to deal with the rate of entry pit fluid returns or surface fracs. The agreements for this purpose will be
required to be set up in advance with truck providers to respond on a 24 hour basis if the situation
demands.
18.0 Buoyancy Control
18.1 General
In areas where swamps, wetlands or watercourse crossings are encountered, Company may request
buoyancy control devices.
The primary method of buoyancy control for pipe diameters greater than NPS 24 will be mechanical
screw anchors. In addition, for those areas deemed not suitable for mechanical screw anchors (i.e., river
crossings, fen bogs, or others) pipeline weighting may consist of bolt-on type concrete weights, bag style
Pipe Saks or continuous coat concrete.
The primary method of buoyancy control for pipe diameters NPS 24, and less, will be geotextile bag
weights. In addition, for those areas deemed not suitable for geotextile bag weights (i.e., river crossings,
fen bogs, or others) pipeline weighting may consist of bolt-on type concrete weights, or continuous coat
concrete.
Buoyancy control devices requested by Company shall be manufactured, applied and installed in
accordance with the Contract Documents.




                                              Page 113 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                            OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Buoyancy control devices shall not be used when, in the opinion of Company, the trench can be
dewatered and the backfill material is stable enough to hold the pipeline in place after the trench
has been backfilled.
Contractor is advised that final quantities for buoyancy control devices and start/stop locations will
not be determined by Company until after trenching has been completed.
Contractor shall receive no additional compensation for relocation of buoyancy control devices
strung ahead of trenching.
Extreme care shall be taken in handling and installing buoyancy control devices to prevent damage to
the pipe, coating and weights or anchors.


In all weighting areas, the required depth of cover shall be measured from the top of the weight to
graded surface, unless otherwise approved by Company.


It is intended that geotextile bag weights are used to counter the effects of buoyancy. However, if
geotextile bag weights cannot be used (e.g. at river crossings), bolt-on concrete weights or continuous
concrete coating may be used. The Contractor’s representative shall recommend the appropriate
buoyancy control device as applicable for the determined soil type to Company for approval.


There are three types of soil conditions which are likely to be encountered during construction. These
are generally described below:


           Shallow muskeg, approximately one meter in depth – This type of installation will include
            peat and organic materials to a depth of approximately one meter below the surface. In this
            case, the trench will be excavated deep enough to allow the pipe to rest on competent soil,
            but the backfill material will have little or no shear strength or mass to assist in holding the
            pipe down. The specific gravity of the surrounding liquid for buoyancy calculations in this
            installation is assumed to be 1.2.
           Mineral soil with standing water or saturated soil – This type of installation will be through
            competent mineral soils which may have standing water in the ditch. The soil may be
            saturated at the time of installation or saturation may occur seasonally, raising the
            possibility of flotation of the pipe. Typical areas include basins, flood plains and stream
            crossings. The specific gravity of surrounding soil for buoyancy calculations in this
            installation is assumed to be 1.0, or the same as water.
           Muskeg, greater than one meter in depth – This type of installation will include peat and
            organic materials extending more than one meter below the surface making it not
            practicable to excavate to set the pipe on competent soil. The backfill used around the pipe
            will be primarily native materials and the pipe will not rest upon competent soil. This
            material may be saturated with water. The control measure for this soil condition will aim
            to have neutral buoyancy as both floating and sinking of the pipe is possible.

Guidelines for the control measures for each type of soil are presented in the table below. It is
important to note that these guidelines were developed without field investigation of the soil


                                             Page 114 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                           OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


properties. Before buoyancy control measures are installed on the pipeline, the site specific conditions,
including competent soil determination, shall be examined by a competent Geotechnical Professional,
provided by the Contractor, in order to confirm the analysis of the soil properties and the appropriate
method of buoyancy control is used. See Attachment B-2.3 for more information about the buoyancy
mitigation installation guidelines for the Project.

            Negative buoyancy of ten (10) percent assumed for spacing in all installations.
            Spacing of gravel filled bag weight is based on assumed bulk density of 2000 kg/m3. The
             filled bags should be weighed to confirm the minimum unit bag weight has been achieved.
            All values ignore any contribution from backfill shear forces or the mass of the mineral soil
             portion of the backfill. This is conservative.
            If weights with a mass other than that specified above are to be used, spacing requirements
             shall be confirmed with Company.
            If a buoyancy control method other than geotextile bag weights are to be used,

19.0 Construction Tie-Ins
19.1 General



                                             Page 115 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                              OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


At tie-in locations, the bell hole trench shall be excavated and adequately sized and protected in
accordance with the Health and Safety requirements of Schedule D - HSE, and Authorities Having
Jurisdiction to ensure the safety of personnel working in or in close proximity to the trench.
The pipe shall be cut to permit proper line-up, with sufficient slack and to ensure stresses caused during
the line-up are kept to a minimum. At each cut, the heat number and the manufacturer's pipe number
shall be indelibly marked on the outside of the pipe on each side of the cut.
All beveling, aligning, welding and inspection shall be done in accordance with this Attachment B-2.4 -
Construction Specifications. Tie-ins shall not be made at transition welds.
Contractor shall allow adequate time in accordance with of this Attachment B-2.4 – Construction
Specifications for non-destructive testing of all tie-in welds prior to coating. Tie-in welds shall not be
radiographed until they are within ten degrees (10°) Celsius of ambient temperature.
During the final weld at a field tie-in location, the pipe shall be fully supported by side booms until a
minimum of one fill pass is completed.
At tie-in welds, Contractor shall prepare and coat the exposed steel surface of the pipe in accordance
with of this Attachment B-2.4 – Construction Specifications using the coating materials specified in
Schedule A - Scope of Work and the coating shall be inspected with a holiday detector and repaired, all
in accordance with this Attachment B-2.4 – Construction Specifications.
All tie-in welds and transition welds shall be completed before the end of each day.
The pipe within bell holes and areas of over excavation shall be supported to the satisfaction of
Company and in accordance with Appendix B-1 Drawings. At the direction of Company, sandbags,
provided by Contractor shall be used if proper compaction and support for the pipe cannot be obtained
using backfill material.
Bell holes shall be properly backfilled and compacted to ensure that subsequent trench settlement does
not occur.
During summer construction special attention to compaction within bell holes shall include compaction
of soils with a hoe bucket or other compaction equipment as follows:
           Returning excavated trench material in lifts approximately thirty (30) to forty five (45)
            centimetres in thickness (will depend on soil conditions);
           Compacting returned lifts with a hoe bucket in areas of over excavation from the bottom of
            the trench to grade, at least sixty (60) centimetres away from the pipe; and
           Once sixty (60) centimetres of material has been placed over the actual pipeline, hoe bucket
            compaction will be used for remainder of lifts.
During winter construction where suitable unfrozen soil conditions exist, Contractor shall follow the
same procedures as above. Where soil conditions include frozen material lumpy material, and
compaction in accordance with the above is not practical in the opinion of Company, Contractor shall
backfill the excavation completely and then crown evenly over the excavation all remaining excavated
soil which will allow material to settle into the excavation during the spring thaw.
Backfill of bell holes shall be in accordance with this Attachment B-2.4 – Construction Specifications.

There shall not be more than three (3) full working days between the lowering-in and backfill operation
and the last incomplete or unfinished tie-in except for tie-ins that cannot be made until completion of

19.2 Final Tie-Ins
After pressure testing and pipe drying is completed to the satisfaction of Company, Contractor shall
complete all final tie-ins in accordance with this Attachment B-2.4 – Construction Specifications. Only
pretested pipe will be used if a pup is required to complete a final tie-in. Contractor shall only use pups
that have supporting test documentation available to confirm the pup has been tested to the proper
test pressure. All final tie-in welds must be radiographically inspected and approved before the piping is
placed in service. Contractor shall keep the number of final tie-in welds to a minimum.
Pipe pups cut off at final tie-ins in lengths of three (3) metres or greater shall be saved for return to
Company in accordance with the requirements of Schedule A - Scope of Work. Each such pup shall be
indelibly marked with the pipe heat number, the pressure test number for that pipe, and the words
"TESTED PIPE".
20.0 Cathodic Protection Test Stations
20.1 General
Cathodic protection test stations will be installed by Contractor, refer to Schedule A - Scope of Work.
21.0 General Backfilling
21.1 General
Contractor shall completely backfill the trench and all other excavations in accordance with the Contract
Documents.
The trench shall not be backfilled until Company confirms that the pipe has the required minimum
depth of cover and the pipe fits the trench. If a section of trench is backfilled without Company approval
and Company so requests, Contractor shall uncover the pipe to allow Company to conduct necessary
inspections. If cover over the pipe is not in accordance with the Contract Documents, Contractor shall
remove the pipe and re-excavate the trench directed by Company until the desired cover is obtained, all
at no additional compensation to Contractor.
To prevent erosion of the backfill in sloping terrain, Company may require trench breakers or sub-
drains to be installed in accordance with Appendix B-1 - Drawings. Company will determine the locations
and which types of breakers shall be installed. Contractor must ensure that the keys are dug as a part of
the ditching operation, and the appropriate amount of space is left open during backfill. Contractor can
suggest additional locations to Company, deletions must be approved by Company. Ditch plugs will be
field marked with survey lath. Contractor must offset the lath for ditching. Contractor must verify that
no marking stakes have been lost.
After lowering-in the trench shall be backfilled as soon as practical. The initial backfill operation, shading
of the pipe, shall be performed by backhoes fitted with cleanup buckets or an alternate process
approved by Company.
Contractor shall make all reasonable efforts to sort shading material from the trench spoil. Backfill
material within one hundred and fifty (150) millimetres of the pipe shall be reasonably well graded, with
a maximum particle size of forty (40) millimetres. The remainder of backfill material acceptable to
Company may be placed back in the trench using hoes, Mormon boards or other equipment as
approved by Company.



                                              Page 118 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                           OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Extreme care shall be taken in backfilling the trench to prevent damage to the pipe coating. No rock,
large clods, frozen backfill, or other hard spoil material that could cause such damage shall be dropped
on the coated pipe.
After three hundred (300) millimetres of cover material has been placed over the pipe, inclusions of
some rock or large clods may then occur in the backfill, provided that:
           This backfill with the inclusions remains reasonably well graded to a maximum particle size
            of three hundred (300) millimetres, with only an occasional, randomly placed particle of
            greater than three hundred (300) millimetres in size; and
           In cultivated land and land under hay production, there shall be no such inclusions in the
            uppermost three hundred (300) millimetres of backfill to grade (as measured prior to
            replacement of topsoil).
Large rocks or boulders not meeting the requirements of this Specification or otherwise unacceptable to
Company for placement back in the trench shall be disposed of in accordance with the clean-up
requirements of this Attachment B-2.4 – Construction Specifications.
When Contractor is unable to practically sort acceptable shading material from the trench spoil and as
approved by Company, pipe protection shall be provided in accordance with this Attachment B-2.4 –
Construction Specifications.
Backfill compaction at road crossings, pipeline crossings, stream and river crossings, irrigated lands,
valve sites and station sites will require a greater level of compaction as detailed on the Drawings or
elsewhere of this Specification.
Contractor is advised that on Crown owned lands, the construction of a peaked roach will be required
on winter and summer construction projects. The roach reduces or eliminates the potential for trench
subsidence that can result in erosion, siltation of water courses, and washouts that risk pipe integrity.
The roach also greatly reduces the need for re-entry on the ROW to perform warranty work.
On winter projects the peaked roach size will be a minimum of one (1) metre high to a maximum of two
(2) metres depending on trench width, depth, and inclusion of frost, and snow in the trench spoil. The
base of the roach must be at least one half (0.5) metres wider than the trench. The minimum roach size
in any given location will be at the discretion of Company Representative. The height is measured after
USM replacement. At bell hole locations the peak of the roach may be packed flat at the discretion of
the Company Representative.
On summer projects in Crown owned lands the peaked roach size will be a minimum of 0.8 metres to a
maximum of 1.6 metres. The base of the roach must be at least 0.5 metres wider than the trench. The
minimum roach size in any given location will be at the discretion of the Company Representative. The
height is measured after USM replacement. At bell hole locations the peak of the roach may be packed
flat at the discretion of Company Representative.
Roaches will be constructed initially with clay, and completed by pushing USM into both sides of the
peaked roach to cover the clay. It is expected that the USM will form up to thirty percent (30%) of the
completed peaked roach height.
To enable accurate placement of the roach the Contractor must take the following actions: After trench
excavation, before backfill, the contractor must appoint a representative with the appropriate abilities,



                                             Page 119 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                            OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


to place offset stakes indicating the distance to the center of the ditch at fifty (50) metre intervals on
straight ROW sections, and at ten (10) metre intervals on side bends and other infection points. The
offset stakes must be placed outside of spoil and USM stockpiles. The position of the roach peak must
be verified by the contractor after roach formation. Deviations in excess of one half (0.5) metres must
be repaired prior to the acceptance of cleanup progress. Company will audit roach placement but
Contractor is not to use the process to place the roach.
21.2 Summer Construction
Contractor is advised that during summer construction, an enhanced awareness of backfill procedures
to mitigate ditch subsidence will be scrutinized by Company, Land Owners and other Authorities.
During summer construction, once there is a minimum of ninety (90) centimetres of trench spoil placed
over the pipe Contractor shall compact each lift by “track packing” the trench line with a grader or piece
of equipment suitable to Company for achieving compaction of the trench spoil. Contractor shall ensure
that the equipment chosen is compatible with the soil conditions and depth of cover to ensure that the
geometry of the pipe is not negatively impacted.
All remaining trench spoil shall be backfilled in lifts of thirty (30) centimetres in thickness to minimize
the risk of future trench line settlement. Contractor shall compact each of these lifts by “track packing”.
Compaction of the trench line shall not occur in rocky soil conditions or in areas of wet ground
conditions (muskeg or swamp areas) that will compromise the integrity of the pipe.
Contractor shall submit a Trench Compaction Plan to Company at time of Bid outlining how he intends
to execute the work to achieve the required level of compaction. Compaction may include graders and
or other mechanical compaction equipment. The Trench Compaction Plan as a minimum must address
the following:
           The type of compaction equipment that Contractor plans to use;
           The method of compacting the trench spoil; and
           The method of confirming achieved compaction results are compatible with existing soil
            conditions adjacent to the ROW, to the satisfaction of Company.
NOTE: If adequate compaction is not achievable due to dry soil conditions, Company will request
Contractor to provide a water truck and a suitable spray system to water trench spoil as it is returned to
the trench. Contractor will be reimbursed in accordance with Schedule C – Commercial Terms.
Excess soil remaining from the trench after compaction work is completed to the satisfaction of
Company and the Authorities Having Jurisdiction shall be spread uniformly across the stripped portion of
the ROW and feathered to the existing grade. No crown will be allowed in agricultural lands. This will
prevent the surfacing of clay during the cultivation of the ROW.
All costs associated with backfilling and compaction of the trench and confirming these compaction
results in accordance with the above (other than the provision of water when requested by Company),
shall be included in the Base Lay Price.
Crown height at any given location will be dependent on land use and as directed by Company.
Contractor shall be responsible for damage to pipe or pipe coating resulting from compaction of the
backfill.



                                              Page 120 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                            OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Where spoil is stockpiled on prairie sod or other unstripped surfaces, the bottom fifteen (15) cm of this
stockpile shall be moved carefully to ensure damage does not occur to the sod layer and such that
scalping and deposition is minimal..
Under no circumstances will topsoil be used for backfill material and extreme caution shall be exercised
by Contractor to ensure that mixing of topsoil and subsoil does not occur. Topsoil shall be replaced
subsequently in a separate operation when the stripped portion of the ROW has been prepared to
Company's satisfaction.
Berms, furrows and terraces shall be constructed across the ROW as necessary to divert the flow of
water away from the backfilled trench and into natural drainage courses to prevent excess erosion along
the pipe prior to final clean-up. Terraces, levees, and water courses shall be restored to their former
condition to function as originally intended.
Contractor shall maintain the backfilling operation within forty-eight (48) hours of lowered-in pipe, and
in accordance with the open trench time requirements of this Attachment B-2.4 – Construction
Specifications. The backfill shall be maintained against sloughing and wash outs by Contractor until the
completion and final acceptance of the Work as provided for in the Contract Documents.
21.3 Winter Construction
Contractor is advised that under winter conditions, accurate placement of backfill materials that
overflow the trench is highly important. The contractor must take steps to verify the positions of
roached material in relation to the actual trench path.
22.0 Clean-Up
22.1 General
On Crown owned treed land under winter conditions where the ability to re-access the ROW will be
difficult or would result in undue environmental disturbance, final cleanup will be attempted. This will
include, but is not limited to:
           full grade replacements;
           roaching the ditchline to a height of one (1) metre in regular ditch areas and up to two (2)
            metres in areas of extra depth and / or width ditch;
           full bank replacements at all water crossings with required stabilization;
           even redistribution of USM including pushing into the sides of the roach;
           construction of permanent sized berms and placement of silt fence;
           placement of rollback for access and erosion control;
           restoration of all access created for the Project;
           seeding of key areas;
           placement of warning signs and posts as per a special frozen ground procedure.
Where cleanup is being attempted under frozen conditions all grade cut surfaces must be ripped away
from the ditchline to improve the bond with replaced grade materials and reduce the potential for the
materials to shift or slump.
On lands with the potential for cultivation – No topsoil will be replaced after the onset of frost to any
degree. Contractor is advised that it is impossible to compact frost infused soil to a degree that will
guarantee the ditchline will not subside at a later date. The decision to suspend topsoil replacement


                                              Page 121 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                          OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


during summer to winter seasonal transition will be made by Company. Suspension of topsoil
replacement will not result in any additional costs to Company.
In lands with the potential for cultivation, summer clean-up of winter construction will not be allowed
before June 22.
Where winter conditions necessitated a narrow topsoil stripping width, secondary stripping will be
performed during summer final clean up to a width that will sufficiently feather out the spoil displaced
by pipe diameter. No subsoil crown will be left in place following final cleanup on cultivated land.
Included in the Base Lay price, the contractor must rip the construction surface where topsoil has been
stripped, and Company has identified that the potential for compaction exists. Depth will be variable
depending on conditions and soils.
Contractor shall commence clean-up operations as soon as practical after backfill but in no case later
than seven (7) days behind backfill. Contractor shall dedicate adequate equipment to the clean-
up operation to maintain the rate of productivity identified in the final construction schedule accepted
by Company for the Work.
Prior to cleanup operations commencing, a meeting shall be held between Company and all Contractor
key personnel involved in cleanup work to discuss specific requirements of the Contract Documents and
Land Owner.
Contractor shall restore the construction ROW, all access roads and all of the sites used throughout the
Project equivalent to their original condition to the complete satisfaction of Company, Land Owner and
tenant and the Authorities Having Jurisdiction. As a minimum, this operation shall include removal of
compaction, discing, harrowing and rock picking after clean-up and topsoil replacement is completed.
Where the pipeline has crossed yards or driveways, the yards and driveways shall be finished to the
complete satisfaction of Company, Land Owner.
In areas where grading was required, Contractor shall reinstate these areas to the original contour,
unless otherwise approved by Company. On private lands, stripped subsoil surface must be final
contoured with a grader.
In areas where subsoil or topsoil is stockpiled on undisturbed sod, the equipment working the last
fifteen (15) centimetres of these soils over the sod shall be fitted with a cleanup bucket or Company
approved equivalent to minimize scalping of the sod layer.
At stripped locations on the working side where subsoil compaction is measurably greater than that of
adjacent subsoil (as tested by a hand penetrometer), Contractor shall relieve the hardness by ripping the
subsoil to a minimum depth of 30 cm or as directed by Company to a depth required to break-up subsoil
compaction with a multi-shanked ripper or other equipment as approved by Company.
In cultivated land and hay land where topsoil has not been stripped, measurably greater subsoil
compaction shall be relieved by paratiller, or Company approved equivalent. Company shall identify
these locations with survey stakes appropriately marked.
Where topsoil has not been stripped, compaction will not be relieved on a speculative basis. This is to
prevent unnecessary admixing caused by the tilling with the topsoil in place. If vegetation or crop
growth is affected the following year, contractor will be required to relieve the subsoil compaction at
that time using a paratiller or equivalent. Work is to be included in the Base Lay price.

PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                            OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT

ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


On cultivated land, hay land and bush land, prior to topsoil return, Contractor shall pick all rocks ten (10)
centimetres in size and greater. Disposal of rocks shall be in accordance with the requirements of this
Specification, as described below.
Contractor shall also collect all debris remaining from construction, clearing debris and survey stakes
and ribbons. This material shall be disposed of at a landfill site or to the satisfaction of Company and the
Authorities Having Jurisdiction.
Unless directed otherwise by Company, all temporary access along the ROW shall be removed and
cleaned up to the satisfaction of Company and Land Owner or tenant. This shall include the removal of
geo textile or rip rap used for ramping wet areas, and the removal of all culverts and bridges. On private
lands, no topsoil is to be replaced until a Company Representative has approved the subsoil surface as
ready.
Once the original grade has been restored and the subsoil has been prepared to a condition acceptable
to Company, which will include levelling, rock picking and removal of any underlying compaction, the
topsoil shall be replaced. Upper surface material or topsoil salvaged during ROW preparation shall be
spread evenly across the area it was salvaged from during clean-up.
On projects located on Crown owned lands, where a roach is being constructed, the Contractor has the
discretion of placing USM stripped from the ditch line, on the work side of the ROW beside the trench,
or on either edge of the ROW. Where USM has been removed from the full width of the ROW to allow
for grading, the contractor has the discretion of placing the USM on either or both edges of the ROW. In
all cases the contractor must understand the requirements to evenly redistribute the USM on both sides
of the ditch line and into both sides of the peaked roach. This may involve transfer of USM over the
roach with backhoes, or if bulldozers are used, reforming of the roach after USM transfer.
Contractor shall return the transition layer evenly across the area of the ROW where topsoil was
previously stripped, as a separate operation prior to replacement of topsoil.
Topsoil removed during grading operations shall be returned and restored to a condition as close to the
original as practical. Every effort shall be made to return topsoil to those areas from which it was
originally removed.
To avoid structure damage or loss of topsoil, replacement shall only take place when the topsoil is not
excessively wet or frozen and not drifting in the presence of strong winds, all as determined by Company
The following procedures shall be followed during the replacement of topsoil:
           Any excess ditch material remaining following the compaction of the ditchline and in excess
            of an acceptable crown height shall be feathered out over the stripped area;
           Following the replacement, compaction and feathering of the ditch soil material (and any
            required rock picking in accordance with this Specification), the topsoil shall be replaced
            over the previously stripped areas;
           On cultivated land, hay land and bush land, rocks shall be removed from the topsoil to a
            condition consistent with the adjacent land, and as a minimum all rocks ten (10) centimetres
            in size and larger shall be removed; and
           Where the topsoil material is stored on native or improved pasture or hay land, care shall be
            taken to ensure that the unprotected sod material is left in an undisturbed state.

On cultivated land, unstripped topsoil on the work side will be paratilled or as approved by Company to
alleviate compaction, where compaction greater than that of the adjacent soil is evident.
All terraces, levees, and watercourses shall be restored to their former condition to the satisfaction of
Company so that they will function as originally intended.
In sloping terrain, to prevent erosion of soil disturbed by construction and to direct surface water from
the ROW, and as part of clean-up activities, Contractor shall properly construct diversion berms across
the slopes in accordance with the Appendix B-1 Drawings, in keeping with good pipeline clean-
up practices and at locations agreed to between Contractor and Company. Where paralleling
other ROWs, the diversion berms shall generally complement existing berms presently in place and
trench breaker. In general, new berms will not direct flow onto another company’s ROW.
Excess trench spoil during winter construction shall be centered and roached evenly over the trench to
allow for settlement of fill during spring break up; breaks shall be left in the crown at obvious drainages
in accordance with the environmental conditions.
Where indicated on the Drawings and where woody debris has been salvaged from the clearing
operation, Contractor shall “roll back” and spread salvaged material across the ROW. Roll back may be
requested as access control, slope stabilization or to support reclamation activities.
Contractor shall install other drainage, erosion or sediment control devices, such as silt fences or
sediment traps as required to control run-off from entering watercourses or private properties.
Contractor shall maintain these devices during the warranty period to ensure they are working
effectively. In forested areas, logs removed from vehicle watercourse crossings are to be placed on the
banks and approach slopes parallel to the watercourse on both sides of the water course and on both
sides of the roach.


Disposal of surplus rock or boulders shall be performed with the agreement of Company, Land Owner
and/or tenant and the Authorities Having Jurisdiction in one of the following manners:
           The surplus rock or boulders may be buried with a minimum of two (2) metres of cover in
            locations not suitable for cultivation as agreed to in writing by the Land Owner. Locations
            where additional native prairie disturbance would be required are not acceptable;
           Contractor shall obtain and supply Company with a copy of written permission outlining the
            conditions for disposal of rock on their property from Land Owner or occupant; and
           If the Land Owner requests that the surplus rock or boulders be removed from his property,
            Contractor shall haul the surplus material to an approved dump site. Contractor shall
            provide in writing to Company the approval of all provincial and municipal Authorities
            Having Jurisdiction over occur. All environmental and safety concerns as outlined in the
            Contract Documents shall apply to all such off site work.
Disposal of rock and boulders remaining from the backfill operation and clean up shall be at no
additional compensation to Contractor.
Prior to any caliper pigging or pressure testing of a section of pipeline, earthwork over the new pipeline
shall be done only when approved by Company and using equipment and following procedures

approved by Company. This shall be limited to a 14G grader, or a dozer with equal or less weight

After either caliper pigging or pressure testing, the pipeline shall be considered an operating buried

If Contractor attempts to perform clean-up operations during adverse weather or wet ground

be cleaned up immediately after the completion of testing.

           Install erosion control devices as required to minimize the potential for erosion in areas

           Ensure that access roads and trails are graded and left in a condition acceptable to Land

Any clean-up not completed before freeze-up shall be finalized the following summer, once
ROW conditions permit, at times acceptable to Land Owners and tenants, and complying with
environmental timing restrictions. Contractor is advised that various timing restrictions in
environmentally sensitive areas will be in place during the spring and early summer.
If clean-up activities occur during a season following pipeline construction, Contractor shall work with
Company’s land agents to address Land Owner concerns such as accessibility to fields, sunken trench
and flooding. The cost for these activities will be Contractor’s responsibility, regardless of the clean-
up season.
All costs associated with clean-up and maintenance of the ROW within the warranty period shall be
included in the Base Lay Price.
22.2 Reclamation & Revegetation
22.2.1 General
Contractor will be responsible for hand broadcast seeding of all road and railway crossing bar ditches,
water crossing banks and approach slopes to water courses at a rate of twenty-five(25) kg/ha. For steep
non-cultivated slopes and banks of water crossings, Contractor shall also apply a cover crop such as fall
rye at a rate of forty-five (45) kg/ha. Company will advise on seed type and final locations for seeding.

Where practical seed shall be raked in or lightly harrowed to cover seed.

22.2.2 Bank Restoration
Contractor shall provide all equipment and labour to restore stream banks to represent the original
contours, unless otherwise approved by Company.
When requested by Company to install geogrid structures with willow and other shrub cuttings

structure is installed, to review the installation procedure.
22.2.3 Fences
Upon completion of all clean up and reclamation of the Site, Contractor shall make final repairs to
fences and other enclosures. New and like new material shall be used in making these repairs.
Structures shall be placed in a condition as good as, or better than those encountered at the beginning
of the construction. Contractor shall furnish and install new pressure treated or cedar posts of equal or
greater diameter than the posts which were previously removed or damaged (painting of posts not
required). Contractor shall furnish and install steel, concrete or specially constructed posts wherever
necessary to match the fence construction of the Land Owner. All fence repairs shall be in accordance
with any special requirements of the Line Lists and as approved by Company, Land Owner and tenant.
At each road crossing boundary where no fence exists, Contractor shall supply and install a post on each
side of the pipeline on each boundary line. Each post shall be one hundred (100) millimetre diameter
and one and a half (1.5) metres long.
Existing fence posts damaged by Contractor during the execution of the Work shall be replaced, re-
installed or repaired at no additional compensation to Contractor.
22.2.4 Clean-Up Acknowledgements
Following the completion of the clean-up and final repair of fences for any respective property and after
Company's general approval of such cleanup, Contractor shall work jointly with Company’s Land Agent
to obtain a signed acknowledgement satisfactory to Company from all private Land Owners and all
occupants. The acknowledgement will confirm that the Land Owner is satisfied with Contractor's clean-
up. Contractor shall submit a copy of this release form to Company for approval four (4) weeks in
advance of final cleanup work commencing.
All land negotiations must be with Company and Company’s land agent present and all agreements
documented, with a copy to Company.
Contractor shall obtain a signed release from any Authorities Having Jurisdiction over public facilities,
used or crossed, acknowledging that the clean-up work has been completed to their satisfaction.
Contractor shall notify Company when it is prepared to obtain such acknowledgements and releases to
allow Company's representative to be present when these are to be obtained. However, the written

22.3 Signs
Contractor shall install warning sign posts and sign plates at all highway, railway and municipal roads

Warning sign assemblies shall be located at easily visible locations near ROW, boundaries, fence lines or

Company, and generally spaced about ten (10) kilometres apart in accordance with the Drawings.
