repaired at no additional compensation to Contractor.
Installation of posts and signs under winter conditions may require a special procedure to minimize the
potential for fall down.
23.0 Internal Cleaning & Inspection
23.1 Construction Pigging
In order that the completed pipe line shall be delivered to Company free from water, dirt, debris,
animals and other foreign objects and also free of defective workmanship such as welding icicles, a
construction cleaning pig furnished and maintained by Contractor shall be run through the entire
pipeline not to exceed the maximum hydrostatic test section length once sections have been lowered-
in and backfilled and prior to filling with water. Contractor shall provide Company, for approval, the
manufacturer’s technical data for the construction cleaning pig it intends to use for this work. This pig
shall be propelled by compressed air furnished by Contractor with a maximum pressure of one hundred
(100) kilopascals. A pressure gauge (0-350 kPa) shall be installed on the launching head.
If in the opinion of Company, all foreign material has not been removed by one running of the cleaning
pig, additional runs shall be made by Contractor until Company accepts that the pipeline is free of all
foreign material.




                                             Page 127 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                           OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Launching and receiving heads or traps shall be attached to the pipe by way of a complete weld by a
qualified welder approved for welding on the Project. All heads or traps required for cleaning shall be
furnished by Contractor and subject to the approval of Company.
Contractor shall provide Company with sufficient notice prior to commencing the running of any pig
through the pipeline. The pig(s) shall not be inserted or removed from any section of the pipeline except
in the presence of the Company.
The rubber discs and wire brushes shall be measured prior to each run of the construction pig to ensure
they are adequate to apply sufficient pressure on the pipe walls to provide effective cleaning of the pipe
walls. When the pig becomes damaged and in the opinion of the Company, the rubber discs or wire
brushes have become excessively worn or distorted, they shall be replaced with new discs or wire
brushes furnished by Contractor, at no additional compensation to Contractor.
After a section of pipeline has been cleaned and the tie-in at such time is impractical, the cleaned
section shall be night capped in the presence of Company. Night caps shall not be removed for tie-
in welding except when Company is present. The nightcap shall be waterproof to ensure no water or
debris enters the pipeline should the possibility of water exist at the tie-in location.
If the pig becomes lodged in the pipeline, attempts shall be made to move it by increasing the air
pressure. The pressure shall not normally be increased beyond one hundred and fifty (150) kilopascals. If
the pig remains lodged, the pig shall be searched for and the backfill removed as required. If the
presence of water is determined by Company to be the cause of the block, Company may authorize
higher pressures to facilitate movement of the water. In such a case, Company may require the pressure
to be released and a dewatering line to be installed at the downstream receiving head, satisfactory to
Company. A cleaning pig that cannot be dislodged using this procedure shall be cut-out and the pipeline
repaired by Contractor, at no additional compensation to Contractor. Upon completion of a repair a
construction pig shall be run again. The pig shall be removed from the line following completion of the
successful run.
23.2 Caliper Pigging
After completion of hydrostatic testing and prior to the installation of valve assemblies, Contractor shall
run a Company supplied Caliper pig propelled by compressed air. Company will provide a qualified
Caliper Pig Technician to maintain the pig and provide direction to Contractor regarding the handling
and running of the pig and interpretation of results.
Contractor shall furnish support services including all labour, supervision, supplies, materials, equipment
and instrumentation including any temporary launching and receiving traps required to perform one run
of the Caliper pig through the completed sections of the pipeline.
The Caliper pig shall not be run in conjunction with other pig runs.
Should an inconclusive chart be produced, due to any negligence on the part of Contractor including but
not limited to debris or ice in the line or inappropriate tool speed as specified by the Caliper Pig
Technician the Caliper pig shall be rerun entirely at Contractor’s expense, including Caliper Pig vendor
daily costs, until a satisfactory run is achieved. Contractor shall use compressors adequate in size and
number to run the pig at approximately five (5) to eight (8) kilometres per hour while holding one
hundred (100) kilopascals back pressure. This pressure shall be maintained during the entire pig run by
regulating the discharge rate of the blowdown valve at the downstream end of the section. Final back


                                             Page 128 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                            OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


pressure requirements and maximum length of section to be caliper pigged at one time shall be as
recommended by the Caliper Pig Technician.
Contractor shall provide and install working gauges of a suitable scale on either end of the section being
pigged.
The maximum allowable pipe defects shall be as specified in CSA Z662, and the requirements of
Pembina specification ESS 2.15 - Post Construction Inspection (ILI) of new pipelines technical
specification.
If the analysis of the Caliper pig run, as determined by the Caliper Pig Technician, shows indications of
pipe defects exceeding these allowable limits, Contractor shall locate and correct the defects and the
Caliper pig shall be rerun the satisfaction of Company, all at no additional compensation to Contractor.
The maximum length of a section that the Caliper pig shall be run through is approximately forty (40)
km, and subject to the Caliper Pig Technicians final approval.
24.0 Hydrostatic Testing
24.1 General
No test shall be conducted unless approved by Company and Company is on site.
Contractor shall provide the Company with seventy (72) hours (week-days only) notice of any hydrotest.
Company shall inform the applicable Provincial regulator (AER/OGC), or other Authorities Having
Jurisdiction of the test. At no time shall a test begin until the proper notifications have been provided to
the Authorities Having Jurisdiction.
All pressure testing shall be performed in accordance with this Attachment B-24 – Construction
Specifications. Company will provide Contractor with information, procedures and Drawings, indicating
pressure restrictions associated with differences in elevation and the corresponding minimum and
maximum test pressures.
All testing equipment, instruments test trailer, safety procedures, test procedures and test records shall
conform to the applicable standard in this specification. Contractor accepts all responsibility for the
accuracy of the test instrumentation used. Company reserves the right to require Contractor to replace
any instrumentation that is malfunctioning.
For hydrostatic test purposes, a minimum of twenty (20) metres of heavy-wall pipe, of sufficient wall
thickness to limit hoop stress to ninety percent (90%) SMYS during hydrostatic testing, as determined by
Company, shall be installed by Contractor between the test head and the pipeline. This pipe can be
permanently installed in the pipeline.

Contractor shall submit a detailed written testing plan to Company at least thirty (30) days prior to
commencement of testing, for approval, and for Company’s submission for approval by Authorities
Having Jurisdiction. See Attachment A-2.9 Hydrotest Plan for more information. Contractor shall supply
water volumes and water withdrawal and discharge locations six (6) weeks prior to test. This plan shall
contain all procedures, equipment and manpower proposed for use in testing of the pipeline, including
but not limited to the following:

          Piping schematics for testing of all fabricated assemblies;
          A detailed section-by-section procedure and schedule for filling and testing, including intake
           screening and water withdrawal rates, where applicable;
          A schematic diagram of the test equipment set-up with sizes, capacities, numbers and
           locations of equipment, including water heaters if used;
          A sketch showing the proposed layout of the test site ( including test shack/test facility);
          Backpressure to be maintained during the filling operation;
          Safety procedures;
          Types and number of pigs to be used for filling, dewatering and drying;
          The method of leak detection, and repair procedures in case of leak, including a listing of
           equipment available to make repairs;
          Method and location of water disposal and discharge rates, where applicable;
          A list of all test personnel, their testing qualifications and positions;
          Winter testing procedures, including heating of water, hoarding/heating of test points,
           protecting recorders and recorder hoses from freezing etc.; and
          A list of all testing instrumentation used with copies of appropriate certifications, i.e.,
           Calibration, Manufacturer, etc.
24.3 Test Instrumentation Provided by Contractor
Minimum Instrumentation for each test section shall be as follows:
          Twenty four (24) hour Pressure Recorders, zero (0) to eighteen thousand (18,000)
           kilopascals, three hundred and five (305) millimetre diameter chart, accuracy to plus or
           minus one percent (± 1%) of full scale:
          Deadweight Tester, zero (0) to eighteen thousand (18,000) kilopascals, accuracy to plus or
           minus one hundredth of a percent (± 0.01%) of indicated pressure c/w weight increments to
           five (5) kilopascals. Digital deadweights shall not be permitted;
          Twenty four (24) hour Temperature Recorders, dual probe, minus thirty degrees (-30°)
           Celsius to fifty degrees (50°) Celsius, three hundred and five (305) millimetre diameter chart,
           accuracy to plus or minus one percent (± 1%) of full scale;
          Ambient Thermometers, minus thirty degrees (-30°) Celsius to fifty degrees (50°) Celsius,
           accuracy to plus or minus two percent (± 2%) of full scale;
          Water Meter, accuracy to plus or minus five tenths of a percent (± 0.5%);
          Stroke Counter, accuracy to plus or minus five tenths of a percent (± 0.5%);
          Pressure Gauges as required at each test head;
          Container Graduated in millilitres for accurately measuring the volume of liquid added or
           removed from the test;
          Supply of Charts for Pressure and Temperature Recorders; and
          All recorders shall have disposable fiber-tip pens.
Contractor shall have a backup set of certified deadweights and pressure and temperature recorders in
the event of equipment malfunction.

Contractor to replace any instrumentation that is malfunctioning.

A back-up pressure recorder will be installed either on the test facility or connected to the test head
directly.

As a minimum Contractor shall supply the items as indicated below; further requirements are included
in Appendix A-4 Contractor Supplied materials.
           All pigs except for Caliper pig;
           Water fill pump with a minimum capacity to permit continuous filling at a rate in the order
            of seven thousand (7,000) litres per minute. When water is withdrawn from a fish bearing

            for the Temporary Diversion of Water for Hydrostatic Testing of Pipelines.
           Boiler and circulating equipment; and

            pressure and temperature recorders. To assure stabilization of the test instruments, the test
            building shall be skidded solidly to the ground at all times during operation of the test
            instruments. The test facility shall be of adequate design to accommodate four (4)
            Company/Company personnel to witness the hydrostatic test operations. Converted school

24.5 Contractor Personnel
Contractor’s testing supervisor shall be responsible for direct supervision and the performance of the
testing.
Unless otherwise approved writing by Company, Contractor shall supply at least four (4) experienced
employees at each test site during the pressuring stage of the test, including but not limited to:
           Contractor’s Testing Supervisor;
           Pump Operator; and
           Fitter.
Unless otherwise approved in writing by Company, Contractor shall supply at least two (2) responsible
employees per test section to be on site during the entire test period to assist in recording the necessary
test readings and periodically check the test heads and valves for leaks.
24.6 Safety Procedures

Contractor shall erect warning signs at all access points to the ROW, at all public crossings, and at all
points where there is exposed pipe or appurtenances as follows:
           Contractor shall maintain regular patrol of all public crossings for the duration of the entire
            test period including the pressuring period for pressures above fifty percent (50%) of the

           All pumps, pressure recorders, deadweight testers and test buildings shall be located at

            of darkness.
           Hoses, regardless of pressure rating, shall not be used for connections between the pump
            and the test assembly.
24.7 Test Medium
24.7.1 General
Water shall be used as the test medium. No chemical additives to the test water are permitted unless
otherwise approved by Company.
Water containing silt or suspended material shall not be used unless it can be treated satisfactorily by
the use of filters.
24.7.2 Water Sources
Company will make arrangements for water withdrawal permits for those water sources identified in
Attachment A-2.3 – Water Source Locations. For any additional water withdrawal sources, Contractor
shall provide sufficient notification, (minimum six (6) weeks) to Company for the acquisition of water
withdrawal permits. Company will make all reasonable efforts to acquire additional water withdrawal
sources at the request of the Contractor.
Contractor is responsible for examination of Company suggested water sources, and identification of
alternative and new water sources. Dugouts, existing wells, lakes, ponds, rivers, and streams are all
potential sources. Contractor is advised that the old exemption of five thousand (5000) cubic meters
without a specific permit, under an issued development disposition such as a PLA, no longer exists.
Company will obtain the regulatory permits for hydrostatic testing and other general water use, based
on information supplied by the contractor. Company does not guarantee the regulatory approval or
amount of water under an approval. Delays in obtaining permits will not result in any extra cost
submissions to Company. Therefore, as much lead time as possible in water source identification is
recommended. Contractor must prove the consideration of this responsibility in the bid process.

24.8 Line Filling
All valves and appurtenances must be checked prior to filling the pipeline to ensure that they are in
proper working order. Fittings must be checked for tightness before filling. New gaskets shall be used.
Fill pumps and associated fuel tanks located within one hundred (100) meters of a water body shall be
placed within an impermeable ground enclosure to prevent hydraulic and/or fuel leaks from entering
the water body. Any leaks or spills shall be cleaned up and disposed of before the enclosure is removed
and the site restored.
Fill equipment shall be sufficient to permit continuous filling at a rate in the order of seven thousand
(7,000) litres per minute. The fill rate actually used at any location shall be satisfactory to Company and
any Authorities Having Jurisdiction. The withdrawal rate of water shall be in accordance with the water


                                             Page 134 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                             OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


withdrawal permits and shall not exceed permitted rates as per the withdrawal authorization (typically
ten percent (10%) of the total flow of the source), or in sloughs and lakes, the volume of water removed
shall not affect shoreline or nesting habitat.
The water intake shall be located at a depth that will not permit air to be drawn in with the water and
shall be screened in accordance with the requirements of any Authorities Having Jurisdiction but, in any
case, the screen shall have a mesh opening no greater than one (1) square centimetre.
When filling any section, a Company-approved bi-directional pig must be run immediately in front of the
water. An air pressure that will create sufficient backpressure to prevent the fill pig from breaking away
from the column of water shall be held in front of the filling pig during the entire fill operation.
Contractor shall provide Company with forty eight (48) hours advance notice prior to commencing filling
operations.
At least twenty-four (24) hours prior to filling the line with water, Contractor shall install the
temperature recorders. A dual probe temperature recorder is required at each end of a test section.
One probe is to be attached to the pipe insulated from the adjacent soil and backfilled at a location
specified by Company but not less than one hundred (100) metres from the end of the backfilled section
of pipe. The second temperature probe is to be installed to record the ground temperature one hundred
and fifty (150) millimetres from the pipe and at the same depth as the pipe. An additional dual probe
recorder shall be similarly installed near the center of any test section longer than ten (10) kilometres.
All three recorders shall be operating at least one (1) day prior to filling and shall continue to be
operated until the end of the test. A maximum of thirty six (36) hour test duration shall be shown on one
chart unless otherwise approved by Company. Temperature test charts shall be replaced on all
Temperature Recorders prior to commencement of pressure test.
Contractor shall provide Company with two (2) source water samples of the water body from which any
water is withdrawn. One sample shall be taken a minimum of one (1) week prior to testing and another
sample shall be taken at the time of water withdrawal for testing. Contractor shall arrange for any
required testing of the water.
Contractor will provide Company sufficient information and documentation for each water source to
enable Company to obtain water withdrawal permits. Contractor shall abide by all restrictions or
regulations contained in these permits. All costs associated with the use of water source locations
including access development and withdrawal equipment shall be assumed by Contractor.
The temporary piping to the fill point shall include a water meter. A recording pressure gauge shall be
installed at the fill point, both for the purpose of estimating the location of the fill pig and the total
volume of fill water used. This piping shall also include a mechanical type filter that will remove all solids
exceeding six and one-half (6.5) millimetres in diameter, or as deemed necessary by the water
withdrawal permit. A check valve shall be installed at the point where the fill pump discharge piping is
tied into the pipeline. The filling operations shall be continuous on an around the clock basis.
Contractor shall ensure that all mainline valves which form part of the test section shall be in the fully
open position during the filling operation and partially closed for the duration of the test to ensure the
valve body is exposed to the full hydrostatic test pressure. Note: valve assemblies will not normally be
permitted to be installed prior to completion of hydrostatic testing of the pipeline.
24.9 Testing Procedure


                                              Page 135 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                               OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


24.9.1 Test Heads
Contractor will provide test heads in accordance with Appendix A-3 - Contractor Supplied Materials.
Contractor shall construct any additional test heads it requires in accordance with the Drawings and
Specifications.
Contractor shall provide Company with full documentation of test heads provided by Contractor. This
documentation shall include material traceability and previous test pressures. Prior to use for
hydrostatic testing on the Project, Contractor provided test heads shall be subjected to a one hour hydro
test at a pressure 1.25 times greater than the highest test pressure of the pipeline system.
Prior to testing, all welds joining test heads to the test section must be radiographed. Except for the tie-
in weld, welding on test heads is prohibited. Immediately after testing, the test heads shall be removed
from piping and pigs removed to the satisfaction of Company.
Contractor shall remove all auxiliary pipe pups from the ends of the test heads unless otherwise
approved by Company. Pups remaining on test heads must be identifiable by a manufacturer pipe and
heat number, wall thickness, and grade.
24.10 Hydrostatic Testing Requirements
Contractor shall test all pipeline sections in accordance with CSA Z662 to pressures and durations as
provided by Company. Company will provide elevations at high points and low points of the test section
and pressures shall be calculated by Company once Contractor has completed installation for each
section.
Contractor shall, prior to installation, also pre-test certain water crossing pipe sections, and pull-
through sections of drilled crossings, as described in Schedule A - Scope of Work and in Appendix B-1-
Drawings for the water crossings. Such pre-tests shall be in accordance with the requirements for testing
fabricated assemblies included in this specification, except that only a one (1) hour test is required.
Pressurizing to test pressure shall be done in daylight hours only unless otherwise approved by
Company.
24.11 Test
Prior to starting the test, all fittings shall be checked for tightness. Bull plugs and blind flanges shall be
installed except where gauges, recorders, or pumps are to be connected. The pressure pump and
connections must be checked before the test commences to ensure that they are capable of
withstanding the pressure to which they will be subjected. A check valve shall be installed between the
test head and the piping from the pressure pump as close as practical to the test head.
Pressure gauges shall be installed on each test head prior to starting the testing operation.
Contractor to ensure temperature recorders are installed in accordance with this Attachment B-2.4 –
Construction Specifications prior to filling and functioning properly.
After filling the test section and then connecting the high-pressure pump, Contractor shall only pressure
the test section in the presence of Company’s testing supervisor. When specifically approved by
Company for a particular test section, Contractor may place three thousand (3,000) kilopascals of
pressure on that test section prior to Company testing supervisor arriving at the test site. Contractor
shall test all instruments and equipment prior to the hydrostatic test in the presence of Company’s


                                               Page 136 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                            OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


testing supervisor. Company’s testing supervisor shall dictate the rate of all pressuring operations when
the pressure is greater than three thousand (3,000) kilopascals
The hydrostatic testing of a section of the Pipeline shall be performed in three stages as follows:
The first stage is a leak check at approximately fifty percent (50%) of the specified minimum yield
strength (SMYS) of the pipe at the low point for a minimum period of one (1) hour to allow visual
inspections to be performed on exposed piping and fittings included in the test section. Any pressure
lost during this period must be explained to the satisfaction of Company‘s testing supervisor, prior to
continuing with Stage 2.
The second stage is a strength test with a minimum duration of four (4) hours where the test section will
be pressured to a minimum pressure of one hundred and fifty percent (150%) of intended maximum
operating pressure. The maximum test pressure at any location in the test section shall not produce a
hoop stress in excess of one hundred and ten percent (110%) of SMYS of the pipe.
The third stage is a leak test where the pressure will be reduced from the strength test pressure to a
lesser pressure, and held to maintain a minimum of one hundred and ten percent (110%) of intended
maximum operating pressure. The leak test duration shall be a minimum of four (4) hours duration.
Following satisfactory completion of the leak check, if the test pressure produces a hoop stress equal to
or greater than one hundred percent (100%) of the specified minimum yield strength of the pipe, testing
continues by raising the pressure to test pressure including making a manual yield plot. Company shall
determine which pipe requires yield plot testing.
Contractor shall ensure the following is available to make a manual yield plot:
       Pressure pump with a capacity which is capable of providing a pressure increase of forty (40)
        kilopascals to one hundred (100) kilopascals per minute or as otherwise specified by Company.
        Contractor shall ensure that the pressure pump is adequately sized for the length and diameter
        of the section to be tested.
       Digital flow meter indicating cumulative volume in cubic metres per minute or stroke counter or
        sufficient size to measure necessary volumes for the yield plot
It is essential that there is sufficient water available to complete the pressurizing to test pressure
without stopping the pump. Yield plotting shall begin as soon as practical after there-commencement of
pumping (at fifty percent (50%) of pipe SMYS), but in any event, no later than when the pressure has
been reached which develops a stress of eighty percent (80%) of the SMYS of the pipe at any point in the
test section. A constant pumping rate shall be maintained throughout this stage; however, some
adjustments will be allowed at the beginning to obtain a suitable rate. As each one hundred (100)
kilopascal increment is indicated on the deadweight tester, the deadweight attendant calls out the
pressure and the meter reader observes the cumulative volume, records the readings in tabular form,
and transfers this data to a graph of pressure versus cumulative volume. The pressure shall be plotted
vertically and preferably to a scale of twenty five (25) millimetres = four hundred (400) kilopascals. The
horizontal scale (volume) must then be adjusted to give an approximate two to one (2:1) slope to the
resulting graph.
The pressure-volume plot will form a straight line until the elastic limit of a portion of the pipe is
reached. It will then curve gradually to the right of a projected straight line. When sufficient data points
have been plotted, the straight-line portion of the plot can be extrapolated to the maximum test


                                              Page 137 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                            OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


pressure. A 0.2% offset (representing two tenths of a percent (0.2%) of the volume of the pipe section
being tested) can be drawn on the plot.
Pumping shall continue until the pressure-volume plot reaches the two tenths of a percent (0.2%) offset
line, or the maximum test pressure has been reached. The test pressure must not be allowed to exceed
either limitation. Pressure cycling shall not be used to find leaks.
After the maximum test pressure has been reached and pumping stopped, or a deviation to the two
tenths of a percent (0.2%) offset line has been reached, the four (4) hour strength test may commence.
The minimum test pressure will correspond to one hundred and fifty percent (150%) of the intended
maximum operating pressure at the high point of the pipeline. The pressure at the highpoint shall match
or exceed this minimum at both the start and the end of the strength test, and at no time during the
strength test period shall the pressure at the high point drop below ninety-seven and one-half percent
(97.5%) of this required minimum. The maximum test pressure at any point in the test section shall not
produce a hoop stress in excess of one hundred and ten percent (110%) of SMYS of the pipe at any time.
Any repressurizing shall not exceed the final pressure reading on the pressure-volume plot for the initial
pressuring of that section to test pressure.
After successful completion of the strength test the leak test will be conducted. The pressure in the test
section shall be reduced so that the maximum pressure does not produce a hoop stress in excess of one
hundred percent (100%) of SMYS of the pipe at the low point in the test section. For the leak test the
minimum at the high point shall be one hundred and ten percent (110%) of the intended maximum
operating pressure. The pressure at the high point shall match or exceed this minimum at both the start
and the end of the test. A stabilization period may be required to allow the test medium to settle out
after the bleed down. Upon completion of the strength test the pump shall be disconnected and bull
plugs and blind flanges installed where required.
A two-hour period where no drop in pressure occurs within the last four hours of the leak test is
required for a successful test. The overall duration of the test may be extended to achieve these
requirements.
The leak check, the pressurization, the stabilization period, the strength test and the leak test should all
be recorded on the same chart, provided that it is neat and that the final test does not run longer
than thirty-six (36) hours; otherwise, new pressure and temperature charts should be installed for the
final twenty-four (24) hours. The four (4) hour strength test and the final four (4) hours of the
subsequent leak test shall both be identified on the pressure chart i.e. with a hand written notation on
the chart.
24.12 Pipe Failures During Test
If any leaks or breaks occur during any of the testing operations, Contractor shall locate, repair and
retest the test section in which the failure took place. Contractor shall immediately notify Company of
all pipe failure and all suspected leaks complete with all particulars.
Leaks or breaks occurring in the pipe metal or pipe seam shall be repaired by cutting out the entire pipe
joint and replacing. If the leak or break has been caused by construction damage only and is in a straight
joint of pipe, it will not be necessary to replace the full joint or pipe; the replacement shall be as
directed by Company. Failures occurring in field bends shall be replaced with field bends of the same
degree.



                                              Page 138 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                           OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


For all leaks and breaks, an accurate record, clearly subdivided by operational time and standby time for
all supervision, labour and equipment and that quantity of materials and supplies used shall be kept
from the time the leak or break is first indicated until it has been located, repaired, refilled and re-
pressured to the same pressure at which the failure was first indicated. Records are to be submitted to
Company on a daily basis.
All pipe sections containing leaks or breaks that are cut out of the pipeline shall be handled carefully and
in accordance with the pipe manufacturer’s representatives or Company’s instructions so not to damage
the defective areas. No cuts shall be made closer than three hundred (300) millimetres to a defect. All
such cut out pipe shall be clearly marked, immediately after the removal from the ditch, with paint to
show the chainage and date of failure and edges of the defect shall be protected with grease. Defective
pipe shall be transported to Company’s warehouse as directed by Company.
Leaks or breaks occurring in the pipeline during any of the testing operations which are as a result of
defective materials or workmanship furnished by Contractor shall be located, repaired and the repaired
test sections refilled and re-pressured by Contractor at its own expense.
Leaks or breaks occurring in the pipeline during any of the testing operations which are a result of
defective permanent materials furnished by Company shall be located, repaired and the repaired test
section refilled and re-pressured to the same pressure at which the failure was first indicated to
Contractor. The work required to affect a repair and bring test section back to the status at the time of
the leak or break shall constitute Extra Work.
Contractor shall comply with the permit requirements for and have the sole responsibility for the
disposal of water at buckles, repairs, leaks and breaks, temporary manifold or scraper trap assembly or
any other tie-ins required by the testing operations. This shall be done in such a manner that the
convenience and safety of the general public is protected and in a manner satisfactory to the
responsible authorities. Any damage resulting from careless or improper disposal of water shall be to
the account of Contractor.
24.13 Pipe Identification
After each successful test, the test number and the test completion date shall be indelibly marked on
the outside of the pipe at each end of the test section and on any pipe cut off the tested section.
24.14 Test Acceptance
Contractor is responsible for holding the test for the specified test periods and until Company declares
the test acceptable. To be declared acceptable, the following conditions must be met during the test:
           There shall be no leaks, when checked in accordance with the requirements specified above;
           If the test section, during the strength test or leak test is bled down or re- pressured, the
            volume of water removed or added shall be measured to an accuracy of plus or minus two
            (± 2) litres and shall be noted on the pressure chart;
           Following any re-pressuring during the strength test or the leak test, the test section shall
            then be allowed to stabilize and the test restarted;
           Deadweight pressure readings shall be taken every fifteen (15) minutes for the first two (2)
            hours and every thirty (30) minutes for the remainder of the test period. Ambient
            temperature readings shall be taken in conjunction with the deadweight pressure readings.
           Temperature and pressure chart recorders shall be operational throughout the test.

24.15 Test Records
24.15.1 Documentation Guidelines
Legible and orderly documentation of each test shall be generated by Contractor testing supervisor with
the assistance of Company. Minimum documentation requirements for each test shall include:
           Description of the test section including pipe sizes, wall thickness changes, pipe grades,
            location of section end points and high and low point and other important elevations, and
            calculated section volume. A line diagram of the test section with pertinent information
            noted on it is acceptable;
           Start and completion times of line fill pumping, and volume of water used to fill the section.
           Start and completion times and pressure changes during the leak check;
           Tabular data and yield plot showing cumulative volume for each one hundred (100)
            kilopascal pressure increment from eighty percent (80%) of SMYS until the on test pressure
            is reached;
           Start and completion times and pressure changes during the stabilization period;
           Tabular data showing pressure observations and ambient temperature readings taken
            throughout the test period;
           The recorder models and serial number, location and test section number shall be noted on
            the back of each pressure and temperature chart. All notes on the charts shall be neat and
            legible; and
           Time and pressure when the test is declared acceptable, and time when the section
            pressure is bled down to a maximum pressure of seventeen hundred (1700) kilopascal.
           Calibration certificates for recorders and instruments used in the test.
All recorded pressures except those shown on the pressure recorder charts, shall be measured using the
deadweight tester.
Contractor’s testing supervisor shall sign original copies of all test documentation at the test site. All test
documents shall be the property of Company.
24.16 Permanent Records
The originals of each of the following documents will be retained by Company for the permanent record
files:
           Test section drawing;
           Cleaning and displacement pig run data;
           Yield plot readings;
           Yield plot graph;
           Deadweight gauge readings;
           Pressure recorder charts;
           Temperature recorder charts;

PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                             OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


           Failure reports;
           Hydrostatic test calculations; and
           Report Forms
Company’s standard report forms described herein will be used, in addition to the pressure and
temperature recorder charts, to provide a record of the tests and related activities. All reports will be
signed by Contractor’s testing Supervisor and will be given to the Company Representative.
           Cleaning and caliper pig run data; this report will be completed whenever a cleaning or
            caliper pig operation has been performed.
           Displacement pig run data; this form will be completed when a displacement operation is
            performed on a test section.
           Hydrostatic Test Calculation Sheet; Contractor’s testing supervisor will prepare this form for
            each test section to illustrate the basic calculations on which the test is based.
           Leak Test Data for Above Ground Assemblies: the deadweight gauge readings and other test
            data for each test section will be recorded on this form. Sufficient data and supplementary
            remarks shall be recorded to adequately provide for determination of acceptance or
            rejection of the test. When the test is approved the report will be signed by Company’s
            testing supervisor, Contractor’s testing supervisor and/or the applicable Provincial regulator
            (AER/OGC), (if available).
           Leak Test Data: the deadweight gauge readings and other test data for each test section will
            be recorded on this form. Sufficient data and supplementary remarks shall be recorded to
            adequately provide for determination of acceptance or rejection of the test. When the test
            is approved, the report will be signed by Company’s testing supervisor, Contractor’s testing
            supervisor and/or the applicable Provincial regulator (AER/OGC) (if available).
           Pipe Failure Report: this form will be completed for each failure that occurs during the
            testing operations on the system. The information recorded on this form will provide a
            complete record of test conditions at the time of failure and a detailed description to
            provide a documented record of any other event that occurred during testing operations.
           Yield Plot Readings; this report will be completed when a yield plot is performed for one
            hundred (100) kilopascal pressure intervals from the eighty percent (80%) of SMYS pressure
            up to the one hundred and ten percent (110%) of SMYS pressure or the pressure which gives
            a deviation to the two tenths of a percent (0.2%) offset line (pipe yield point).
           Yield Plot: as the yield plot readings are recorded, they will be transferred to a graph of
            pressure versus cumulative volume. The pressure will be plotted vertically and the volume
            (horizontal scale) must be adjusted to give an approximate two to one (2:1) slope to the
            resulting graph.
Upon completion of the testing operations, Contractor’s testing supervisor will compile a summary
report for each of the test sections of the pipeline. These reports and the originals of all test report
charts, drawings, plots and graphs, as outlined above, will be retained for permanent record files.
24.17 Depressurizing & Dewatering
Dewatering will be completed according to the requirements of the specifications, the Authorities
Having Jurisdiction and the Alberta Environment Code of Practice for the Release of Hydrostatic Test
Water from Hydrostatic Testing of a Petroleum Liquid and Gas Pipeline or the Oil and Gas Waste
Regulation under the British Columbia Environmental Management Act.


                                              Page 141 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                          OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Immediately after the test has been completed, the pressure shall be slowly released from the section
to a maximum pressure of fifteen hundred (1500) kilopascals. Care must be exercised in removing bull
plugs or blind flanges to avoid injury or damage caused by a pressure build up due to a leaking valve.
Extreme care must be taken when depressurizing. No valve larger than NPS 2 shall be used for
depressuring. Only a responsible employee of Contractor, with Contractor’s testing supervisor and
Company present, shall be permitted to open a bleed valve after the test. Valves shall be opened slowly
and the depressurization continued at a rate that does not develop severe vibrations, as determined by
Company. Any fittings that are attached to the bleed valve during depressurizing must be adequately
braced to prevent movement and shall have a pressure rating equal to or greater than the test head
pressure rating. Depressurizing devices or hoses shall not be attached to the bleed valve.
Prior to dewatering, all drain lines and the test heads to which they are attached shall be firmly tied
down and braced to prevent movement. Dewatering shall be carried out by propelling a bi-
directional pig with compressed air. Air pressure shall be reduced as the run nears completion to
minimize stored energy in the system. A minimum of two (2) runs shall be made for each test section.
The discharged water shall be filtered in accordance with the specifications.
Water disposal sites shall be selected by Contractor and approved by Company to prevent inter- basin
transfer of water. Dewatering shall be adjacent to nearby watercourses or onto vegetated upland areas
free of trees, unless otherwise approved by Company. Scour of stream banks and bed must be avoided,
and in any event discharge rates shall not exceed ten percent (10%) of the flow in any receiving stream.
Dewatering outlets will be equipped with diffusers to reduce erosion with the diffused water aimed
onto an impermeable liner, geo-fabric or equivalent. If water is discharged into a dry watercourse, the
diffused water shall be aimed onto the specified liner over temporary rock riprap or other stable surface
material to minimize soil erosion. Care shall be taken so that water is disposed of without flooding
adjacent areas. Water disposal shall be in accordance with the requirements of any Authorities Having
Jurisdiction and shall be subject to the approval of Company.
When dewatering within thirty (30) m of a water body, the discharge water shall pass through a filter of
straw wrapped in textile, or Company approved equivalent filter.
Details on proposed dewatering locations shall be provided to Company for approval in accordance with
this Attachment B-2.4 – Construction Specifications.
Contractor shall provide Company with three water samples from each test water discharge, the
samples to be taken during the first fifteen (15) minutes, midway through the discharge, and near the
end of the discharge.
Drying of the pipeline sections shall be completed in accordance with the Contract Documents and to
the satisfaction of Company.
Should a chemical drying agent be used, all fluids recovered with the associated pig runs shall be
collected and disposed of at an industrial waste disposal site.
Where the discharge location for test water is in a different river basin than the source of that water,
the test water shall not be discharged into a watercourse or onto any sloping ground or draw leading to
a watercourse.
24.18 Pipeline Drying




                                             Page 142 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                            OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Pipeline drying shall be conducted using foam pigs. Minimum criteria for foam pig drying are the
following:
           Pipeline drying shall be carried out by propelling foam pigs with compressed air, at a
            maximum velocity of eight (8) km per hour. Each run shall use one or more thirty two (32)
            kilogram per cubic metre density foam pig(s) with a one hundred and twenty eight (128)
            kilogram per cubic metre density crisscross foam pig or solid cup type pig behind it. A foam
            pig shall be retrieved that is clean and dry to the satisfaction of Company.
           A minimum of two (2) runs shall be made for each test section. Successive runs shall be
            made in the same direction until the pipeline is dry to the satisfaction of Company.
           Immediately after pipeline drying runs have been completed and approved, Contractor shall
            install welded watertight nightcaps (or Company approved alternate) on the ends of the test
            section.
The removal of foam pigs shall only be done in the presence of Company and during daylight hours
unless otherwise approved by Company.
24.19 Methanol Wash
If requested by Company, the Contractor shall run a methanol wash through the pipeline during daylight
hours in the presence of Company. The length of a section to be washed shall not exceed 30 km. During
Winter Construction, the washing of a section shall be completed within twenty four (24) hours of the
completion of dewatering of that section. Contractor shall be aware that methanol is classified as a
dangerous substance and that safe handling procedures shall be used.
The methanol wash is to be run between polyurethane pigs using compressed air and a line pack to
ensure a maximum rate of eight (8) kilometres per hour.
The initial fluid used may contain water to a maximum of fifteen percent (15%) by weight. Contractor
shall supply the methanol in the following minimum quantity:
All the methanol solution displaced from the Pipeline shall be recovered and retained until disposal of
the methanol can take place in a manner acceptable to Company. Under no circumstances shall a
methanol solution be discharged to the ground or allowed to reach the ground water or water course.
The volume of the recovered methanol solution and its specific gravity shall be measured by Contractor
in the presence of Company. The methanol solution recovered shall have a volume greater than fifty
percent (50%) of the volume of pure methanol introduced, and it shall contain a minimum of sixty
percent (60%) by weight of pure methanol. A number of clean samples of the methanol solution shall be
measured with a hydrometer and thermometer to determine its average specific gravity and
temperature.
The specific gravity of the recovered solution shall be equal to or less than the values in the following
table at the measured temperature:

                          Table 24.19.1:Specific Gravity of Recovered Methanol

                          Temperature (Celsius)       SG of 60% Methanol

If the volume and content of the recovered solution do not meet the above criteria, then the methanol

seal.
24.20 Hydrostatic Test of Above Ground Piping & Assemblies (Visual)
24.20.1 General
Fabricated assemblies not supplied by Company pre-tested, shall undergo a one (1) hour above ground
visual test prior to installation into the pipeline. Hydrostatic tests of fabricated assemblies shall comply
with the specifications for the testing of the pipeline, except for the changes described in the following
paragraphs.
24.20.2 Filling
Filling of fabricated assemblies may be conducted by hauling the water to the assembly or if an
approved water source is in close proximity to the assembly it could be used. Valves being tested with
fabricated assemblies shall be tested in the partially open position to ensure the body of the valve is
subjected to the test.
24.20.3 Test Procedures
The hydrostatic testing of a fabricated assembly that can be completely visually inspected during the
pressure test shall consist of a leak check, followed by a strength test and a complete visual inspection
for leaks as per the test pressures and durations indicated in Attachment A-2.9 Hydrotest Plan. The leak
check shall be performed when the pressure in the test section produces a stress of fifty percent (50%)
of specified minimum yield strength (SMYS) in that part of the fabricated assembly that, upon
pressurization, develops the greatest percentage of SMYS. The strength test shall be at a minimum of
one hundred and fifty percent (150%) of intended maximum operating pressure for a continuous one (1)
hour period, but shall not at any time produce a hoop stress of one hundred and ten percent (110%) or
more of SMYS at any location in the test section. The complete visual inspection shall be conducted after
the strength test, and at a pressure of at least one hundred and ten percent (110%) of the intended
maximum operating pressure, but no higher than the pressure equivalent to one hundred percent
(100%) of SMYS hoop stress.
Prior to starting the test, all fittings shall be checked for tightness. Bull plugs and blind flanges shall be
installed except where gauges, recorders, or pumps are to be connected. The pressure pump and
connections must be checked before the test commences to ensure that they are capable of


                                               Page 144 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                            OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


withstanding the pressure to which they will be subjected. A check valve shall be installed between the
test assembly and the piping from the pressure pump.
Two (2) pressure gauges shall be installed on each assembly prior to starting the testing operation. At a
location to be determined by Company, the pressure recorder and deadweight tester shall be connected
to the test assembly so that both instruments will measure the test pressure.
A temperature recorder shall be connected to the test assembly so that the recorder will measure the
temperature of the test medium. If the temperature probe cannot be installed in a thermowell, the
probe shall be attached to the underside of the pipe, insulated and wrapped.
24.20.4 Dewatering & Drainage
All piping and valve bodies shall be thoroughly drained and dried to Company satisfaction. Valve bodies
will require body bleeds to be drained and vent lines to be blown out with the use of compressed air.
Company will direct Contractor in the draining of valve bodies.
24.20.5 Test Acceptance
Company will accept that one (1) hour visual test based on the criteria identified in this Specification.
24.20.6 Test Records
Test documentation will be consistent with this Specification with the exception of yield plot and pigging
data requirements that do not apply to the one (1) hour Strength Test followed by a one hundred
percent (100%) visual test conducted on fabricated assemblies.
24.21 Hydrostatic Pre-Test of Water Crossing Sections
24.21.1 Pre-tested Water Crossing Sections
Water crossing sections to be pre-tested prior to installation are identified in Schedule A - Scope of
Work and shall be tested for a duration of one hour to a pressure provided by Company, in accordance
with this Specification, “Hydrostatic Test of Fabricated Assemblies”.
24.22 Winter Testing Requirements
Exposed pipe shall be adequately covered and sufficiently heated to prevent freezing. The hoarding and
heating shall be maintained until the section is dewatered and dried. Open ditches shall be kept free of
standing water.
Test water shall be heated and circulated to achieve a minimum discharge temperature of two degrees
(2°) Celsius. The maximum temperature at the inlet end shall not exceed fifty degree (50°) Celsius to
prevent damage to the coating. Contractor shall continue to circulate for a minimum of two (2) hours
once the minimum discharge temperature is reached. During filling operations Contractor shall maintain
a minimum water temperature of two degrees (2°) Celsius.
Where a possibility of freezing exists, all exposed portions of any test section shall be hoarded in. The
hoarded areas shall be heated if necessary to prevent any part of the section under test from freezing.
The hoarding and heating shall be maintained until the section is dewatered and dried.

Prior to discharging water during the water circulation process Contractor must have written approval
from Company. Water discharge shall be in accordance with permits acquired by Company and the
Authorities Having Jurisdiction.
25.0 Installation of Valves & Fittings
25.1 General
Company will either provide pre-tested, fabricated and painted assemblies or the components for
assembly fabrication in accordance with Schedule A – Scope of Work and Appendix A-3 – Company
Supplied Material. Contractor shall install complete mainline valve assemblies and check valve
assemblies at the required locations and as shown on the Drawings and in accordance with this
Specification.
During hauling, Contractor shall ensure that valve stem extensions, grease lines and vents are
maintained free of all moisture, dirt and other foreign materials. All valves, pipe and fittings shall be
thoroughly cleaned on the inside of any dirt, dust and other foreign material immediately prior to
installation.
All flanges shall be installed so that the bolt holes straddle the vertical centerline of the pipe and the
flange face is perpendicular to the longitudinal pipe centerline.
Flange face and gaskets shall be cleaned immediately prior to make up. Flange bolts shall be tightened
evenly, using torque wrenches, so that gasket seating pressure is uniform.
Company approved thread lubricants shall be used on all bolt threads. Misalignments shall not be
corrected by force or uneven bolt tightening and no installation procedure shall be used that will cause
difficult replacement of components. Misalignments shall be corrected in a manner approved by
Company at no additional compensation to Contractor.
Damaged or defective pipe, valves, fittings and other material shall be reported to Company by
Contractor at time of receipt at point of delivery. After custody transfer of material to Contractor, all
damage shall be deemed Contractor's responsibility to repair or replace at his own expense.
25.2 Fabrication of Assemblies
Contractor shall take all necessary precautionary measures to protect the integrity of valves and fittings
during welding operations and will be held liable for any damage caused. As a minimum, the following
mitigative measures shall be employed:
       Ball valves and gate valves shall be fully open during welding;
       Welding in close proximity to valve bodies shall be conducted in accordance with
        manufacturer's specifications; and
       Insulation or other non-flammable material shall be placed in the valve bore, both ends to
        protect seals and seats from weld splatter and debris, and
       Preheat and weld interpass temperatures shall be restricted to the weld area to ensure that
        valve seals and seats are not damaged.
25.3 Installation of Assemblies
Valve assemblies shall be installed and supported in accordance with this Specification and the drawing.



                                              Page 146 of 148
PIPELINE CONSTRUCTION SERVICES                                                              OCTOBER 4TH 2015
WAPITI EXPANSION PIPELINE PROJECT
AGREEMENT# 4500076993
ATTACHMENT B-2.4 – CONSTRUCTION SPECIFICATIONS


Refer to the drawings for spacing between pipes where more than one pipe is being installed in a
common trench. To achieve required spacing at assemblies, Contractor will need to excavate the trench
wider for a distance equal to the length of several pipe joints either side of the assembly. Field bends
may also be required either side of the assembly to ensure no stress is placed on the assembly.
Excavation for valve assemblies and assembly tie-ins shall be kept to a minimum. Where over-
excavation at valve assemblies occurs at S-bend risers, pipe supports and tie-ins, the soil under the riser,
assembly or pipe shall be compacted to a minimum eighty five percent (85%) standard proctor dry
density. If the original material is not suitable to achieve required compaction, select material shall be
imported. The piping and assembly shall be supported on a compacted base.
Friction pipe piles shall be driven to refusal with a hammer with a per blow energy of not less than
45,000 joules. The mass of the hammer shall be not less than twice that of the pile and not less than
1300 kg. Proper cushion to protect the top of the pipe pile shall be provided between the hammer and
pipe.
At mainline valve installations, the area within the fenced enclosures shall be graded level. All valves
shall be set in accordance with the Drawings.
All valve operators shall be installed by others. Contractor shall not adjust operators nor shall it install
any electricals associated with same. Valve operator mounting flanges on valves supplied without the
operator pre-mounted, shall be kept covered and water tight. Valve stem extensions must be
maintained free of all moisture, dirt and other foreign objects.
Piping runs containing valves or fittings or branch connections shall be properly supported and installed
in accordance with the Drawings.
All buried pipe, valves and fittings shall be externally coated as outlined under of this Specification.
Backfilling of assemblies shall be conducted carefully in accordance with this Attachment B-2.4 -
Construction Specifications, and Appendix B-1 - Drawings to ensure that pipe and coating are not
damaged. Company may require select material be imported if original material is too rough to place
around piping and fittings.
Damage caused to painted assemblies during transport and installation shall be painted in accordance
with the requirements of this Attachment B-2.4 - Construction Specifications.
26.0 Painting
Contractor shall supply all materials and labour and shall apply one top coat of paint on all above ground
piping as indicated on the Drawings, or as directed by Company, including pipe valves, vent pipes, vent
hoods, pipe supports and structural steel. All priming and painting shall be carried out in accordance
with the painting standards in Schedule A - Scope of Work.
All painting shall be done in a workmanlike manner satisfactory to Company. Prior to painting, surfaces
shall be thoroughly wire brush cleaned, washed with solvent and dried, with all rust, scale, dirt, oil or
grease removed to meet the requirements of the primer specified. All primers and paint shall be evenly
applied in accordance with the manufacturer's specifications. The finished surface shall be free of runs,
drips, or flows of any kind.

manufacturer. On winter construction, painting shall be deferred and completed at the time of final or
summer clean-up.
